Diagnosed as the **same stale-service-worker-cache class of bug already root-caused in PR #107** — not a new regression: `index.html` (network-first) had already picked up the new markup (`data-i18n="finance_chart_net"` etc., and the new `#fin-chart-svg`/`#fin-chart-total` ids), but the user's device was still running the **old cached** `js/classic-globals.js` (missing the new `finance_chart_*` translation keys, so `tr()` fell back to returning the raw key string) and the **old cached** `js/calendar.js` (whose old `renderFinanceChart()` still queried the now-removed `#finance-chart` id, found `null`, and silently no-op'd — leaving the hardcoded HTML placeholder "0 грн" untouched and the new SVG element empty). Confirmed this wasn't a real code bug by re-checking: the exact same deployed code, loaded fresh (this repo's own Playwright verification, no service worker involved), correctly shows translated labels and a populated chart — matches PR #107's already-documented lesson that a stale `CACHE_NAME` bug can only be caught by a **pre-existing installed** service worker, never by a fresh-load test, no matter how thorough. Told the user to fully close and reopen the app (not just a soft refresh) to let the already-deployed v14 service worker take over. **Separately** (a real, actionable ask): the user also shared a dashboard mockup wanting a big balance plus two colored mini-stat cards beneath it — added a green-gradient "Дохід цього місяця" card and a red-gradient "Витрата цього місяця" card to `#fin-balances` (`js/analytics-csv.js`'s `renderFinance()`), directly under the total balance and above the existing (unchanged) per-wallet chip row. New `finance_month_income`/`finance_month_expense` i18n keys (uk+en); `.fin-mini-stat-val` added to the `body.amounts-hidden` blur list alongside the other balance-bearing elements. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`/`functions-sweep`, all pass) plus a one-off Playwright pass confirming both new mini-stat cards render with correct monthly totals and colors. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v14→v15 per the standing rule (yet again — this is now the single most frequently-forgotten-until-caught step in this repo's UI-change workflow; worth triple-checking on every future `js/*.js`/`index.html` change before considering a PR done).
- **Small polish pass from real-device screenshots (some at magnified zoom)** (PR [#131](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/131), merged (squash) as `a5d044b`, deployed to Firebase Hosting 2026-07-11): user sent 5 photos, several taken with Android's screen-magnifier gesture zoomed into specific trouble spots rather than a persistent large-font accessibility setting (confirmed by comparing one full-screen, non-zoomed shot against the others — everything scales normally in the full view). Real, reproducible issues found: (1) **`.quick-action` buttons could visually overflow into each other** — fixed 68px column + `white-space:nowrap` on the label meant a longer word like "Інструменти" simply overflowed past its own column with no wrap, which is what read as "the 4 buttons aren't centered." Fixed by making the column `width:auto` (min 68px, max 84px) and letting the label wrap (`white-space:normal` + `overflow-wrap:anywhere` as a fallback for extreme cases) instead of overflowing. (2) **`#btn-refresh` (topbar sync icon) had zero visible feedback** — its click handler just called `fbLoadNow()` with no spinner, no toast; the internal `fbSetStatus()` call inside `fbLoadNow()` targets `#fb-status`/`#fb-text` elements that **don't actually exist anywhere in the current markup** (confirmed via grep — dead reference, already a silent no-op, not something this session broke). Wired a real spin animation (`.spinning` class + `@keyframes spin`, `prefers-reduced-motion`-aware) plus a `showToast(tr('sync_synced'),'check')` call after the awaited `fbLoadNow()` resolves. (3) Bumped `.hero-balance-val` (main Finance-tab balance figure) font-weight 800→900 per direct request. (4) Bumped `.tx-del` (edit/delete icons in the transaction list) from 15px→19px, trimming padding 15px→13px to keep the same ~44px touch target established in the earlier a11y pass — net button size unchanged, icon itself bigger. **Verified**: full local suite (all 5 scripts) plus a one-off Playwright pass confirming the spin class appears/disappears correctly around the awaited sync call, the toast text and timing, and that all 4 quick-action labels now render on one line without spilling into neighboring buttons. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v15→v16 per the (by now well-drilled) standing rule.
- **Fixed wallet names collapsing to ~1 letter in the transaction list** (PR [#133](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/133), merged (squash) as `461e729`, deployed to Firebase Hosting 2026-07-12): user sent zoomed-crop screenshots (Android magnifier gesture, not a persistent large-font setting — confirmed by comparing against a full non-zoomed screenshot earlier in the same conversation) and clarified via `AskUserQuestion` that a wallet literally named "Кредитна картка ПУМБ" was rendering as basically one letter + ellipsis, not just a zoom artifact. **Real root cause, found by measuring actual `getBoundingClientRect()` widths in a Playwright session** (not by reading the CSS, which looked reasonable on its own): `.tx-right` (amount + edit + delete buttons) was a single horizontal row with `flex-shrink:0`, so it always claimed its full natural width — on a 330px-wide transaction card that came to **215px (65% of the row)**, driven by the two 45px touch-target icon buttons (from the earlier a11y pass, then made visually bigger again in PR #131) plus the amount text plus gaps. That left only ~75-115px for the *entire* left side (category icon + category name + wallet badge + date/comment) — with a category name like "Продукти" already present, the wallet badge had essentially no room left and its `text-overflow:ellipsis` truncation collapsed it to one character. This is a different, deeper cause than the one already fixed in PR #112/#113 (which addressed vertical overlap and gave `.wallet-tag` an `overflow:hidden` safety net, but never addressed *how little horizontal space* the tag actually had to work with in the first place). **Fix**: restructured `.tx-right` into two stacked rows — amount on top, a new `.tx-actions` wrapper with the edit/delete buttons below it, both right-aligned — so `.tx-right`'s total width becomes the *max* of the two rows (~110px) instead of their *sum* (~215px), handing roughly 100px back to the left side. Also added `flex-shrink:0` to `.wallet-tag` itself so it wraps to its own line within `.tx-cat`'s `flex-wrap` when the category name doesn't leave room on the same line, rather than shrinking in place alongside it (a secondary contributor to the same failure mode). **Verified precisely, not just visually**: wrote a one-off Playwright script that creates a wallet with the user's exact reported name via the real Wallets-manager UI flow, adds a transaction using it, and measures `.wallet-tag`'s rendered width before/after the fix — went from **32px (icon only, no readable text)** to **138px (shows most of the name before eliding)** on the same 390px viewport. Full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`/`functions-sweep`, all pass — `e2e-crud.mjs` in particular directly exercises the restructured `.tx-right` DOM via its own edit/delete button locators, confirming the markup change didn't break that flow). `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v16→v17 per the standing rule. **Lesson**: when a CSS layout complaint doesn't make sense from reading the stylesheet alone (this one didn't — `.wallet-tag`'s rules looked fine in isolation), measure real rendered widths of the *whole row*, not just the one element being complained about — the actual bottleneck here was a sibling (`.tx-right`) two components away, not anything wrong with `.wallet-tag`'s own CSS.
- **Fixed calendar shift-badge overflow and dropped `umbrella` from the random category-icon pool** (PR [#135](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/135), merged (squash) as `aeabdeb`, deployed to Firebase Hosting 2026-07-12): two unrelated small complaints from real-device screenshots. (1) The `.badge` pill shown in each calendar day cell (a shift type's `short` label, e.g. "ДЕНЬ+") had no overflow handling of its own — on a narrow phone a longer short-label could be wider than its day cell, and since the parent `.day-cell` has `overflow:hidden`, the badge just got silently clipped mid-character with no ellipsis or other visual cue that truncation happened. Added `max-width:100%;overflow:hidden;text-overflow:ellipsis;white-space:nowrap` to `.badge` itself (same established pattern as `.wallet-tag-name`), and shrank it slightly further at the existing `@media(max-width:600px)` breakpoint (font-size 11px→9.5px, padding 1px 4px→1px 3px) to reduce how often truncation is even needed. (2) A transaction's category icon rendered as a literal umbrella, which the user found nonsensical ("чому на іконці переказ намальован зонтик"). Root cause: `categoryIcon()` (`js/core.js`) falls back to a deterministic string-hash pick from `CAT_ICON_FALLBACK_POOL` for any category name not in the explicit `CAT_ICON` map — confirmed by running the exact same hash function in isolation against the user's actual category name ("% поповнення ПУМБ"): it lands precisely on `'umbrella'` in the old 10-item pool. `'umbrella'` itself stays in `ICON_PATHS` (still used deliberately for vacation/day-off, `setIcon('ic-vacation','umbrella')`) — only removed from this *generic* fallback pool, since having no thematic connection to an arbitrary finance category is what made it look like a bug rather than a deliberate icon choice. Re-ran the same hash check post-fix: that exact category now resolves to `'globe'` in the trimmed 9-item pool. **Verified**: full local suite (all 5 scripts, pass) plus a Playwright pass checking in a shift and measuring the badge vs. its day-cell width, plus a standalone Node check re-implementing the hash function to confirm the specific reported category name's icon changed from `umbrella` to `globe`. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v17→v18 per the standing rule.
- **Distributed the 4 quick-action buttons evenly across the row width** (PR [#137](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/137), merged (squash) as `2216437`, deployed to Firebase Hosting 2026-07-12): user annotated a screenshot (drawn white circle + red arrow, their own annotation, not app content) pointing at a large empty gap to the right of the last quick-action button ("Цілі"), calling it untidy. `.quick-actions` was `display:flex` with no `justify-content`, so the 4 buttons clustered left-aligned with unused space on the right on typical phone widths (confirmed via Playwright at 412px: buttons only spanned the first ~330px of a ~392px row). Added `justify-content:space-between` so they spread across the full row when there's spare room; `overflow-x:auto` (unchanged) still handles a future 5th/6th action overflowing. **Verified**: full local suite (all 5 scripts, pass) plus a Playwright measurement at 412px width confirming the 4 buttons now span from ~12px to ~400px instead of clustering in the first ~330px. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v18→v19 per the standing rule.
- **Fixed the "ПриватБанк (готівка)" rates source always silently failing** (PR [#142](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/142), merged (squash) as `1c66007`, deployed to Firebase Hosting 2026-07-12): user saw real console errors (`api.privatbank.ua ... net::ERR_FAILED`, blocked by CORS — `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` header absent) and asked to actually fix it rather than leave it as expected noise. `fetchPrivatCashRates()` (`js/settings-managers.js`) called `api.privatbank.ua` directly with no fallback — PrivatBank's server has never sent CORS headers for this origin, so the direct call was **always** going to fail for every user, silently downgrading the "ПриватБанк (готівка)" rates-source option to just NBU rates underneath (already caught by an existing `try/catch` so nothing crashed, but the feature never actually worked as advertised). **Fix**: added a `PRIVAT_RATES_FALLBACK_URL` using the exact same `api.allorigins.win/raw?url=...` CORS-relay pattern `fetchLiveRates()` already uses for the NBU endpoint's own fallback — try the direct PrivatBank call first, and on failure relay through allorigins instead of giving up. No `firebase.json`/CSP change needed: `connect-src` already allow-lists both `api.privatbank.ua` and `api.allorigins.win` (added for the NBU fallback back in the CSP-hardening pass). **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`, pass — `e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`/`functions-sweep` unaffected, this doesn't touch their surfaces) plus a dedicated one-off Playwright check (not committed) that routes `api.privatbank.ua` to abort like a real CORS failure and confirms the exact same fetch-fallback code path then successfully calls `api.allorigins.win` and parses the relayed PrivatBank JSON — this sandbox has no route to either real host, so this was the only way to verify the fallback logic itself without waiting for a live deploy. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v20→v21 per the standing rule. Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a clean `origin/main` worktree — succeeded on the first attempt, no IAM gap.
- **PR #142's `api.allorigins.win` fallback turned out unreliable too — replaced with a real server-side Cloud Function proxy** (2026-07-12, same session as the above, direct follow-up after the user reported the fix still failing with fresh screenshots): the allorigins relay itself started returning `500 (Internal Server Error)` for the PrivatBank URL specifically, and — because allorigins' *error* response apparently omits CORS headers even though its successful responses (used for the already-working NBU fallback) include them — the browser reported this as a second CORS failure on top of the original one, so the user saw two stacked CORS-looking errors instead of real data. Root cause is almost certainly PrivatBank rate-limiting or blocking requests originating from allorigins' server IP (a public, heavily-shared relay is an easy target for that kind of blocking) — not something fixable by retrying or tweaking the request. **Real fix, not another third-party relay**: added a Cloud Function proxy (`exports.privatRates` in `functions/index.js`, `onRequest` v2 HTTPS) that fetches PrivatBank server-side (Node 20's built-in global `fetch`, no new dependency) and returns the JSON verbatim (502 + `{error}` on any upstream failure, logged via `logger.warn`). Exposed to the client at the **same-origin** path `/api/privat-rates` via a new Firebase Hosting rewrite (`firebase.json`'s `hosting.rewrites`) rather than calling the `*.cloudfunctions.net` URL directly — this means the browser never needs a CORS header on the response at all (same-origin requests aren't subject to CORS), and no `firebase.json` CSP `connect-src` change was needed either (`'self'` already covers it). `js/settings-managers.js`'s `PRIVAT_RATES_FALLBACK_URL` now points at `/api/privat-rates` instead of the allorigins URL; the direct-PrivatBank-call-first, proxy-on-failure control flow in `fetchPrivatCashRates()` is otherwise unchanged. **A real caching bug this would have introduced if missed**: `sw.js`'s generic same-origin fetch handler is cache-first for everything that isn't HTML — without an exception, the very first successful `/api/privat-rates` response would have been cached by the service worker and served stale *forever* after that, silently freezing PrivatBank's cash rates at whatever they were on first load. Added an explicit bail-out (`if (url.pathname.startsWith('/api/')) return;`, checked before the HTML/cache-first branches) so any current or future Hosting-rewrite-backed API endpoint always hits the network, matching the existing pattern of narrow, deliberate exceptions to the generic same-origin caching rule (see the `FIREBASE_SDK_ASSETS` allowlist comment right above it in the same file). `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v21→v22. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`/`functions-sweep`, all pass — none of these previously exercised `functions/index.js`'s HTTPS surface, only its scheduled-function surface via `lib/sweep.js`) plus two dedicated one-off Node checks (not committed): (1) `npm install` in `functions/` (this sandbox does have registry access despite lacking access to `api.privatbank.ua`/`api.allorigins.win` themselves — confirmed by the install actually succeeding) then invoking the real exported `privatRates` handler directly with a stubbed global `fetch` and a minimal `EventEmitter`-based fake Express `req`/`res` (the real `onRequest`/`cors` middleware needs `res.on`/`res.setHeader`/`res.getHeader` to exist, not just `res.status`/`res.json` — a bare mock throws inside the `cors` package, not inside our own code) — confirmed both the success path (200, upstream JSON passed through verbatim) and the upstream-failure path (502, `{error:'PrivatBank fetch failed'}`, logged via `logger.warn`, no unhandled rejection) end-to-end against the real `firebase-functions`/`cors` library code, not just by reading the handler. **Lesson**: a third-party CORS-relay fallback is not a permanently reliable fix even when it's independently verified working for a *different* upstream (the NBU fallback via the same allorigins service has had no reported issues) — a relay's reliability is really a property of the specific *target* host's tolerance for that relay's traffic, not the relay generically, and a bank API is a plausible candidate for IP-based bot/proxy blocking that a generic news/government API (NBU) wouldn't trigger. When a fetch genuinely needs to reach a host that actively resists being called from arbitrary origins/proxies, routing it through infrastructure you actually control (a Cloud Function you own, called same-origin via a Hosting rewrite) is the robust answer, not a different public relay that might have the exact same problem.
- **Incident, same session: briefly deployed all of `functions/node_modules` (5535 files) to public Firebase Hosting — caught and fixed within minutes** (2026-07-12): while deploying the `privatRates` Cloud Function above, ran `cd functions && npm install` inside the *same* git worktree already checked out for `firebase deploy --only functions,hosting --project maxtr-c238f`, then ran that combined deploy. `firebase.json`'s hosting config is `"public": "."` (the whole repo root — this app has no build step, see "Commands" above) with a **custom** `"ignore"` array; supplying a custom `ignore` list in `firebase.json` **replaces** firebase-tools' own default ignore list (`["firebase.json", "**/.*", "**/node_modules/**"]`) rather than extending it, and this repo's custom list had never included `**/node_modules/**` — apparently untested until now because every previous `hosting` deploy happened either before `functions/node_modules` existed in that worktree or from a separate worktree/command that never ran `npm install` first (the documented Cloud Function deploy recipe under "Commands" is `npm install && firebase deploy --only functions,firestore:rules` — deliberately *not* `hosting` in that same invocation, which in hindsight is exactly the footgun this incident fell into by combining them). Result: that one deploy's Hosting release briefly served all 5535 files under `functions/node_modules/**` publicly at `maxtr-c238f.web.app/functions/node_modules/...` — publicly-published npm package source, not secrets or credentials (no `.env`/service-account keys live under `functions/`, and `node_modules` itself is `.gitignore`'d so nothing in the repo history was exposed), but still unintended bulk exposure of exact dependency versions/file layout and a large amount of garbage content briefly live on the production site. **Caught immediately** by noticing the deploy log itself said "found 5539 files in ." where every prior hosting deploy this session had said "found ~55-60 files" — a scale mismatch that shouldn't need explaining away. Confirmed the cause by counting `functions/node_modules` in the same worktree (5535 files, matching almost exactly). **Fixed**: added `"**/node_modules/**"` and, for defense in depth, `"functions/**"` outright (the Cloud Functions source doesn't need to be statically hosted at all — it's deployed separately via the `functions` deploy target) to `firebase.json`'s hosting `ignore` array. Redeployed `hosting` alone immediately (before doing the proper commit/PR/log flow for the fix, given this was actively-exposed content) — confirmed the very next deploy's log read "found 55 files in .", back to the expected count, and Hosting releases are atomic/versioned so this new release fully replaced the exposed one with no window where both were simultaneously live. **Lesson for future deploys**: (1) never run `npm install` inside a worktree that will also be used for a **hosting** deploy of a repo whose hosting `public` root is `.` — do `functions`-only deploys from a worktree you then discard, or run `npm install` in a scratch copy outside the deploy worktree entirely; (2) a custom `ignore` array in `firebase.json` needs `**/node_modules/**` (and any other directory that could ever contain installed dependencies) explicitly — it does not inherit firebase-tools' sane defaults once overridden, a non-obvious footgun worth checking for in any Firebase Hosting config that already has a custom `ignore` list; (3) the file-count line in `firebase deploy`'s own log output (`"found N files in ."`) is a cheap, always-available sanity check — a sudden large jump versus prior deploys of the same repo is worth pausing on before letting the deploy proceed, not just after the fact.
- **Confirmed the `privatRates` proxy above actually works in production, then quieted the now-unnecessary console noise around it** (2026-07-12, same session): user sent a follow-up screenshot still showing the direct `api.privatbank.ua` CORS failure in the console and asked "а зараз? що?" (so, what now?). Verified server-side (this sandbox can't load `maxtr-c238f.web.app` directly, but *can* reach `*.googleapis.com`) via the Cloud Logging API for the `privatrates` Cloud Run revision: a real request at `2026-07-12T08:38:42Z` (`11:38:42` Kyiv time) returned `200`, 317 bytes — 19 seconds before the exact "Оновлено — ПриватБанк, 12.07.2026, 11:39:01" timestamp visible in the user's own screenshot, i.e. the same page load. The proxy was already working; the console noise was just the *expected* first-attempt CORS failure (browser-level, unsuppressible) plus our own `console.warn` logging it before falling back. Since PrivatBank's CORS block is permanent, not intermittent (confirmed repeatedly across sessions), there was no reason to keep attempting the direct call at all — every load was guaranteed to both waste a request and log a scary-looking (but harmless) CORS error for no benefit. **Fix**: `fetchPrivatCashRates()` (`js/settings-managers.js`) now calls `/api/privat-rates` (the Cloud Function proxy) directly as the only method, with no direct-`api.privatbank.ua`-then-fallback dance — removed the now-dead `PRIVAT_RATES_URL` constant and the `try/catch`-plus-`console.warn` wrapper entirely, renamed the proxy constant to `PRIVAT_RATES_PROXY_URL` for clarity now that it's not a "fallback". `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v22→v23. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`, all pass). **Lesson**: distinguishing a *permanent* failure mode (this host will never send CORS headers, confirmed across two separate investigations now) from a *transient* one (the allorigins relay's intermittent 500s, or NBU's own occasional hiccups) matters for more than just picking a fix — a permanent failure means the "try direct first" pattern that's correct for NBU's fallback is actively wrong here, since it guarantees a wasted request and log noise on every single load with zero chance of ever succeeding.
- **Category icons are now themed by keyword + manually pickable, instead of pure hash-random** (2026-07-12): user's screenshot showed "Мобільний зв'язок" (mobile/phone bill) rendered with a random unrelated glyph, and asked for (1) icons that actually match the category and (2) — "ще краще" (even better) — a manual picker from a big collection, like another app they'd seen. Both done. **Data model note that shaped the whole design**: categories in this app are (and always have been) plain strings in `AppState.categories.income`/`.expense` — no id, no object, no per-category record at all; `categoryColor()`/`categoryIcon()` (`js/core.js`) have always been pure functions of the category *name* (hash-based), which is exactly why the icon looked random for any name outside the small `CAT_ICON` exact-match table. Adding manual per-category customization therefore meant adding a *new* parallel lookup keyed by name, `AppState.categoryIcons` (a plain `{name: iconName}` object) — mirroring how `AppState.subcategories`/`AppState.budgets` already key off category name (via `subKey`/direct), not inventing a new pattern. **Three-tier fallback in `categoryIcon(name)`, in order**: (1) `AppState.categoryIcons[name]` — the user's manual pick, if any; (2) `CAT_ICON[name]` — exact-match table, unchanged, covers `DEFAULT_CATEGORIES`; (3) **new** `CAT_ICON_KEYWORDS` — a substring/regex match against ~13 common Ukrainian finance words (телефон/мобільн→phone, оренда/квартир→house, кредит→bank, продукт/харч→cart, транспорт/таксі/бензин→car, кава→coffee, кафе/ресторан/фастфуд→burger, etc.) that catches most *custom*, user-typed category names (which by definition can never be in the exact-match table) without requiring any manual action — this is what actually fixes "Мобільний зв'язок" specifically, since that exact string was never going to be in `CAT_ICON`; (4) the pre-existing hash-based `CAT_ICON_FALLBACK_POOL`, unchanged, as the true last resort for names matching none of the above. **Manual picker**: clicking a category's icon badge in the Categories manager (`js/settings-managers.js`'s `renderCategoriesList` — the badge is now a real `<button data-action="open-category-icon-picker">`, not an inert `<span>`) opens a new `#category-icon-modal` with a grid of 39 curated icons (`window.ICON_NAMES`, exposed from `js/classic-globals.js` right next to `window.Icon`/`ICON_PATHS` — deliberately a *curated subset* of the full icon set, excluding pure UI/action glyphs like trash/chevron/gear/search/pencil/grip/lock that make sense as button icons but not as a thing representing a spending category), following the exact same `.modal-overlay`/data-action/capture-phase-click pattern every other manager modal in this codebase already uses — picking one writes `AppState.categoryIcons[name]` and re-renders every surface that shows category icons (categories manager, budgets manager, Finance tab, analytics donut chart) since they all already call the same shared `categoryIcon(name)` function, so nothing else needed touching. `renameCategory`/`deleteCategory` got the same rekey-on-rename/delete-on-remove treatment `AppState.subcategories`/`AppState.budgets` already had for exactly this reason (both already existed in those functions — just extended the pattern, not invented a new one). **Persistence**: wired through all 4 of the usual places for a `finance`-doc-scoped `AppState` field (`js/state.js` default, `seedConfigFromDocs()`'s Firestore load and `fbSaveNow()`'s Firestore save in `js/color-picker.js`, `saveConfigLocal()`'s localStorage save also in `js/color-picker.js`, and the localStorage-cache-before-cloud-load path in `js/app-init.js`) — same 4-places checklist this file's own "Finance-tab widgets" section already documents for `AppState.widgets`. No `firestore.rules` change needed — the `finance` doc's validation is a shallow `keys().size() < 60` check with generous headroom (~20 keys before this), not a field allowlist. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`, all pass) plus a dedicated one-off Playwright script (not committed) — opens the picker, confirms a 39-icon grid renders, picks `umbrella`, confirms the row's badge updates immediately, confirms it persisted into the `mx_cfg_<uid>` localStorage blob's `categoryIcons` key, confirms the Budgets manager's category row picks up the same custom icon (proving the shared-function design actually works end-to-end, not just in the one screen it was set from), and confirms it survives a modal close/reopen — zero console/page errors beyond the sandbox's expected blocked live-rates fetch. The rename-carries-the-icon-over rekey logic itself was verified by code-reading only (identical 3-line pattern to the already-proven `subcategories`/`budgets` rekey immediately above it in `renameCategory`), not scripted through the UI, since driving the app's custom `uiPrompt()` dialog through Playwright for a rename round-trip wasn't worth the added script complexity for a change this mechanically identical to existing, working code. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v23→v24.
- **Collapsed the Finance tab's transaction history to 3 most-recent + a "View all" toggle** (2026-07-12): user asked for exactly this ("щоб історія операцій показувала три останні а інша типу подивитись усі") — the `#tx-list-container` list (`renderFinance()` in `js/analytics-csv.js`) previously always rendered every transaction matching the current type/category filter, inside a `.tx-list` with `max-height:500px;overflow-y:auto`, so a long history just meant a lot of internal scrolling. Added a module-level `txListExpanded` flag (deliberately *not* an `AppState` field — nothing outside this file needs to read or persist it, so a plain transient `let` is enough, same category as e.g. `AppState.expandedCatIdx` being per-file transient state but without even needing cross-file access) plus a `TX_LIST_COLLAPSED_COUNT=3` constant. `AppState.transactions` is already newest-first (every add path uses `.unshift()`, confirmed by checking `js/finance.js`/`js/color-picker.js` — not date-sorted, insertion-order, but that's already what the pre-existing unslicing list displayed, so slicing the first 3 of the already-correctly-ordered `filtered` array needed no new sort step). When `filtered.length>TX_LIST_COLLAPSED_COUNT`, a `.tx-view-all-btn` (`.btn.btn-ghost`, new `justify-content:center;width:100%` CSS rule) renders below the list showing `"Переглянути всі (N)"` or `"Згорнути"` depending on state, dispatched through this file's existing `CLICK_ACTIONS` table (`toggle-tx-list-expanded` → `toggleTxListExpanded()`, which flips the flag and calls `renderFinance()` again) — same pattern phase 11 of the window.*/onclick-removal audit item already established for this file, no new dispatch mechanism needed. Deliberately did **not** wire a reset-on-filter-change (switching the Всі/Дохід/Витрата/Переказ chips or category filter leaves `txListExpanded` as-is rather than forcing back to collapsed) — the flag is module-private to `analytics-csv.js`, and resetting it from `setTxFilter()` (a different file, `js/finance.js`) would mean exporting a reset function across a new cross-file edge for a debatable UX nicety; if a filter's own result now has ≤3 items the `showAll` check's `filtered.length<=TX_LIST_COLLAPSED_COUNT` clause already displays everything regardless of the flag, so the only visible consequence of not resetting is that an already-expanded view stays expanded after switching filters, which reads as reasonable rather than buggy. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`, all pass — `e2e-crud.mjs` only ever has 1 transaction on screen at a time, so it never exercises the collapse threshold, but confirms no regression) plus a dedicated one-off Playwright script (not committed): adds 5 transactions via the real FAB flow, confirms exactly 3 render by default, confirms the button reads "Переглянути всі (5)", clicking it shows all 5 and flips the button to "Згорнути", clicking again collapses back to 3. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v24→v25.
- **Fixed the Finance-chart's big balance figure not blurring under "hide amounts"** (2026-07-12): user screenshot showed the topbar hide-amounts toggle correctly blurring the transaction-list amounts and the chart's Середнє/Найкращий/Найгірший mini-stat chips, but leaving the chart's own large `.fin-chart-total` figure (e.g. "7 962 грн", `#fin-chart-total` in `js/calendar.js`'s `renderFinanceChart()`, added by the PR #127 chart redesign) sharp and readable. Root cause: `body.amounts-hidden` in `index.html`'s CSS blurs a fixed list of selectors (`.hero-balance-val`, `.wallet-chip-val`, `.chip-stat-val`, `.fin-mini-stat-val`, etc.) that's never been updated since — `.fin-chart-total` uses its own distinct class, never added to that list, so it was never covered. Same category of miss as PR #129's `.fin-mini-stat-val` gap, just one release later and one element newer. Added `.fin-chart-total` to the blur selector list, and also `.fin-chart-tooltip` (the tap-a-point tooltip on the same chart, e.g. "Лип: 43 445,91 грн" — shows a real amount too, same gap, just not yet reported since it only appears on tap) while already in there. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`, all pass) plus a dedicated one-off Playwright script (not committed) asserting `getComputedStyle(#fin-chart-total).filter` is `none` before toggling hide-amounts and contains `blur(...)` after, plus a no-regression check that the already-working `.hero-balance-val` blur is unaffected. **No `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bump** — this is a CSS-only change inside `index.html`'s own `<style>` block, and `index.html` is served network-first (not cache-first) per `sw.js`'s own fetch handler, so unlike a `js/*.js` behavior change, there's no stale-cached-JS-vs-fresh-HTML mismatch risk here for the standing cache-bump rule to guard against; every online load already gets the fix immediately regardless of the installed service worker's cache generation. **Lesson, worth adding to the standing checklist alongside the existing `sw.js` cache-bump one**: any new amount-bearing element added to the Finance tab (a new chart, a new stat chip, a new mini-widget) needs to be explicitly added to `body.amounts-hidden`'s selector list in `index.html` — it is not something a shared CSS class or component inherits automatically, and this is now the second time a real feature shipped with this exact gap (first: `.fin-mini-stat-val` in PR #129; second: `.fin-chart-total`/`.fin-chart-tooltip` here) with no automated test catching either, since none of the 4 scripted tests assert on `body.amounts-hidden` at all. Worth considering a small permanent test asserting every element matching a "shows a real money amount" heuristic is covered, next time this class of bug recurs a third time.
- **Added a structured debt due-date field + reminders (local + push), closing the previously-documented gap** (2026-07-12): user asked directly to build the "debt due soon" reminder this file's own Known-gaps list had flagged as blocked on a real due-date field. Each debt in `AppState.debts` (`js/debt.js`) previously had only `entries[]` with a *freeform text* `date` per payment (a settlement-history label, e.g. "10.02.2026" typed by hand) — no field representing "when does the whole debt need to be paid off." Added `dueDate` (a real ISO `YYYY-MM-DD`, via a genuine `<input type=date>` enhanced with the existing `enhanceDateInput()` picker, not another free-text field) as a new field directly on the debt object itself, alongside `name`/`note`/`currency`/`startAmount` in the "Дані розрахунку" panel — set/read in `updateDebtInfo()`/`renderDebt()`, defaulted in `addNewDebt()`. **New UI**: a 4th chip (`#debt-due-chip`, hidden when no `dueDate` is set) next to the existing Початкова сума/Сплачено/Платежів chips, showing the formatted date plus "через N дн." / "сьогодні" / "прострочено на N дн." (computed in a new `renderDebtDueChip()`), with the icon turning red (`var(--red)`) inside 3 days of due and staying purple otherwise — so the due date is visible at a glance, not just something that silently triggers a notification later. **Local notifications**: added `checkDebtAlerts()` to `js/notifications.js`, mirroring `checkRecurringAlerts()`'s exact convention (fires once, exactly one calendar day before `dueDate`, deduped via a `xamssDebtAlert_<id>_<date>` localStorage key) — new `AppState.notifSettings.debtAlerts` toggle (defaulted in `js/state.js`, a new settings row "Наближається термін боргу" wired the same `data-action="toggle-debt-alerts"` way every other notification toggle already is), wired into `runNotificationChecks()`. **Push notifications (the actually-hard part)**: extended `functions/lib/sweep.js`'s `sweepProfile()`/`sweepToken()` with a real 4th server-side check — debts previously weren't visible to the Cloud Function sweep *at all*, since they live in a **separate** Firestore doc (`debt`/`debt@<profileId>`, not `finance`) that the sweep never read. Added a `debtDocName(profileId)` helper (same `@<profileId>` suffixing convention as `financeDocName`) and a second parallel doc fetch in `sweepToken()` (both the default profile's finance+debt docs now fetch concurrently up front, and every other profile's finance+debt docs fetch concurrently as a second batch — same "reads in flight together, only the per-profile loop itself stays sequential" pattern the PR #117 scaling pass already established, extended rather than reinvented), a `sentDebt` dedup field on the token doc's per-profile state (parallel to `sentBudget`/`sentRecurring`), and the check itself in `sweepProfile()` (exact `dueDate === tomorrow` match, same one-day-ahead convention as recurring — deliberately not a configurable lead time, to match the existing precedent rather than add a new UX pattern for one feature). No `firestore.rules` change needed — both `finance` and `debt` docs already share the same shallow `keys().size() < 60` validation (not a field allowlist), and `dueDate` lives *inside* the `debts` array, not as a new top-level doc key. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`/`functions-sweep`, all pass — `functions-sweep.mjs` gained 6 new cases: fires exactly one day ahead, dedup, no-fire when not tomorrow or `debtAlerts` off, a missing `debt` doc treated as zero debts rather than throwing, and a full `sweepToken`-level integration test proving the new parallel debt-doc fetch is wired correctly end-to-end — plus all 8 pre-existing direct `sweepProfile()` calls needed a `debtSnap` argument added to their call sites once the signature grew a 9th parameter, otherwise they'd hit `db.doc()` on a deliberately-`null` `db` and throw) plus a dedicated one-off Playwright script (not committed) covering the client side: chip hidden with no debts/no dueDate, chip shows "через 5 дн." after setting one via the real date-picker input, the value persists into the `mx_debt_<uid>` localStorage cache, and the new Settings toggle exists. **Test-script gotcha worth flagging**: the first draft of the manual script set a due date without first creating a debt via the real "+ Додати розрахунок" flow — a brand-new account starts with **zero** debts (unlike wallets/categories, which seed defaults; already documented once before under the PR #102 entry above), so `getCurrentDebt()` returned `undefined` and `updateDebtInfo()`'s own `if(!cd) return;` guard silently no-opped the whole interaction with no error — fixed by driving the app's real `uiPrompt()` dialog (`#ui-dialog`/`#ui-dlg-input`/`#ui-dlg-ok`) to add a debt first, same recipe already documented elsewhere in this file for `uiConfirm()`-gated flows. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v25→v26.
- **Added a debt payoff progress bar ("savings goal"-style), closing another previously-documented gap** (2026-07-12): the phrase "'savings goal' style debt reminder" in this file's own gaps list was vague enough (from a past session's discussion, not this one) to be worth checking before building — used `AskUserQuestion` rather than guessing, offering 4 interpretations (a simple payoff progress bar like the existing Goals widget; a real savings-goal tied to a specific wallet earmarked for paying off the debt; a "how much to set aside monthly" calculator derived from dueDate+balance; or "something else"). User picked the first, simplest option. Implementation deliberately mirrors `renderGoals()` (`js/goals-profile.js`) — same `.salary-bar-wrap`/`.salary-bar-fill` CSS classes reused rather than styled fresh, same "green once done, otherwise a gradient" color rule — just computing "% of `startAmount` already paid off" (`paid/startAmount`, where `paid` is a value `renderDebt()` already computed for the existing "Сплачено" chip) instead of "% of a savings target saved." New `#debt-progress-wrap` sits between the balance hero-metric and the existing chip-stat row, hidden via a new `renderDebtProgress(cd, paid)` (`js/debt.js`) whenever `startAmount` isn't set (a 0/0 bar would be meaningless) — same "hide, don't show a broken 0%" pattern the due-date chip above already established for its own not-set case. Purely a display feature, no new data field, no `firestore.rules`/Cloud Function/notification changes needed — `startAmount` and the derived `paid` value already existed. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`/`functions-sweep`, all pass — untouched by this change) plus a dedicated one-off Playwright script (not committed): bar hidden at `startAmount=0`, shows 0% once a start amount is set with no payments yet, shows 40% (purple) after a 400/1000 payment via the real payment-entry flow, then 100% (green) once a second payment fully pays it off. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v26→v27.
- **Fixed disabling push notifications throwing a 404 service-worker error** (PR [#139](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/139), merged (squash) as `08d370b`, deployed to Firebase Hosting 2026-07-12): user's browser console showed `deleteToken failed FirebaseError: Messaging: We are unable to register the default service worker... firebase-messaging-sw.js ... A bad HTTP response code (404)` when toggling push notifications off. That file was deliberately merged into `sw.js` itself in an earlier pass (see "Layout" above) and no longer exists as a separate file — but this was the first time anything actually tried to fetch it directly. **Root cause, confirmed by reading the Firebase JS SDK's own source directly off GitHub** (not guessed): unlike `getToken()`, `deleteToken()` takes **no options argument at all** — it only checks whether `messaging.swRegistration` is already set (a plain property, set as a side effect by `getToken()` when passed an explicit `serviceWorkerRegistration`), and if it's falsy, falls back to calling `registerDefaultSw()`, which tries to register `/firebase-messaging-sw.js` at the root scope. This falls back precisely when a user re-opens the app in a fresh session (so `getToken()` was never called yet this session) and toggles off push that was already enabled from a previous session — a very common real path, not an edge case. **Fix**: in `disablePushNotifications()` (`js/notifications.js`), set `messaging.swRegistration = await navigator.serviceWorker.register('sw.js')` directly before calling `deleteToken()` if it isn't already set — the same property `getToken()` sets internally, just done explicitly since `deleteToken()` gives no way to pass it as an argument. **Verified precisely, not just by inspection**: wrote a dedicated Playwright script with a `STUB_MESSAGING` that faithfully reproduces the real SDK's actual internal check (throws a `messaging/failed-service-worker-registration` error unless `swRegistration` is pre-set) rather than the other test scripts' trivial no-op stub — confirmed the *exact* reported error reproduces with the old code (temporarily reverted the fix to double-check) and disappears with the fix restored. Full local suite (all 5 scripts) also passes. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v19→v20 per the standing rule. **Lesson**: when a bug report includes a specific SDK internal error message, reading that SDK's actual source (via `raw.githubusercontent.com`, since `unpkg.com` is blocked by this sandbox's egress proxy) to find the *exact* internal condition being hit is more reliable than guessing at the public API surface — the first fix attempt here (passing a `serviceWorkerRegistration` option to `deleteToken()`, mirroring `getToken()`'s API) would have silently done nothing, since `deleteToken()` doesn't accept a second argument at all.
- **Started acting on the full design-review artifact (see the design-review session, 2026-07-13): shipped the first 3 roadmap items, all pure `index.html` CSS-token work, no `js/*.js` behavior change.** After a deep design-review request produced a published artifact scoring the app 7.5/10 with a prioritized roadmap, the user asked to start with the top 3 items. (1) **Fixed the light-theme surface-hierarchy bug**: `[data-theme="light"]` had `--bg:#f2f2f7` and `--bg2:#f2f2f7` — literally identical, collapsing a layer the dark theme relies on for "card on card" depth (dark has 4 distinct steps: `#1c1c1f`→`#242327`→`#2c2b30`→`#38373d`). Changed light to `--bg:#f4f3f1`, `--bg2:#ececea`, `--bg3:#e2e0dd` (kept `--bg1:#ffffff` — the card surface — unchanged), giving light theme 4 real distinct steps for the first time, mirroring dark's relationship (card brightest, page and nested-chip backgrounds recede from it, each at a different step). (2) **Added a spacing scale (`--sp-1..8`, 4px base), a type scale (`--text-2xs..2xl` + `--weight-body/strong/display/mega`), and elevation/shadow tokens (`--shadow-color`, `--shadow-modal`, `--shadow-raised`)** to `:root`, with per-theme overrides only where the actual color/tint needs to differ (light theme gets a warm-tinted `--shadow-color:20,15,10` instead of pure black, and a lighter-opacity `--shadow-modal`/`--shadow-raised` so shadows tuned for the dark theme don't look muddy on white cards). Deliberately additive only — existing hardcoded px/rgba values elsewhere in the file were left alone (documented in the artifact's own roadmap as "apply going forward, don't mass-refactor now" given no visual-regression test coverage per pixel). (3) **Added a tinted box-shadow to `.hero-metric` and `.hero-balance`** (`var(--shadow-raised)`, a purple-tinted shadow — `.fin-fab` already had one) so the app's two most prominent "headline number" cards get a subtle elevation lift instead of relying on a 1px border alone; also replaced the hardcoded `box-shadow:0 24px 70px rgba(0,0,0,.55)` on `.modal-card`/`.dlg-card` with `var(--shadow-modal)` so modals now pick up the same per-theme tuning. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`, all pass) plus a dedicated one-off Playwright script (not committed) that switches into both themes via `window.setTheme()`, reads the computed `--bg`/`--bg2` custom-property values directly (asserting they're no longer equal) and `.hero-balance`'s computed `box-shadow` (asserting it's non-`none`), and screenshots the Finance tab in both themes — confirmed visually: light theme's wallet/mini-stat chips now visibly separate from the white balance card instead of nearly matching the page background. **No `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bump** — same reasoning as the already-documented `.fin-chart-total` blur-fix entry above: this is a CSS-only change inside `index.html`'s own `<style>` block, and `index.html` is served network-first, so there's no stale-cached-JS-vs-fresh-HTML risk for the standing cache-bump rule to guard against. **Remaining roadmap items from the design-review artifact** (not done this session, in priority order per the artifact): retune shadows/badges component-by-component for full light-theme parity, a donut-chart entrance animation + softer shadow, list stagger-in animation for transaction/shopping rows, and a skeleton-loading state for the first `fbLoadNow()`.
- **Continued the design-review roadmap: donut-chart entrance animation + list stagger-in for transactions/shopping** (2026-07-13, same design-review session): items 4-5 from the artifact's roadmap. (1) **Analytics donut** (`.analytics-donut`, `renderAnalytics()` in `js/analytics-csv.js`) previously had a flat `conic-gradient` background with no shadow and no entrance animation — added a `filter:drop-shadow(...)` using a new per-theme `--donut-glow` token (purple-tinted, softer in light theme same as the other elevation tokens from the previous session) and a `donutIn` keyframe (`prefers-reduced-motion`-guarded). Since the donut is an existing DOM element whose `.style.background`/`.innerHTML` get mutated in place on every data change (period filter, new transaction) rather than being re-created, a CSS animation class alone only fires once — added the standard `classList.remove` → `void offsetWidth` (forces reflow) → `classList.add` restart dance so the animation replays on every render, not just first paint. (2) **List stagger-in**: added a `rowIn` keyframe (translateY+opacity, `prefers-reduced-motion`-guarded) applied to `.tx-item` (transaction rows, `js/analytics-csv.js`'s `renderFinance()`) and a new `.shop-row` marker class (shopping rows, `js/shopping.js`'s `renderShoppingList()`) — deliberately a *new* class for shopping rather than applying the animation to the shared `.mgr-row` class those rows already carry, since `.mgr-row` is reused by every settings-manager list (wallets, categories, budgets, rates, etc.) and animating all of those wasn't in scope for this pass. Both render loops gained an `idx` param and set `el.style.animationDelay = Math.min(idx*35, 280) + 'ms'` per row, capped so a long list doesn't produce a multi-second cascade. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`, all pass) plus a dedicated one-off Playwright script (not committed): added 4 transactions via the real FAB flow and confirmed `.tx-item` rows carry increasing `animationDelay` values (`0ms`, `35ms`, `70ms`), confirmed `#analytics-donut` picks up the `.donut-anim` class and a non-`none` drop-shadow filter after a real render, added 2 shopping items via the real add-button flow and confirmed both carry `mgr-row shop-row` and a stagger delay — zero console errors, screenshot confirmed no layout breakage. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v27→v28 (this round touches `js/*.js` render behavior, unlike the previous CSS-only round, so the standing cache-bump rule applies here). **Remaining roadmap items**: retuning shadows/badges component-by-component for full light-theme parity (flagged in the artifact as large/gradual, deferred), and a skeleton-loading state for the first `fbLoadNow()` (deferred — touches the load sequence across multiple render functions, wants its own focused pass rather than being folded into this one).
- **Branch-hygiene lesson recurred once more, worth restating tersely since it's now happened at least 3 times**: PR #153 (the donut/stagger PR above) hit the exact same phantom `mergeable_state:"dirty"` 405 already documented for PR #112/#131/#90 — caused by committing PR #153's work on top of the local pre-squash commit from PR #152 instead of fetching `origin/main` first. Fixed the same documented way: `git diff <old-local-commit> <new-tip>` to extract just the new work, `git checkout -B <branch> origin/main`, `git apply` the diff, recommit, `git push --force-with-lease`. Went from `mergeable_state:"dirty"` to `"clean"` immediately. **The actual habit to build, stated as a checklist rather than prose this time**: every single time work resumes on this designated long-lived branch — not just "at the start of a new session" — run `git fetch origin main && git checkout -B <branch> origin/main` *before* the first commit of that unit of work, even if the previous unit of work was merged just minutes earlier in the same session.
- **Note for future sessions: the local stop-hook flags every squash-merged commit on `main` as "Unverified" (committer `noreply@github.com`, not `noreply@anthropic.com`) — this is expected, not a regression to fix.** GitHub's merge API sets the committer identity itself when squash-merging a PR; this is independent of any local `git config` in the session and has been true for every prior PR merged in this repo's history (spot-checked `a3ecec8`, `deeed6b`, `cc13700`, `326abd1`, `d1e0b71` — all show the same pattern). The hook's suggested remedy (amend + force-push) would mean rewriting `main`'s shared history, which conflicts with this repo's own git safety rules (no force-push to main without explicit authorization) and isn't warranted for something this systemic and pre-existing. Asked the account owner directly (2026-07-13) whether to change anything about this — answer: leave it as-is. Don't re-litigate this on a future stop-hook firing for the same reason; just note it and move on.
- **Added the last design-review roadmap item: a skeleton-loading state for the Finance tab's first cold-start `fbLoadNow()` round-trip** (2026-07-13, same design-review session): per CLAUDE.md's own "Client-side caching/sync" section, a *returning* user already gets an instant paint from localStorage before `fbLoadNow()` even runs — the "empty flash, then jump to real data" the artifact flagged only actually happens for a brand-new device/first-ever sign-in with nothing cached yet, where `switchTab('finance')` (called in `js/app-init.js`'s `init()`, before `await fbLoadNow()`) renders a momentarily-empty/zero Finance tab that then visibly jumps once the Firestore round-trip resolves. Scoped the fix to exactly that window rather than every tab: `init()` already computes `cfgCached` (whether a valid config cache was found in localStorage) as a side effect of the existing cache-load logic, so `if(!cfgCached) renderFinanceSkeleton();` right after `switchTab('finance')` (still synchronous, before the first `await`, so the browser never paints the intermediate empty state — only the final skeleton state) is enough to detect "cold start" with no new state tracking. New `renderFinanceSkeleton()` (`js/analytics-csv.js`, next to `renderFinance()`) overwrites `#fin-balances`/`#tx-list-container` with shimmer placeholder blocks (new `.skeleton-block`/`.skeleton-row` CSS classes, `prefers-reduced-motion`-guarded shimmer animation) shaped like the real hero-balance/mini-stat/wallet-chip/transaction-row layout — no explicit cleanup call needed, since `fbLoadNow()` already unconditionally calls `renderFinance()` again once it resolves, which overwrites the skeleton markup with real content the same way it would overwrite genuinely-empty content. Deliberately scoped to the Finance tab only (not Shifts/Debt/Shopping) since it's the only tab whose content actually renders during the cold-start window — the other tabs' render functions only run lazily when the user switches to them via `switchTab()`, by which point the initial `fbLoadNow()` has almost always already resolved. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`, all pass) plus a dedicated one-off Playwright script (not committed) with a *deliberately delayed* (1.5s `setTimeout`) Firestore stub — unlike every other test script's instant-resolving stub, needed here specifically to make the skeleton window observable at all — covering both cases: (1) cold start (no localStorage seeded) shows real skeleton nodes in both containers while the delayed load is in flight, then zero skeleton nodes plus real hero-balance content once it resolves; (2) warm start (localStorage pre-seeded via `page.addInitScript()`, matching a returning user) never shows a single skeleton node and renders the cached transaction instantly instead — confirming the `cfgCached` gate correctly suppresses the skeleton for the common case it isn't needed for. Screenshot of the mid-flight cold-start state confirms no layout breakage. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v28→v29 (changes `js/*.js` render behavior). **This closes out every item from the original design-review artifact's roadmap** (light-theme surface fix, spacing/type/shadow tokens, tinted hero-card shadows, donut-chart animation, list stagger-in, and now this skeleton state) except the one deliberately left as large/gradual: retuning shadows/badges component-by-component for full light-theme parity, which the artifact itself scoped as ongoing work rather than a single pass.
- **Started the light-theme shadow retune, batch 1: 10 plain black/neutral elevation shadows tokenized and tuned per-theme** (2026-07-13, same design-review session): the last deliberately-gradual roadmap item. Grepped every hardcoded `box-shadow`/`filter:drop-shadow` in `index.html` and split them into two categories: plain black `rgba(0,0,0,...)` shadows (simple elevation, no color semantics — the ones that actually look muddy/heavy on a white light-theme surface, per the original design-review artifact's finding) vs. purple-tinted glow shadows (`rgba(139,92,246,...)` on FAB/buttons/badges/tab-glow — a different, deliberately-deferred category since a saturated color glow doesn't have the same "looks wrong on white" problem a neutral black shadow does). This batch did only the first category: 10 usages across `.onboard-icon`, `.auth-card`, `.tabs` (bottom nav), `.quick-action-icon`, `.toggle-track::after` (toggle knob), `.cs-panel`+`.dp-panel` (custom-select/date-picker dropdown popovers — share one token since they already used the identical shadow value), `.debt-chip.active`, `.mgr-row.dragging`, and `#toast`. Added 9 new tokens (`--shadow-onboard-icon`, `--shadow-auth-card`, `--shadow-nav`, `--shadow-quick-icon`, `--shadow-toggle-knob`, `--shadow-popover`, `--shadow-chip-active`, `--shadow-drag`, `--shadow-toast`) to `:root`, each a full box-shadow value referencing `rgba(var(--shadow-color),ALPHA)` (reusing the `--shadow-color` token from the earlier light-theme session: `0,0,0` dark / `20,15,10` warm-tinted light) — offset/blur kept identical to the original per-component value so dark theme renders pixel-identical to before, only the light-theme alpha changed, scaled down by the same ~0.33 ratio `--shadow-modal` already established in the first design-review session (a dark-tuned alpha reads as muddy on white; roughly a third works out close to right by eye). Two inset "glossy sphere" bevel shadows on `.avatar-opt`/`.color-opt` (dark-bottom + light-top inset, simulating a 3D highlight on the colored circle itself) were deliberately left untouched — they're self-contained to the swatch's own circle, not reacting to the page background the way a drop shadow does, so they don't have the "wrong theme" problem the others did. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`, all pass) plus a dedicated one-off Playwright script (not committed) reading all 9 tokens' actual computed values in both themes (confirmed dark values are byte-identical to the pre-change hardcoded ones, confirming zero visual regression there) and confirming `.tabs`' real computed `box-shadow` matches the token — plus a second screenshot-only script capturing the onboarding screen and Settings tab in light theme, visually confirming soft/subtle shadows instead of a heavy black smear. **No `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bump** — CSS-only change inside `index.html`'s own `<style>` block, same reasoning as the earlier `.fin-chart-total` blur-fix and the first design-review round's token session (network-first HTML, no stale-cache risk). **Remaining scope for this item** (next batch, whenever picked up again): the purple-tinted glow shadows — `.lock-logo`, `.tab-btn.active .tab-icon-wrap` (the per-tab `--tab-glow` system), `.day-cell.today`, `.empty-state-icon`, `.add-btn`, `.fin-fab`, `.modal-save`/`.dlg-ok` — a distinct follow-up since the right question there isn't "is this too dark" but "is this too saturated/loud" on a white background, a different tuning judgment call than this batch's straightforward alpha-scaling rule.
- **Light-theme shadow retune, batch 2: purple/colored glow shadows** (2026-07-13, same design-review session, directly following batch 1): the remaining half of the roadmap's "retune shadows for light theme" item — 8 tokens covering `.lock-logo`, the 5-color `.tab-btn.active .tab-icon-wrap` system (purple/green/orange/slate/pink, plus its `tabRipple` pulse keyframe), `.day-cell.today`'s ring, `.empty-state-icon`, `.add-btn`(+hover), `.fin-fab`, and `.modal-save`/`.dlg-ok` (share one token, identical value). **Different tuning rule than batch 1, deliberately**: batch 1's plain black shadows look *muddy* on white (fixed with a ~0.33 alpha ratio); a saturated color glow doesn't have that problem, it looks *louder/more cartoonish* on white instead, since white doesn't recede the color the way near-black does — so this batch used a milder ~0.55-0.6 alpha-reduction ratio, and (unlike `--donut-glow` from an earlier session, which switched to the light-tuned `--purple2` hex) kept the literal `--purple`/tab-color RGB unchanged in both themes, since these shadows sit directly under elements that *are* that exact color (a purple gradient FAB casting a slightly-softer purple shadow is more correct than casting a shifted hue). The 5-color tab-glow system needed 2 new alpha-only tokens (`--tab-glow-shadow-alpha`, `--tab-glow-ripple-alpha`) rather than 5 separate light-tuned color tokens, since the existing `--tab-glow` CSS custom property already carries the raw RGB per active tab and only the alpha needed to vary by theme — kept the RGB values themselves untouched (they're not part of the app's `--green`/`--orange`/etc. token system to begin with; `.tab-btn.tab-c-finance.active` etc. hardcode their own literal green/orange/slate/pink like the box-shadow did). **Deliberately excluded**: the `:focus-visible` outline ring (`box-shadow:0 0 0 4px rgba(139,92,246,.22)`) — an accessibility affordance, not a decorative shadow, and reducing its alpha risks hurting focus-ring visibility rather than fixing a "looks wrong" problem, so it was left exactly as-is rather than assumed to need the same treatment as everything else in this batch. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`, all pass) plus a dedicated one-off Playwright script (not committed) reading all 8 tokens' computed values in both themes (dark values confirmed byte-identical to the pre-change hardcoded ones — zero regression) and confirming `.fin-fab`'s and the active tab icon's real computed `box-shadow` pick up the tokens with the correct alpha, plus screenshots of the Finance tab in both themes confirming the FAB/tab-icon glow reads softer in light theme instead of the previous unturned intensity. **This closes out the entire "retune shadows for light theme" roadmap item and the full original design-review artifact roadmap** — no `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bump needed (CSS-only, same reasoning as every other pure-`index.html`-style change this session).
- **Picked up 3 of the design-review's lower-priority component suggestions** (2026-07-13, same design-review session, after the user explicitly asked for the "менш пріоритетні" items following the shadow-retune close-out): (1) **`.btn-danger` gap fix**: re-checked the original review's claim that the app had "no third button variant for destructive actions" before implementing anything — that claim was wrong. `.btn-danger` already exists in `index.html` (a translucent-red/hover-fills-red variant) and is already correctly used on 5 real destructive actions (delete debt, remove PIN, clear month, unlink phone, delete category). The one real gap: `#shopping-clear-btn` ("Очистити куплені") still used the neutral `.btn-ghost`, despite deleting data the same way `clear-current-month` (already `.btn-danger`) does — switched it. **Lesson**: worth re-verifying a review's own findings with a fresh grep before acting on them; the original review missed this class entirely, probably from reading only the `.btn`/`.btn-ghost`/`.btn-primary` cluster and not searching separately for `.btn-danger`. (2) **Calendar day-cell shift-type tint**: `.day-cell.has-shifts` previously only changed `border-color`/`.day-num` text color — the shift-type's own color was only visible via the small `.badge` pill's text, not the cell itself, so a month didn't visually "read" as colored patches at a glance. `js/calendar.js`'s `renderCalendar()` now sets a `--cell-tint` custom property (via the file's existing `hexA()` helper, same `.07` alpha `.day-cell.today` already uses for its own tint — reused for consistency) from the day's first shift type, and `.day-cell.has-shifts{background:var(--cell-tint,var(--bg2))}` picks it up. **Real bug caught by the verification script, not by code review**: `.day-cell.weekend-cell{background:rgba(239,68,68,.03)}` was declared *after* `.has-shifts` in the stylesheet — equal specificity (two classes each), so on any day that was both a weekend *and* had a shift, the weekend tint silently always won, making the new shift-type tint invisible on Saturdays/Sundays specifically (2 of every 7 days). Fixed by moving `.weekend-cell` before the `.has-shifts` cluster so a cell with actual shift data takes priority over the generic weekend look, which also matches the intent better (a real shift is more informative than "this happens to be a weekend"). Multi-shift days use only the *first* shift's color (deliberate simplification — color-blending multiple shift-type hues for a day with several shifts wasn't worth the complexity for a "read at a glance" feature). (3) **Debt-chip active state gradient + tinted shadow**: `.debt-chip.active` previously used a flat `background:var(--chip-color,var(--purple))` and the plain neutral `--shadow-chip-active` token from shadow-retune batch 1 — didn't match the gradient-background + color-tinted-shadow treatment the active tab icons already have. Since a debt's chip color is arbitrary user-picked hex (via the shared color-picker pattern), not a fixed palette value, used CSS `color-mix(in srgb, var(--chip-color,var(--purple)) X%, ...)` to derive both a darker gradient stop (`65%` mixed with black) and a tinted shadow (`color-mix(... var(--chip-shadow-mix), transparent)`) directly in CSS with no JS color math needed — `--chip-shadow-mix` is a new token (`45%` dark / `28%` light, continuing batch 2's "milder reduction for glow shadows" rule) so the shadow's intensity is still theme-aware despite the base color being fully dynamic. The now-single-use `--shadow-chip-active` token from batch 1 was removed rather than left dangling, since nothing else referenced it. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`, all pass) plus a dedicated one-off Playwright script (not committed): confirms `#shopping-clear-btn` carries `btn-danger` and resolves to the red text color; adds a real shift via the day-modal and confirms the resulting `.has-shifts` cell's *actual computed background* (not just the custom property) matches the shift type's tinted color — this is what caught the weekend-cell ordering bug, a custom-property-only check would have missed it since the property itself was always set correctly, only the final cascade resolution was wrong; adds a debt via the real `uiPrompt()` "+" flow (a brand-new account starts with zero debts, same gotcha already documented earlier in this file) and confirms the active chip's computed `background-image` contains a gradient and its `box-shadow` is non-`none`. Screenshots of both the calendar (visible blue-tinted "5" cell) and debt tab (visible purple-gradient active chip) confirm no layout breakage. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v29→v30 (this round changes `js/calendar.js` render behavior, unlike the two shadow-retune batches which were CSS-only).
- **Flipped CSP from report-only to enforcing** (2026-07-13): the report-only monitoring period (see the "CSP report-only check requested" entry above) had already come back clean from a real-device console check, and this session the user gave the explicit go-ahead this file's own CSP entry said was the last blocking condition ("CSP зроби"). Changed `firebase.json`'s header key from `Content-Security-Policy-Report-Only` to `Content-Security-Policy` — the policy value itself is unchanged (same `default-src 'self'; script-src 'self' https://www.gstatic.com; ...` string from the original CSP-hardening pass). **Verified beyond just re-running the existing suite**: wrote a one-off Playwright script (not committed) that reads the *actual* enforcing header value straight out of `firebase.json` (so it can't silently drift from what's really configured), serves `index.html` through a tiny local HTTP server that injects that real header on every `.html` response (unlike report-only, an enforcing header actually blocks non-conforming resources instead of just logging, so this needed a real enforcing response, not another `securitypolicyviolation`-listener-only check), and drives the full stubbed-Firebase flow — sign-in, all 5 tabs, opening the Finance FAB modal and closing it via the real backdrop click, opening Settings — while listening for both `securitypolicyviolation` events and console/page errors. Zero of either. Also ran the full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`, all pass — unaffected, since none of them route through a server that sets this header, this was specifically why the dedicated one-off script above was necessary). **This verification's real limitation, same one already flagged when this was first set to report-only**: the stubbed-Firebase sandbox environment can only prove the same-origin script/style/module graph is clean under real enforcement — it has no way to exercise the actual cross-origin flows this policy is riskiest for (a real Google Sign-In popup, phone-auth's invisible reCAPTCHA iframe, a live Firestore read/write, real FCM token registration, the NBU/PrivatBank rate fetches) since those are exactly the things the stub replaces. The real-device confirmation for those already happened in report-only mode per the earlier entry (console showed zero CSP violations across normal use), which is what makes flipping to enforcing now reasonable rather than reckless — but if a real user hits an auth/push/rates issue shortly after this deploys, **the fastest diagnosis path is checking whether it's CSP-caused first** (revert is a single-line change: flip the header key back to `-Report-Only` in `firebase.json` and redeploy hosting) before assuming it's a code regression. Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a clean `origin/main` worktree. No `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bump — this only changes a Hosting response header in `firebase.json`, not any `index.html`/`js/*.js` content the service worker precaches.
- **Fresh design-review pass (published as an Artifact) plus "виправ все" — implemented the full prioritized punch list from it in one session** (2026-07-13, new session, same branch continued): user asked for a from-scratch design review, then to fix everything it found. The review itself was grounded in the *current* code (not a stale baseline — this repo had already been through the design-review-artifact session above) — read `index.html`'s actual CSS tokens/components and took fresh Playwright screenshots (dark+light, 390×844) before writing anything, scoring the app 8.2/10. Full review is a published Artifact (not re-pasted here); this entry logs what was actually shipped from its punch list:
  - **Real bug, quick fix**: `js/ui-widgets.js`'s `enhanceAllSelects()` scoped its one-time `querySelectorAll` to `.app select`/`.app input[type=date]` — but several controls live in modals that are DOM *siblings* of `<main class="app">`, not descendants of it, so they silently stayed unstyled native browser controls forever. Confirmed 3 real instances by reading the actual DOM structure (not guessing): `#fin-date` in `#tx-form-modal` (the date field in "Нова операція" — visible in a screenshot as a native date popup among otherwise-custom-styled dark inputs), and two more the review's own code-reading turned up beyond what the screenshot alone showed: `#fx-conv-from`/`#fx-conv-to` in the FX-converter panel (`populateFxConverterSelects()` never called `enhanceSelect` after setting `innerHTML`) and `#goal-new-wallet` in the new-goal form (`renderNewGoalForm()` same gap). Fixed by dropping the `.app` scope from `enhanceAllSelects()` entirely (both helpers are idempotent via a `dataset.enhanced` guard, so widening the selector is safe) plus adding the two missing explicit `enhanceSelect()` calls after dynamic population.
  - **Ambient glow**: extended the radial purple glow that previously only existed on `.lock-screen` to `.app` itself (`radial-gradient(480px circle at 50% 0%, ...)`, `.06` alpha dark / `.035` light) — every screen now has a faint top-anchored atmosphere instead of only the auth screen.
  - **Tab-switch crossfade**: added a `.tab-content` class to all 5 `<section id="tab-*">` elements and a `tabContentIn` keyframe, restarted on every `switchTab()` call the same forced-reflow-restart trick already used for `.donut-anim` — switching tabs is now a soft 180ms fade+rise instead of an instant hard cut.
  - **Typography rebalance**: the review found `font-weight` values clustering almost entirely in 600-900 (only 7 of 127 declarations used 500, zero used 400) — lowered a curated set of genuinely-secondary caption classes (`.tx-meta`, `.settings-row-sub`, `.stat-sub`, `.analytics-cat-amt` → 400/500, `.settings-row-title`/`.fin-mini-stat-label` → 600, `.chip-stat-lbl` → 500) and raised the two true "hero number" classes (`.hero-balance-val`/`.hero-metric-val`, 30px→34px + `letter-spacing:-.02em`) so the weight/size range actually has contrast instead of everything reading at similar volume. Deliberately a curated pass, not all 127 declarations — matches this repo's own established pattern of gradual token-adoption (e.g. the spacing-scale migration) rather than a risky one-shot rewrite of the whole stylesheet.
  - **Sliding segment-control indicator**: added `initSegThumb(container, {tint})` (`js/ui-widgets.js`) — a `ResizeObserver`+`MutationObserver`-driven sliding "thumb" pill, applied to exactly 3 fixed-width equal-segment controls (`#fin-type-seg` income/expense/transfer, `.auth-tabs` login/register, `.fin-chart-toggle` Баланс/Дохід/Витрата) via one `initSegThumb()` call each in `__init_ui_widgets__()` — deliberately *not* a global `.type-btn.active` rule, since the category-manager type toggle and the theme/lang chip rows are variable-width wrapping rows where a sliding thumb doesn't make sense (left untouched, still the old background-swap style). The `ResizeObserver` (rather than manually calling a reposition function from every toggle handler scattered across `finance.js`/`auth.js`/`calendar.js`) is what makes this safe to init once and forget — it correctly fires when a container goes from `display:none` (a closed modal) to visible, so there was no need to touch `setFinanceType`/`setAuthMode`/`setFinChartSeries` at all. The income/expense/transfer thumb also carries the semantic tint color (green/red/blue) via an `opts.tint(activeBtn)` callback, preserving the pre-existing color-coding that a flat neutral thumb would have erased.
  - **Bottom-sheet modals + drag-to-dismiss**: `.sheet-grabber` existed in the markup of all 22 `.modal-card` instances but was permanently `display:none` — turned it on under the existing 600px breakpoint (`.modal-overlay{align-items:flex-end}`, `.modal-card{border-radius:26px 26px 0 0}`, a `sheetUp` slide-in keyframe) so every manager modal presents as a native-feeling bottom sheet on mobile instead of a centered scale-in popup. Added real drag-to-dismiss: `initSheetDrag(card, onDismiss)` (`js/ui-widgets.js`) using Pointer Events scoped strictly to the `.sheet-grabber` handle itself (never the surrounding `.modal-card-body`, so it can't fight that body's own scroll) — drags past 110px call `onDismiss()` after a slide-away transition, shorter drags snap back. Wired from two places since `#shift-modal` (the calendar day-detail modal) has its own `closeModal()` and isn't in `closeManagers()`'s id list (a PR #119 fix, documented above, made that split deliberate): `settings-managers.js`'s `__init_settings_managers__()` wires every other `.modal-card` to `closeManagers`, `calendar.js`'s `__init_calendar__()` wires `#shift-modal` specifically to its own `closeModal`.
  - **Gradient-stroke hero cards**: added `--surface-hero`/`--stroke-hero` tokens and a `::before` gradient-border trick (`mask-composite:xor`/`exclude`, the standard cross-browser CSS gradient-border technique) to `.hero-metric`/`.hero-balance` — the two "this is the one number that matters on this screen" cards (Finance balance, Shifts earned, Debt balance) now have a subtle purple gradient ring and tonal fill instead of the flat single-tone `bg1`+1px-border every other card uses; every other card (`.chart-section`, `.cal-wrap`, `.fin-form`, `.mgr-row`, etc.) is untouched — additive, not a replacement of the existing `--bg1`/`--bg2`/`--bg3` system.
  - **Deliberately not done this pass** (flagged in the review as bigger/riskier lifts, or explicitly gradual): migrating the remaining ~120 hardcoded px spacing values to the `--sp-*` tokens (still "apply going forward," same as the existing spacing-scale precedent); extending the sliding-thumb treatment to the category-manager/theme/lang chip rows (different shape of problem, wrapping variable-width rows, not a drop-in reuse of `initSegThumb`).
  - **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`/`functions-sweep`, all pass) plus two dedicated one-off Playwright scripts (not committed): one exercising every fix directly (14 assertions — date-picker wrapping, both newly-found select fixes, ambient-glow background-image, tab-crossfade class, segment-thumb position+tint on `#fin-type-seg` and separately on `.auth-tabs`, hero-card `::before` pseudo-element, the typography weight change, bottom-sheet corner radius + grabber visibility, and both drag-to-dismiss outcomes — past-threshold dismiss and below-threshold snap-back, driven via synthetic `PointerEvent`s since Playwright's own touch/mouse APIs don't cleanly simulate a single continuous pointer capture sequence) — all passed, zero unexpected console/page errors (the one caught "failure" was the already-documented expected live-rates-fetch noise, a filter-regex miss in the verification script itself, not a real issue; confirmed by reading the actual error text against CLAUDE.md's own documented exception); a second script for screenshots only (Finance tab dark+light, an open bottom sheet) to visually confirm no layout breakage — all clean. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v30→v31 (this pass changes `js/*.js` behavior new HTML markup depends on — `data-action`-adjacent wiring like every prior onclick-removal phase — so the standing stale-cache rule applies).
  - **Merged and deployed**: PR [#161](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/161), squash-merged as `a805503` after both CI jobs (`smoke`, `firestore-rules`) went green (~70s total). Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add` off `origin/main` (not the long-lived session worktree, per the standing lesson from the earlier `functions/node_modules`-exposure incident above) — succeeded on the first attempt, log read "found 55 files in ."
