(matches the expected count from every prior hosting-only deploy this session's history logs, no `node_modules`-style anomaly). GitHub Pages auto-deploys on push to `main`, no separate action needed. Firestore rules and Cloud Functions had no changes this pass, nothing to redeploy there.
- **User-reported login failure investigated (real device, both email/password and phone) — resolved as user-side, but surfaced one real leftover-branding gap** (2026-07-13, same session): user hit "Помилка входу. Спробуйте ще раз." on email/password sign-in and "SMS тимчасово недоступні..." on phone sign-in, both on a real Android device. The phone one is the already-well-documented carrier/region SMS block (see the Auth section above, Firebase Support case 10414309) — expected, not actionable. The email one mapped to `authErrorMessage()`'s **generic fallback** (`js/auth.js`), meaning the real Firebase error code wasn't one of the ~18 explicitly handled ones — worth investigating rather than assuming a typo. This sandbox has no `gcloud` CLI and no sanctioned way to query Identity Platform's sign-in error logs directly (minting a raw OAuth token from `claude-deploy@`'s service-account key for that is a sensitive pattern flagged in the "phone sign-in SMS" investigation entry above as needing explicit per-use authorization, not something to reach for speculatively) — so asked the user to trigger "Забули пароль?" as a lower-risk diagnostic instead. **Result: the reset email arrived successfully** (confirmed via a real screenshot of the user's inbox), which confirms the account exists and the Firebase Auth backend/email delivery pipeline is healthy — the original login error was very likely just a mistyped password, not a systemic issue. **Real, separate finding from that screenshot**: the password-reset email itself is still branded **"Xamss"** ("Reset your password for Xamss" / "Your Xamss team") — the pre-rename app name. Grepped the whole repo for "Xamss" and found zero other occurrences (the rename to "Zminka" is otherwise complete) — this is because Firebase Auth's email templates (Authentication → Templates in the Console) are configured out-of-band from this repo's code, not something a PR can fix. Documented as a manual to-do in `SETUP.md` §7 (new section) — update Password reset / Email verification / Email change templates' text from "Xamss" to "Zminka" — plus a lower-priority note that the email landed in the user's Spam folder (Gmail), likely just the default `noreply@<project>.firebaseapp.com` sender lacking SPF/DKIM, fixable later via a custom sending domain in the same Templates section if it becomes a real problem. Neither fix applied this session — both need the account owner's hands in the Firebase Console UI, not a code change.
- **Fixed a real, launch-relevant bug: Google sign-in silently fails in the installed TWA/APK, works fine in a browser tab** (2026-07-13, same session, direct follow-up to the SMS/email investigation above): user confirmed via live testing — "Помилка входу" (the same generic `authErrorMessage()` fallback as the email case above) from both the installed TWA icon and the sideloaded APK, but signing in via Google succeeds from a plain browser tab/link on the same device. This is a known, well-documented class of issue: TWAs (and standalone-launched/Add-to-Home-Screen PWAs) are a stripped-down Custom-Tab shell without full multi-window browser chrome, so `window.open()`-based popups — which is how `signInWithPopup(auth, googleProvider)` (`js/auth.js`) works — are unreliable or fail outright in that context, unrelated to anything in this repo's own CSP/config (`firebase.json` sets no `Cross-Origin-Opener-Policy` header at all, ruled out directly). **Real production consequence**: since "Google Play submission is mid-flight" (see that section above) and *every* Play Store install will run as a TWA, this would have broken Google sign-in — one of only 3 sign-in methods, and the one with no known carrier/region caveats unlike phone — for 100% of Play Store users at launch, not just this one report. **Fix**: added `isPopupUnreliableContext()` (`js/auth.js`) — detects a TWA via `document.referrer.startsWith('android-app://')` (the standard, documented signal) or a standalone-launched PWA via `matchMedia('(display-mode: standalone)')` — and `googleSignIn()` now calls `signInWithRedirect(auth, googleProvider)` instead of `signInWithPopup` in either case, falling back to the existing popup path everywhere else (desktop/mobile browser tabs, where popups work fine and are faster/less disruptive). Added `signInWithRedirect`/`getRedirectResult` to `core.js`'s Firebase Auth import + its explicit re-export list (the pattern this file already uses for every other pass-through SDK function — `export {...}` at the bottom, since import statements themselves can't carry `export`). `getRedirectResult(auth).catch(...)` added inside `__init_auth__()` (not bare top-level, per this file's own module-layout rule for new side-effecting code) to complete the flow and surface any error after the full-page navigation back from Google — `onAuthStateChanged` already handles the success path, this only needed to cover the failure path a redirect flow has no synchronous try/catch for. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`, all pass — needed adding `signInWithRedirect`/`getRedirectResult` stub exports to all 3 Playwright test files' hand-written `firebase-auth.js` stubs first, or the whole module graph fails to import per this repo's own documented "missing export blanks the whole page" gotcha) plus a dedicated one-off Playwright script (not committed) built specifically to prove the *branching* logic itself, not just that the page still loads: a stubbed `signInWithPopup`/`signInWithRedirect`/`getRedirectResult` that each push a tag onto `window.__authCalls`, tested across 3 contexts — plain browser (popup fires, redirect doesn't), simulated TWA via `Object.defineProperty(document,'referrer',...)` in a Playwright `addInitScript` (redirect fires, popup doesn't), and simulated standalone via overriding `window.matchMedia` to fake `display-mode: standalone` (same result) — all 7 assertions passed, zero console/page errors in any context. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v31→v32 (changes `js/*.js` behavior).
  - **Correction from an automated PR review (Codex), confirmed correct and applied**: the redirect fallback above was necessary but not sufficient — `js/core.js` still initialized Firebase with `authDomain:"maxtr-c238f.firebaseapp.com"`, while the app's actual canonical serving domain is `maxtr-c238f.web.app` (see "Android / Google Play packaging" above). Firebase's own [redirect best-practices doc](https://firebase.google.com/docs/auth/web/redirect-best-practices) is explicit: `signInWithRedirect`'s result is relayed back through an `authDomain`-hosted helper page, and if `authDomain` doesn't match the app's own serving domain, browsers that partition/block third-party storage (increasingly the default, and Android WebView/TWA contexts — exactly what this fix targets — tend to run under *more* restrictive storage policies, not less) can lose the redirect result entirely, leaving the user still signed out after a "successful" round trip to Google. Fixed by changing `authDomain` to `"maxtr-c238f.web.app"` in both `js/core.js` (main app) and `sw.js` (duplicate config used for FCM background messages) — now first-party relative to the canonical Hosting domain, so the helper page loads same-origin. **Follow-on fix this required**: `firebase.json`'s CSP `frame-src` only allowed `https://*.firebaseapp.com` (plus `https://www.google.com` for reCAPTCHA) — added `https://*.web.app` too, or the app's own enforcing CSP would have blocked the very auth iframe this change was meant to make reliable. `maxtr-c238f.web.app` was already an Authorized domain (automatic for any `*.web.app`/`*.firebaseapp.com` of the same project, per SETUP.md §2), so no Firebase Console change was needed. **Verified**: full local suite re-run (all pass — `authDomain`'s value doesn't affect the stubbed-Firebase test flow, but this confirms the edit didn't break anything else), plus a dedicated one-off Playwright script (not committed) serving `index.html` with the *real* enforcing CSP header read straight out of `firebase.json` (same recipe as the original CSP-enforcement verification) and driving all 5 tabs + the Finance FAB while listening for `securitypolicyviolation` events — zero violations, confirming the widened `frame-src` doesn't regress the CSP work from the earlier session. **Lesson**: an automated review bot's suggestion is worth actually verifying against the specific deployment's config (not reflexively applying or dismissing) — this one correctly connected a documented Firebase best-practice to this repo's specific `authDomain`/hosting-domain mismatch, something neither the original bug report nor the first pass at this fix had caught, and would have left the reported TWA sign-in bug only partially fixed.
  - **Merged and deployed**: PR [#164](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/164), squash-merged as `c37aad9` after both CI jobs (`smoke`, `firestore-rules`) went green. Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add` off `origin/main` — succeeded on the first attempt, log read "found 55 files in ." (matches the expected count, no `node_modules`-style anomaly). GitHub Pages auto-deploys on push to `main`. **Not yet re-tested live by the reporting user** (this session has no way to drive a real Android TWA/APK install) — the fix is verified as far as this sandbox's stubbed-Firebase Playwright recipe can reach (branching logic correct, CSP clean under the real enforcing header), but the actual real-device confirmation (does Google sign-in now succeed from the installed TWA/APK) still needs the user to retest and report back.
- **The `authDomain` change from the Codex-review follow-up above was itself a regression — reverted same session, real-device tested this time.** Real-device retest came back with Google's own OAuth error screen, `Error 400: redirect_uri_mismatch`, from **both** the TWA and the APK (a real screenshot from `accounts.google.com`, not our app). Root cause: switching `authDomain` from `maxtr-c238f.firebaseapp.com` to `maxtr-c238f.web.app` changes the `redirect_uri` our app's OAuth request sends to Google — but the underlying Google Cloud Console OAuth 2.0 Client (auto-created by Firebase when Google sign-in was first enabled) only has `https://maxtr-c238f.firebaseapp.com/__/auth/handler` registered as an **authorized redirect URI**, not the `.web.app` equivalent. Being in Firebase Auth's own "Authorized domains" list (which I'd verified before making the change) is a **separate, unrelated check** from Google's OAuth client redirect-URI allowlist — the former is Firebase's own guard against `auth/unauthorized-domain`, the latter is enforced by Google's OAuth server itself and was never going to be satisfied just because the domain happened to already be Firebase-authorized. **This made things strictly worse than the original bug report**: before, only the TWA/APK path was broken (browser tab still worked); after the `authDomain` change, `redirect_uri_mismatch` broke **every** Google sign-in path, including the previously-working browser tab, since popup mode also routes through `authDomain`. **Reverted immediately**: `authDomain` back to `maxtr-c238f.firebaseapp.com` in both `js/core.js` and `sw.js`, keeping the `isPopupUnreliableContext()`/`signInWithRedirect` TWA-detection logic from the original fix intact (that part was correct and unaffected by this). Left the CSP `frame-src` widening (`https://*.web.app`) in place — harmless on its own, and needed if `authDomain` is ever correctly migrated later. **The Codex suggestion itself wasn't wrong on the general Firebase best-practice** — it's just incomplete for this specific project: actually adopting `maxtr-c238f.web.app` as `authDomain` would need the corresponding `https://maxtr-c238f.web.app/__/auth/handler` redirect URI added to the OAuth client in **Google Cloud Console → APIs & Services → Credentials** first (a manual step, same category as the Console-only fixes documented elsewhere in this file) — not attempted this session, and not worth re-attempting without that prerequisite in place first. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v32→v33. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`, all pass — `authDomain`'s literal value doesn't affect the stubbed test flow either way). **Lesson, stated plainly**: "Authorized domain" in Firebase Auth settings and "authorized redirect URI" in the underlying Google OAuth client are two different allowlists enforced by two different systems — confirming one is populated does not imply the other is, and this gap is invisible from Firebase Console's own Authentication UI (it only ever surfaces as Google's OAuth error page, which nothing in this sandbox's stubbed-Firebase test setup can reach). Next time an `authDomain` change is considered, check the actual OAuth client's redirect URIs in Google Cloud Console directly, not just Firebase's Authorized domains list.
  - **A second automated review comment (Codex) on the revert PR correctly restated the residual trade-off**: reverting `authDomain` fixes the confirmed `redirect_uri_mismatch` break but re-opens the theoretical third-party-storage risk for `signInWithRedirect` in TWA/WebView contexts, since `authDomain` (`firebaseapp.com`) is cross-site relative to the serving origin (`web.app`) again. No new action taken — this is exactly the trade-off already reasoned through and documented above; the bot's own suggested fix (add the `.web.app` redirect URI in Google Cloud Console) needs the account owner's manual Console access, same as already noted, and doesn't change the decision to revert now given the confirmed-broken state took priority over the unconfirmed theoretical one. **Merged and deployed**: PR [#166](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/166), squash-merged as `6b9ec7f` after both CI jobs went green. Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add` off `origin/main` — succeeded on the first attempt, "found 55 files in .". GitHub Pages auto-deploys on push to `main`. **Still needs real-device confirmation from the user** that Google sign-in (from a browser tab, and separately from the TWA/APK) works again post-revert — not yet re-tested as of this entry.
- **Root-caused and fixed the TWA/APK Google sign-in failure for real this time — confirmed via a real console log, not guesswork.** User confirmed post-revert: plain browser/PC sign-in via Google works again (screenshot showed a real signed-in session with live data). TWA/APK still failed, but this time with **no Google OAuth error page** — the request now reaches Google fine — instead the app itself bounced back to the login screen with the generic `authErrorMessage()` fallback. Asked the user to get the real error via `chrome://inspect` (USB debugging, since TWA content is inspectable the same as any Chrome tab) rather than guess again after the previous regression — deliberate change of approach given guessing already broke things once this session. **Real error captured**: `FirebaseError: Firebase: Error (auth/internal-error)`, thrown from deep inside `firebase-auth.js`'s internal XHR error handler (`n.onerror`) — a generic catch-all Firebase throws when an internal SDK call fails without a more specific code, consistent with exactly the storage-partitioning failure mode Codex's review had flagged: `authDomain` (`firebaseapp.com`) being cross-site relative to the TWA's actual origin (`web.app`) breaks the SDK's ability to read back the redirect result. This confirms Codex's theory was correct, not just plausible. **The real, complete fix needed two parts, not one** — this is why the first attempt (PR #164) broke things: (1) `authDomain` must equal the serving origin (`web.app`), **and** (2) the Google Cloud Console OAuth 2.0 Client's Authorized redirect URIs must include `https://maxtr-c238f.web.app/__/auth/handler` — doing only (1) without (2) is what produced the `redirect_uri_mismatch` regression. **Verified there's no API path for step (2)**: unlike most GCP resources, "Web application" OAuth 2.0 Client ID redirect URIs have no public, documented REST API — they're Console-UI-only (confirmed from direct technical knowledge before attempting anything, specifically to avoid repeating the previous session's mistake of acting on an unverified assumption) — so did **not** attempt this via `claude-deploy@`'s elevated IAM permissions despite the user offering to authorize it, since there's no legitimate API call to make; calling an undocumented internal Console endpoint would be exactly the kind of brittle, unsupported workaround this repo's own conventions warn against. Gave the user the direct Console link (`console.cloud.google.com/apis/credentials?project=maxtr-c238f`) and exact steps instead. **User added the redirect URI manually, confirmed done** — only then was `authDomain` switched back to `"maxtr-c238f.web.app"` in `js/core.js` and `sw.js` (the same one-line change as PR #164, now safe since the prerequisite is actually in place this time). `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v33→v34. **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`/`smoke`/`e2e-crud`/`e2e-modals`, all pass — as before, `authDomain`'s value doesn't affect the stubbed test flow, real verification is necessarily device-side). **Lesson for this specific class of fix, worth remembering if `authDomain` ever needs touching again**: a Firebase config value that looks like a pure app-code change can have a silent, external prerequisite (an OAuth client's redirect URI allowlist) that's invisible from this repo, from Firebase Console's Authentication UI, and from any tool available in this sandbox — the only way either half of this fix's correctness was ever actually confirmed was a real device's console log, twice (once to catch the `redirect_uri_mismatch`, once to catch the `auth/internal-error`). Neither failure mode is reproducible in the stubbed-Firebase Playwright sandbox this repo's automated tests run in.
  - **Merged and deployed**: PR [#168](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/168), squash-merged as `ce2eedb` after both CI jobs went green. Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add` off `origin/main` — succeeded on the first attempt, "found 55 files in .". GitHub Pages auto-deploys on push to `main`. **Still needs one more real-device retest**: does Google sign-in now succeed from the installed TWA/APK with both halves of the fix in place (code + the manually-added Google Cloud Console redirect URI)? Not yet re-confirmed as of this entry — this is the third real-device round-trip for this specific bug, each one having narrowed the root cause further (popup failure → `redirect_uri_mismatch` → `auth/internal-error`), so a fourth confirmation is what would actually close out this issue.
- **Fourth real-device round: same `auth/internal-error`, but a genuinely new, better-scoped root cause — and a real regression this session had introduced without realizing it.** User confirmed browser/PC sign-in was now stable (screenshot of a signed-in session), but TWA/APK still showed the identical `auth/internal-error` stack trace as before, byte-for-byte, despite both halves of the previous fix (matching `authDomain` + the Google Cloud Console redirect URI) being in place. Critical follow-up question asked before touching any more code (after already causing one blind-fix regression this session, deliberately slowing down this time): **does the error appear immediately on app open, or only after tapping the Google button?** Answer: **immediately, before any interaction.** This reframed the whole bug — it was never really about the redirect round-trip failing, it was `getRedirectResult(auth)` (added in PR #164, called unconditionally in `__init_auth__()` on *every* app load) rejecting with `auth/internal-error` in this specific TWA/WebView's environment regardless of whether a Google sign-in was ever attempted — almost certainly an IndexedDB/persistence-access restriction specific to that WebView provider, unrelated to `authDomain` at all. **Real production impact**: every single TWA/APK user was seeing a scary "Помилка входу" banner the instant they opened the app, whether they ever touched the Google button or not — a regression PR #164 introduced and no prior session entry had caught, because the stubbed-Firebase Playwright sandbox's `getRedirectResult()` stub always resolves cleanly (`Promise.resolve(null)`), so this specific rejection-on-every-load behavior was never exercised locally. **Fix**: added `GOOGLE_REDIRECT_PENDING_KEY` (`js/auth.js`) — `googleSignIn()` now sets a `sessionStorage` flag immediately before calling `signInWithRedirect()`, and the `getRedirectResult().catch()` handler only calls `setAuthError(...)` if that flag is present (confirming a redirect was actually attempted this session), clearing the flag in a `.finally()` regardless of outcome so it can't linger and cause a stale false-positive on some later unrelated load. Failures with no pending flag are still `console.error`-logged for diagnosability, just not shown to the user. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v34→v35. **Verified, and this verification itself hit a real test-infrastructure gotcha worth documenting**: the first draft of a dedicated one-off Playwright script (not committed) simulating "app reopens after a redirect attempt" via `page.reload()` failed in a confusing way — after the reload, the stubbed `getRedirectResult()` never got called at all (no console log from the stub), because this app's real `sw.js` service worker had already registered and activated during the first load, and on the second navigation it intercepted fetches *before* Playwright's `page.route()` stubs could apply, breaking the whole module graph silently (`ERR_CONNECTION_RESET`/`ERR_FAILED` on the real, unreachable gstatic.com/firebase URLs the SW's own fetch handler tried to pass through). Fixed by launching the test browser context with `serviceWorkers: 'block'`. A second, subtler issue after that: even with the SW blocked, the very first assertion (error shown right after a genuine pending-redirect load) still failed — root cause was a **pre-existing, unrelated line** in this file's `onAuthStateChanged` handler, `setAuthError('')`, unconditionally called on every *signed-out* callback invocation (a reasonable original intent — clear a stale previous-session error on fresh load) — my test stub's `getRedirectResult()` rejected synchronously (a same-tick microtask), running *before* `onAuthStateChanged`'s callback (a `setTimeout(...,0)` macrotask in the stub) — so the clear ran *after* my error-set and wiped it, an ordering that happened to be the reverse of the real device's actual timing (where the error visibly persisted, confirming Firebase's real SDK resolves `getRedirectResult()` later than its own initial `onAuthStateChanged` callback). Fixed by making the stub's `getRedirectResult()` reject via a short `setTimeout` instead of synchronously, matching the real ordering — all 4 assertions then passed correctly (no error on a normal load with no pending flag; no error before ever clicking Google; error *does* show right after a genuine pending-redirect load; the flag clears so a third, unrelated load doesn't keep re-showing a stale error). **Lesson, worth remembering for any future test script that does more than one navigation on the same page**: an already-registered service worker from an earlier navigation in the same script can silently break `page.route()` interception on a later navigation — block service workers via the browser context (`serviceWorkers: 'block'`) for any Playwright script that calls `goto()`/`reload()` more than once against this app. **Second lesson**: a hand-written stub's promise-resolution timing (sync vs. async) can produce a different, misleading result than the real SDK if the app code has any ordering dependency between two independently-registered async handlers — when a test result looks wrong, check whether the *stub's* timing model actually matches the real library's before assuming the app code is broken.
  - **Merged and deployed**: PR [#170](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/170), squash-merged as `ef247a9` after both CI jobs went green. Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add` off `origin/main` — succeeded on the first attempt, "found 55 files in .". GitHub Pages auto-deploys on push to `main`. **Still needs real-device confirmation**: does the "Помилка входу" banner still appear immediately on TWA/APK app open (should now be gone entirely), and separately — does an actual Google sign-in attempt from the TWA/APK now succeed end-to-end (the `authDomain` + Google Cloud Console redirect-URI fix from the prior entry should already cover this, but hasn't been cleanly confirmed yet since every real-device retest so far hit this *other* bug first). Not yet re-tested as of this entry.
- **Fifth real-device round confirmed the previous fix worked exactly as scoped, and found the actual CSP gap blocking Google sign-in — this time backed by a live, direct test, not another guess.** User confirmed the "error on every load" regression from the prior entry is gone (no banner on plain app open). Then tapped "Продовжити через Google" and got `auth/internal-error` again — but *only* after tapping, confirming the guard is working correctly (it's not hiding a real failure, the real failure is still there). Before touching code again, asked the user to run a direct IndexedDB probe in the same open DevTools console (`indexedDB.open(...)`) to test the storage-partitioning theory directly rather than guess a third time — **result: `IDB OK`, ruling that theory out entirely.** Re-read the *same* console screenshot more carefully instead of just the final error line, and found a real, functional CSP violation buried among the already-known-harmless `.js.map` sourcemap noise: `Loading the script 'https://apis.google.com/js/api.js?onload=__iframecb...' violates ... script-src 'self' https://www.gstatic.com` — a genuine blocked script load (gapi's loader, used internally by Google Identity's redirect flow), not a devtools-only artifact like the `.map` violations. Our CSP's `script-src` never included `https://apis.google.com` — only `www.gstatic.com`. **Fix**: added `https://apis.google.com` to both `script-src` and `connect-src`, and `https://content.googleapis.com` to `frame-src` (gapi's iframe postMessage relay target) in `firebase.json`. **Verified**: full local suite (all pass) plus the same real-enforcing-CSP-header Playwright script used for every prior CSP change in this repo, re-run with the updated policy — zero violations in the stubbed-Firebase flow (this sandbox still can't load the real `apis.google.com` script to confirm it now actually succeeds, only that our own policy syntax is valid and doesn't regress anything else). No `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bump — CSP-header-only change in `firebase.json`, same reasoning as every prior CSP-only entry (network-first HTML, no stale-cache risk). **Lesson, distinct from every earlier one this session**: when scanning a real console log for the actual failure, don't stop at the first/most-visible error or assume every CSP violation in the list is the already-known `.js.map` noise — read each one; this specific violation was sitting in the middle of five near-identical `.map`-file violations and easy to skim past, but was the one that actually mattered. This is also the first fix this session grounded in *directly reading real console output* rather than inferring from a stack trace or a documented best-practices doc — worth defaulting to that first next time, before theorizing.

Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add` off `origin/main` — succeeded on the first attempt, "found 55 files in .". - **CONFIRMED FIXED: Google sign-in now works from browser, TWA, and APK alike ("так усюди заходить" — user's exact words).** Screenshot showed a real signed-in session (Finance tab, onboarding checklist, "0 записів") rather than the login screen, console showing only the already-known-harmless `.js.map` sourcemap noise — no `auth/internal-error`, no CSP violations. **This closes out the entire Google-sign-in-in-TWA saga** that ran across this whole session: `signInWithPopup` failing silently in TWA/APK (root cause 1: TWAs don't reliably support `window.open()` popups) → `isPopupUnreliableContext()`/`signInWithRedirect` fix (PR #164) → that surfaced `redirect_uri_mismatch` (root cause 2: `authDomain` didn't match the serving origin, and the matching OAuth redirect URI wasn't registered in Google Cloud Console) → revert-then-properly-reapply once the account owner registered the URI (PR #166, #168) → that surfaced `auth/internal-error` on *every* app load regardless of sign-in attempts (root cause 3: `getRedirectResult()` called unconditionally on init, unrelated to the actual redirect flow) → the `GOOGLE_REDIRECT_PENDING_KEY` session-storage guard (PR #170) → that finally isolated the *real* remaining failure to only-after-tapping-Google, which turned out to be root cause 4: CSP blocking `https://apis.google.com/js/api.js` (gapi's loader, needed internally by Google Identity's redirect flow) → PR #172. **Four distinct, independently-necessary root causes, four independent fixes, six real-device round-trips** — worth remembering as a concrete illustration of why "it's still broken" after a plausible-sounding fix doesn't mean the fix was wrong, it can mean the bug was multiple stacked problems that only reveal the next layer once the previous one is actually cleared. **What made this session's back half productive instead of another round of regressions**: switching from "reason about it and guess" to "ask for the actual real-device console output before touching code again" starting with PR #170's investigation — every fix from that point on (PRs #170, #172) was grounded in a specific, directly-observed error rather than a plausible theory, and none of them needed a follow-up revert, unlike the two earlier attempts (PR #164's popup-context fix was fine, but the *first* `authDomain` attempt in that same PR had to be reverted in PR #166 specifically because it was reasoned from Firebase's general best-practices docs rather than confirmed against this project's actual Google Cloud Console state).
- **Cosmetic follow-up: silenced the `.js.map` sourcemap CSP-violation noise entirely** (2026-07-13, same session, right after the fix above was confirmed): user asked what to do about the ~35 remaining `connect-src` violations still showing in DevTools for `firebase-{app,firestore,auth,messaging}.js.map` — already established earlier this session as harmless (DevTools itself fetching sourcemaps to symbolicate stack traces, invisible to users without DevTools open, zero functional impact). Worth fixing anyway, not just explaining away: this exact category of noise is what let the real `apis.google.com` violation hide in plain sight earlier in this same investigation (explicitly called out as a lesson above) — leaving it in place risks the same near-miss next time someone reads a real console log. Fix: added `https://www.gstatic.com` to `connect-src` (it was already trusted in `script-src` for the same files' actual script content, so allowing the sourcemap fetch too doesn't expand what's trusted, just what network requests are permitted for an already-trusted origin). **Verified**: full local suite (all pass) plus the same real-enforcing-CSP-header script re-run with the updated policy — zero violations. - **Follow-up: closed the GitHub Pages exposure flagged in the entry above** (2026-07-13, same session). GitHub Pages ("Deploy from a branch" → `main`/root) runs the repo through Jekyll by default whenever no `.nojekyll` file is present — this repo had neither `.nojekyll` nor a `_config.yml`, so every push to `main` was publishing the repo root essentially as-is to `sudak666.github.io/Maxtr/`, independent of and in addition to whatever `firebase.json` excluded from Firebase Hosting. Confirmed this wasn't theoretical by actually installing Jekyll (4.4.1) in-sandbox and running a real `jekyll build --safe` against the repo with no config: the output contained `CLAUDE.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `AUDIT.md`, `SETUP.md`, `MIGRATION_PLAN_transactions.md`, `firebase.json`, `firestore.rules`, all of `scripts/` and `tests/`, and — the one that matters most — **all of `functions/`, including `functions/index.js`, the actual Cloud Function source**, none of which `firebase.json`'s ignore list has any bearing on since Pages is a completely separate deploy path. **Fix**: added a root `_config.yml` with a Jekyll `exclude:` list mirroring `firebase.json`'s hosting `ignore` set (`*.md`, `docs/`, `scripts/`, `tests/`, `functions/`, `firebase.json`, `firestore.rules`, plus `_config.yml`/`Gemfile*` housekeeping for itself) — deliberately *not* a `.nojekyll` file, since that would disable `exclude:` entirely and revert to publishing everything. Also added `_config.yml` to `firebase.json`'s own ignore list (Pages-specific config, no reason to also ship it to Firebase Hosting). **Verified with a real before/after Jekyll build, not just documented Jekyll behavior**: the "before" build (no config) reproduced the exposure exactly as described above; the "after" build (with `_config.yml`) contained only `index.html`, `js/`, `sw.js`, `manifest.json`, the icons, `landing/`, `landing.html`, `privacy.html`, `terms.html` — and every one of those files `diff`/`cmp`'d byte-for-byte identical between source and build output, confirming Jekyll's well-known behavior of copying front-matter-less files through untouched (so this only changes what gets *published*, not the *content* of what's published — no risk of Jekyll's Liquid templating mangling `index.html`/`js/*.js`). `node tests/unit.mjs` (13/13 pass), `firebase.json` validated as JSON. No `sw.js` bump — no app behavior changed. **Merged and deployed**: PR [#176](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/176), squash-merged as `b7fdcc0` after both CI jobs went green. Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add` off `origin/main` — succeeded on the first attempt, "found 40 files in ." (unchanged from the prior deploy, as expected — `_config.yml` is new but immediately excluded from Hosting too). GitHub Pages itself auto-rebuilds on push to `main` with no agent action needed; there's no MCP/API tool in this toolset for checking the legacy Pages build system's status directly (it isn't a GitHub Actions run), so this session did not independently confirm the Pages rebuild picked up `_config.yml` — the account owner can spot-check `https://sudak666.github.io/Maxtr/CLAUDE.md` (expect a 404) a few minutes after this merge if independent confirmation is wanted, same caveat as the still-unconfirmed Firebase Hosting spot-check from the entry above (this sandbox's egress proxy blocks both `*.web.app` and, presumably, `*.github.io` content fetches the same way).

- **User confirmed the app is pre-launch with no real users yet** (not published to Google Play, no production user base) and asked to fix everything without holding back on backward-compat concerns. Documented as a standing fact in `CLAUDE.md`'s Operating conventions. This directly unblocked the one concrete item flagged but deliberately left alone in an earlier housekeeping entry: the legacy `xamss*`-prefixed localStorage keys. **Renamed** `xamssTheme`/`xamssLang`/`xamssHideAmounts`/`xamssNotif`/`xamssReminderShown`/`xamssRatesSource`/`xamssRatesUpdatedAt`/`xamssBudgetAlert_*`/`xamssRecurAlert_*`/`xamssDebtAlert_*` to `mx<Name>`, across `js/theme-preinit.js`, `js/classic-globals.js`, `js/notifications.js`, `js/settings-managers.js`, and the landing page's own copies (`landing/js/theme-preinit.js`, `landing/js/landing.js` — same origin, shares localStorage, both needed to move together to keep the theme toggle in sync). Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add` off `origin/main` — succeeded on the first attempt, "found 40 files in .", "uploading new files [0/6]" matching the 6 changed JS files.

- **Completed the transactions → Firestore-subcollection migration (audit item 8), added list virtualization, verified CSP, and expanded tests — a four-part task-worker assignment on `claude/transaction-migration-performance-qw907l`.** Investigated each of the four asks before writing code (an Explore agent mapped every read/write touchpoint of `AppState.transactions` across `js/*.js`) rather than assuming the existing `MIGRATION_PLAN_transactions.md` plan still applied as written.
  - **Transactions migration — done as a direct cutover, not the plan's original dual-write/dual-read rollout.** That plan (see the file itself, now updated) was written to protect a live user base through a slow, cautious rollout; since the app is confirmed pre-launch with no real users (see the Operating conventions entry above), the phased approach's whole rationale no longer applied, so this session went straight to a clean cutover instead: `users/{uid}/max_tracker/{financeDoc}/transactions/{txId}` (txId = the existing `Date.now()`-based numeric id, stringified) is now the sole persistence path for transactions. All 6 real mutation call sites found by the Explore agent (`addTransaction`/`deleteTransaction`/`deleteTag` in `js/finance.js`, `renameCategory` in `js/settings-managers.js`, `processRecurring` and the migration step itself in `js/color-picker.js`) now write directly to the transaction's own subcollection doc via new helpers in `js/firebase-sync.js` (`saveTransactionDoc`/`deleteTransactionDoc`/`batchWriteTransactions`/`batchDeleteTransactionsByIds`/`loadTransactionsFromSubcollection`/`deleteAllTransactionDocs`) instead of `scheduleSave()`'s whole-`finance`-doc rewrite — a single transaction edit no longer rewrites the entire transaction history plus every other finance field on every save, which was the actual problem statement (1 MiB doc-size risk, doc-level-not-field-level optimistic concurrency, slow initial load). `fbLoadNow()` does a one-time client-side migration per account/profile (copies `finance.data` into the subcollection the first time it finds the subcollection empty but the legacy array non-empty, then sets a `txMigrated` flag mirroring the existing `catBackfillDone`/`catLegacyMerged` pattern — guards against a later load, after every transaction has since been deleted, re-migrating the stale array back in). `fbSaveNow()` no longer writes a `data` field onto the `finance` doc at all — it's dropped automatically since every finance-doc write already used `{merge:false}`. `firestore.rules` got a new sibling `match` block for the subcollection (owner-only, scoped to a `finance`/`finance@<profileId>` parent, shallow field validation matching the existing doc-level rule's style). `functions/lib/sweep.js`'s `sweepProfile()`/`sweepToken()` now fetch the subcollection via the Admin SDK in parallel with the finance/debt doc reads they already did, falling back to `finance.data` only when the subcollection is empty (pre-migration account, or a race with a client that hasn't loaded yet) — kept as an optional trailing parameter specifically so every pre-existing `functions-sweep.mjs` test kept passing unmodified. `deleteAccountUser()` (`js/auth.js`) now also deletes every doc in the subcollection, since Firestore never cascade-deletes a subcollection when its parent doc is deleted (would otherwise leave the subcollection orphaned). `scripts/backfill-transactions.mjs` (the plan's original operator script) is left in place but now optional/superseded — the client does the same copy automatically. `CLAUDE.md`'s Firebase data model section, `AUDIT.md`'s item 8, and `MIGRATION_PLAN_transactions.md` itself all updated to reflect this as done.
  - **List virtualization — CSS `content-visibility`/`contain-intrinsic-size`, not a JS windowing library.** The task explicitly allowed either a virtual-scroller or CSS containment; chose containment given this repo's deliberate no-bundler architecture (no framework to hang a windowing library's DOM-recycling off of, and `renderFinance()`'s already-existing collapsed/"view all" toggle in `js/analytics-csv.js` means the only real risk is the *expanded* view, where a heavy account's full history renders as one unbounded `innerHTML`-then-`appendChild` pass). Added `content-visibility:auto; contain-intrinsic-size:auto 84px;` to `.tx-item` in `index.html` — skips layout/paint for off-screen rows without changing the render function itself at all; unsupported browsers just ignore both properties (pure progressive enhancement, and the Android/TWA target is Chromium-based anyway, where support has existed since Chrome 85).
  - **CSP — already fully enforcing, nothing left to do.** Checked `firebase.json` directly before assuming the task's phrasing ("script-src self + hashes for classic scripts") described the current state: the header key is already the real enforcing `Content-Security-Policy`, not `-Report-Only` (flipped over several sessions documented earlier in this file — the apis.google.com/Google-Sign-In saga). `script-src` is `'self' https://www.gstatic.com https://apis.google.com` with no `'unsafe-inline'`; all four classic (non-module) scripts were already externalized to same-origin files in an earlier session specifically *instead of* using hashes, since a hash has to be hand-recomputed on every future edit to that script — a maintenance trap this repo deliberately avoided (see that session's own entry above). Confirmed zero remaining inline `onclick=`/`<script>` blocks in `index.html`. Found and fixed one stale comment in `js/core.js`'s `securitypolicyviolation` listener that still described the policy as report-only from before it was flipped — updated to match reality. No functional change needed.
  - **Testing expanded**: `tests/firestore-rules.mjs` got 9 new cases against a real local Firestore emulator for the new transactions-subcollection rule (owner write/delete, cross-user denied, unauthenticated denied, missing/wrong-typed required fields denied, wrong-parent-doc denied) — ran manually against `firebase-tools emulators:start --only firestore` per the file's own documented recipe, all 35 cases (26 existing + 9 new) passed. `tests/functions-sweep.mjs`'s fake `db` got a `.collection(path).get()` implementation (backed by the same path-keyed Map, storing a plain array of tx objects) plus 4 new cases (subcollection preferred over stale legacy data, budget sum reads from the subcollection, empty subcollection falls back to legacy data, and one `sweepToken`-level end-to-end case) — all pre-existing cases kept passing unmodified since an unpopulated collection path just falls back to the old behavior. `tests/smoke.mjs`/`tests/e2e-crud.mjs`/`tests/e2e-modals.mjs`'s hand-written Firestore stubs were upgraded from inert no-ops to a real (if minimal) path-keyed in-memory store supporting `collection`/`getDocs`/`writeBatch` (required simply for the module import to succeed once `js/core.js` imports those — a missing export blanks the whole page per this repo's own documented gotcha — but also makes `tests/e2e-crud.mjs`'s create/edit/delete assertions genuinely exercise the new subcollection write path instead of writing into a stub that silently discarded everything). Added a new **`tests/stress-tx-list.mjs`**, wired into CI (`.github/workflows/smoke-test.yml`): seeds 400 transaction docs directly into the stubbed subcollection before page load, drives the real "view all" expand flow, and asserts every row renders (proves virtualization doesn't silently under-render — `content-visibility` is layout/paint-only, it doesn't reduce the DOM node count), that `content-visibility:auto` is actually live on a rendered row (not just present unparsed in the stylesheet), and that nothing errors — this is the only test exercising either the migration or the virtualization at any real scale (`e2e-crud.mjs` only ever has one transaction). `CLAUDE.md`'s Commands section updated with entries for `e2e-modals.mjs` (previously undocumented) and the new stress test, plus a stale "two persisted automated checks" claim fixed to match the now-larger suite.
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v37→v38 — multiple `js/*.js` files' behavior changed substantively (the persistence layer, not markup-dependent wiring this time, but the standing rule from the earlier stale-cache incident is to bump on any real `js/*.js` behavior change rather than judge case-by-case).
  - **Verified**: full local suite — `tests/unit.mjs` (13/13), `tests/functions-sweep.mjs` (22/22, up from 18), `tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs` (now exercising the real subcollection write path), `tests/e2e-modals.mjs`, `tests/stress-tx-list.mjs` (new), `tests/firestore-rules.mjs` against a real local emulator (35/35, up from 26), and `node --check functions/index.js` — all pass. - **Optimized `renderFinance()`'s transaction list to a targeted DOM update instead of a full rebuild** — a follow-up performance item from the same round of asks that prompted the transactions-subcollection migration/virtualization/CSP-verification work above (user pasted a task table asking specifically for "targeted updates" via `data-id` in the Finance tab, distinct from the transactions-migration item). `renderFinance()` (`js/analytics-csv.js`) is called from ~20 places across `js/*.js`, many unrelated to any specific transaction (a wallet rename, a budget edit, switching tabs back) — it used to unconditionally `lc.innerHTML=''` and rebuild every visible `.tx-item` from scratch on every single call, which was both wasteful and visibly replayed the row's CSS entrance animation on every unrelated re-render. Reworked to match existing `.tx-item` nodes by `data-id` (`dataset.txId`) against the new `visible` list: a matched row's content is still fully regenerated (via a new `txItemInnerHtml()` helper extracted from the old inline template, so nothing risks showing stale wallet/tag/category data), but the *outer element itself* is reused — keeping its click/keydown listeners bound without re-registration and, since CSS `animation` doesn't restart on innerHTML/attribute mutation of an already-connected node, not replaying the pop-in animation. Only genuinely new transactions get a freshly-created node (and therefore the animation, which is the more correct UX — an actual new transaction should visibly appear, an unrelated re-render shouldn't make the whole list flicker); existing nodes are repositioned via `insertBefore` if their order changed; nodes for transactions no longer in `visible` are removed. **One real bug caught before it shipped**: transitioning from the empty-state (`emptyStateHtml()`) or cold-start skeleton (`renderFinanceSkeleton()`) markup would have left that non-`.tx-item` content sitting in `#tx-list-container` forever, since the diff only ever looked for `.tx-item`/`.tx-view-all-btn` children — caught by writing the dedicated test below before assuming the implementation was correct, not by manual inspection; fixed with an explicit `:not(.tx-item):not(.tx-view-all-btn)` cleanup pass before the diff runs each time. Added `tests/tx-list-targeted-update.mjs` (wired into CI): tags each row's *outer* DOM element with a custom attribute (which only survives on a reused node — `item.innerHTML=...` only replaces children, never the element's own attributes — so this proves node identity, not just matching content) and confirms it survives an unrelated re-render (clicking the already-active filter chip), an add (new node appears, existing ones untouched), and a delete (only the deleted row's node disappears). `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v38→v39 (`js/analytics-csv.js` behavior changed). **Verified**: full local suite — `tests/unit.mjs`, `tests/functions-sweep.mjs`, `tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs` (exercises the empty→populated transition, incidentally covering the cleanup-pass fix above), `tests/e2e-modals.mjs`, `tests/stress-tx-list.mjs`, and the new `tests/tx-list-targeted-update.mjs` — all pass. `CLAUDE.md`'s Firebase data model and Commands sections updated with a description of the new render pattern and test. Not yet merged/deployed as of this entry.

- **Accessibility pass: touch targets, font sizes/contrast, skeleton loading states, modal focus management, CSP re-verification** — another pasted task table, this time with a "Хто" (who) column marking most items as the account owner's own work and only "touch targets" as shared; asked to clarify scope via `AskUserQuestion`, the owner chose to have all 5 done this session anyway. Investigated each with an Explore agent before writing any code, which paid off twice: **modal focus management (item 4) turned out to already be fully implemented** (`setupModalAccessibility()` in `js/settings-managers.js`, undocumented in `CLAUDE.md` until this entry — focus trap, Escape-to-close, and focus-restore for all 23 `.modal-overlay`s via a generic `MutationObserver`, not per-modal wiring), so no code was needed there, just live verification (see below) and a documentation fix; and **CSP (item 5) was also already fully enforcing** with zero inline `<script>`/`onclick=` remaining (re-confirmed by direct grep, no code change needed — matches this file's earlier CSP-verification entry from the same day).
  - **Touch targets**: `.filter-chip`/`.settings-group-chip`/`.debt-chip`/`.debt-chip-add-labeled`/`.subcat-toggle` (~25-32px before) bumped to comfortably clear 44px via real padding increases, not a hit-slop pseudo-element trick — these sit in tightly `gap`-packed flex-wrap rows where an invisible extended hit area risks bleeding into a neighboring chip's own hit area. `.mgr-color` 34×34→44×44. `.mgr-del`/`.mgr-edit`/`.debt-chip-del` (already exactly 44px) got a few more px for safety margin. Deliberately scoped to what was literally asked ("усіх іконок видалення/редагування/чіпів") — left `.subchip button` (~17px, hardest to fix without a layout change), `.drag-handle`, several small non-chip buttons, and the already-known `.tab-icon-wrap` (documented separately under Mobile UI redesign) as explicitly out of scope, not silently missed.
  - **Font sizes + `--muted2` contrast**: computed `--muted2`'s actual WCAG contrast ratio by hand (relative-luminance formula, not eyeballed) — dark theme `#68676e` measured ~2.5-3.0:1, light theme `#75757b` measured ~4.1:1, both under the 4.5:1 AA floor for normal text. Replaced with `#98979e` (dark) / `#626269` (light), both verified ≥4.5:1 against `--bg`/`--bg1`/`--bg2`. `.tx-meta`/`.wallet-tag` (transaction row date/comment and wallet/tag badges — the two most-frequently-read 11px instances) bumped to 12px, paired with the chip font-size bumps above (13px, since padding was being touched anyway). Did **not** attempt a sweeping bump of the ~30 other sub-13px selectors the audit found (calendar `.wday`/`.day-num`, chart labels, stat/hero micro-labels, etc.) — this repo already has a documented precedent (see the "Decluttered the Finance tab" entry) for declining exactly this tradeoff (system-wide font bump = large blast radius across carefully-fitted compact layouts, for marginal gain over a scoped fix), and nothing here overrides that reasoning for the untouched selectors.
  - **Skeleton loading states**: `js/calendar.js` gained `renderShiftsSkeleton()` (mirrors `renderFinanceSkeleton()` in `js/analytics-csv.js` exactly — same cold-start `if(!cfgCached)` call site in `js/app-init.js`'s `init()`), filling `#calendar-grid` with shimmer blocks and hiding `#calendar-empty-state`. Root cause this fixes: the Shifts tab isn't rendered at cold start the way Finance is (`init()` only calls `switchTab('finance')`), so a user tapping the Shifts nav tab before the first `fbLoadNow()` resolves would see the "no shifts logged yet" empty state instead of a loading indicator — misleadingly implying no data exists rather than that it's still loading.
  - **Modal focus management**: verified live rather than trusting the static-code read — extended `tests/e2e-modals.mjs` with real assertions (opening a modal moves focus inside the card; Escape closes the topmost modal; focus returns to the triggering element; Tab from the last focusable element wraps to the first) against the *existing* `setupModalAccessibility()` implementation. All passed on the first run, confirming it already worked correctly; promoted it from undocumented to a real `CLAUDE.md` UI-conventions entry so the next session doesn't have to rediscover it.
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v39→v40 (`js/calendar.js`/`js/app-init.js` behavior changed, plus the CSS/font changes in `index.html`).
  - **Verified**: full local suite — `tests/unit.mjs`, `tests/functions-sweep.mjs`, `tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs`, `tests/e2e-modals.mjs` (4 new assertions), `tests/stress-tx-list.mjs`, `tests/tx-list-targeted-update.mjs`, `node --check functions/index.js` — all pass. Also took a set of Playwright screenshots (Finance/Debt/Settings/Wallets-manager/Shifts, dark + light) as a one-off manual visual sanity check for the chip/button size and font changes — no overflow or layout breakage observed; not committed (matches this repo's established one-off-verification-script convention). Not yet merged/deployed as of this entry.

- **"ФАЗА 3: UI/UX Поліпшення" — a third task-worker-style ask this session (Finance-tab redesign completion, manager-design unification, pull-to-refresh, empty-state illustrations, themed push icons).** Investigated each item's actual current status first (another Explore agent pass) rather than assuming the pasted task list described a from-scratch state — found the Finance redesign and empty-state infrastructure were already ~80-95% done from earlier sessions, so this pass only needed to close specific real gaps, not rebuild from zero. User chose to do all 5 items, and explicitly chose to add illustrations to empty states despite the tension with this app's existing no-emoji/monochrome-icon-only convention — resolved by staying inside that convention's spirit rather than breaking it (see below).
  - **Finance-tab redesign completion**: `#finance-chart-section` (the 6-month balance/income/expense line chart) moved from the main Finance scroll into `#tools-modal`, alongside the analytics/rates/converter sections that moved there in an earlier session — the Finance tab's main scroll is now genuinely just balance+quick-actions+transaction-list+FAB+goals(if any)+budgets(if any). `chart` removed from `WIDGET_ORDER_DEFAULT`/`WIDGET_SECTION_IDS`/`WIDGET_DEFS` (now just `['goals']`) — `applyWidgetVisibility()` simplified accordingly, since `renderGoals()` already handled its own show/hide internally and the loop was dead code once `chart` left. `renderFinanceChart()` needed no changes at all — it already runs unconditionally on every Finance-tab switch regardless of the chart section's DOM location. `TX_LIST_COLLAPSED_COUNT` bumped 3→5 (`js/analytics-csv.js`) to match "last 5 operations" from the task list.
  - **Manager design unification**: auto-rules and recurring managers were the two remaining holdouts still using the pre-redesign `.debt-row` always-expanded stacked-fields layout — converted both to the same collapsed-summary-row-with-pencil-toggle-to-expand pattern the shift-types/categories managers already used (new `AppState.expandedRuleId`/`.expandedRecurringId`, mirroring `expandedShiftTypeId`). **Found and fixed a real pre-existing bug via live screenshot verification, not code reading**: `.mgr-num` (shared by shift-types' Pay/Hours fields too) was `flex:1 1 90px;width:90px` — nested inside a column-flex `.mgr-field`, `flex-basis:90px` applies to the *vertical* axis there, silently making every such input 90px tall as well as wide (rendered as a solid near-black square, no visible text). Fixed by dropping the `flex` shorthand (plain `width:90px` was always sufficient) — this also silently fixed the same latent bug in the already-shipped shift-types manager.
  - **Pull-to-refresh**: didn't exist at all before this (confirmed via a repo-wide grep) — added `setupPullToRefresh()` (`js/app-init.js`), gated on `scrollTop===0` and no open modal, using damped 1:1 finger tracking (`translateY`, ×0.5, capped at 100px) on a new fixed `#ptr-indicator` spinner, triggering the *same* `fbLoadNow()`+toast flow the topbar's `#btn-refresh` button already used past a 70px threshold. Relies on `body{overscroll-behavior-y:contain}` (new) to suppress the browser/OS's own native pull-to-refresh bounce, which is what lets this use passive (non-`preventDefault`-ing) touch listeners with no scroll-jank cost. New `tests/pull-to-refresh.mjs` dispatches synthetic `TouchEvent`s (Playwright has no built-in touch-drag API) to verify all three cases (short pull snaps back, long pull actually refreshes, pulling mid-scroll does nothing) — genuinely exercises the real gesture code, not a mocked stand-in.
  - **Empty-state illustrations**: `emptyStateHtml()` (`js/ui-widgets.js`) now wraps the existing monochrome icon in a larger (112px) soft-glow circle plus 3 floating accent-dot "sparks", instead of a plain 48px icon badge — built entirely from the app's own icon set/palette (no emoji, no external artwork), the resolution chosen for the tension between "add illustrations" and the standing no-illustration-artwork convention. Whole block gets a `prefers-reduced-motion`-aware fade-in+pop entrance animation. All 5 existing call sites (Finance, Shifts, Debt ×2, Shopping) picked this up with no changes needed.
  - **Themed push-notification icons**: `functions/index.js`'s `sendPush()` gained a 4th `type` parameter (`'daily'|'budget'|'recurring'|'debt'`), looked up in a new `NOTIF_ICONS` map to set `webpush.notification.icon`; `functions/lib/sweep.js`'s 4 call sites each pass their own type. `sw.js`'s `onBackgroundMessage` handler reads `payload.notification.icon` instead of hardcoding `icon-192.png`. Generated 4 new icon PNGs (`notif-icon-{daily,budget,recurring,debt}.png`, repo root) with Pillow (installed into this sandbox for the purpose) — purple-gradient rounded-square background matching `icon-192.png`'s existing branding, simple white glyph (bell/warning-triangle/repeat-circle/bank) per type, hand-drawn via Pillow primitives at 4× supersampling for anti-aliasing rather than reusing the SVG `ICON_PATHS` set, since notification icons need static image URLs. Added to `sw.js`'s `STATIC_ASSETS` precache list. `tests/functions-sweep.mjs` got 4 new assertions (one per push type) verifying the correct `type` string reaches `sendPushFn`; the display side (`sw.js`) has no automated coverage — needs a real FCM background-message delivery this repo's stubbed-Firebase Playwright recipe can't simulate, so verify manually on a real device if this needs re-checking.
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v40→v41 (`js/*.js` behavior changed, plus 4 new same-origin icon assets to precache).
  - **Verified**: full local suite — `tests/unit.mjs`, `tests/functions-sweep.mjs` (26/26, up from 22), `tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs`, `tests/e2e-modals.mjs`, `tests/stress-tx-list.mjs` (now asserting 5, not 3, collapsed rows), `tests/tx-list-targeted-update.mjs`, and the new `tests/pull-to-refresh.mjs` — all pass. Plus a round of one-off Playwright screenshot verification (not committed) that caught the `.mgr-num` bug above before it shipped, and confirmed the moved chart section renders correctly inside `#tools-modal`, the new empty-state illustrations look right in both light/dark, and the new auto-rules/recurring manager rows render correctly collapsed and expanded. `CLAUDE.md` updated across the Finance-tab-widgets, Mobile-UI-redesign, and Notifications sections. - **UI/gesture punch-list pass** (2026-07-15, `claude/ui-improvements-gestures-q6gkba`), a 10-item list handed over verbatim by the account owner. Committed/pushed to that branch, not merged (this session ran as a branch-develop task, not the usual PR-created-and-merged-by-agent flow) — see the pushed commit for the exact diff.
  - **Auth-screen flash on every page refresh**: `#lock-screen` was `display:flex` with the full sign-in form visible by default in the raw HTML, only hidden once Firebase Auth's `onAuthStateChanged` resolved (an async IndexedDB-backed persisted-session check) — so an already-logged-in user briefly saw the email/password form flash on every refresh before it got hidden. Fixed by starting the element with a new `lock-screen-checking` class (CSS hides `.auth-card` + the lang-toggle row and shows a small branded spinner instead while it's present) and having `js/auth.js`'s `onAuthStateChanged` handler remove that class on its very first callback, whichever way it resolves. Verified structurally (the class is present in the raw served HTML, before any JS runs) rather than by racing a live timing window, since the stubbed test auth resolves via a same-tick microtask — much faster than real Firebase Auth, so there's no observable "checking" window to catch in that harness.
  - **Bottom nav decluttering**: removed `#nav-settings` from the 5-tab bottom pill nav (now 4: Фінанси/Графік змін/Розрахунки/Покупки) and added an explicit gear button (`#btn-settings`) to `.topbar-right` that calls the same `switchTab('settings')`. `js/app-init.js`'s `switchTab()` and nav click-wiring updated for the removed element; `js/core.js`'s `currentTabName()` (used only for error-log tagging) no longer depends on any `#nav-*.active` element existing — now reads the visible `.tab-content` directly, which is more robust anyway. Freed-up per-tab width used to bump `.tab-icon-wrap` 42px→48px (38px→44px under the 600px breakpoint) and its icon 20px→23px.
  - **Icons enlarged app-wide**: base `.btn .ico` 16px→18px (topbar buttons etc.), `.quick-action-icon` circle 52px→56px (icon 24px→26px), `.mgr-edit`/`.mgr-del` icon glyph 16px→19px, `.debt-row-edit`/`.debt-row-del` 15px→18px, `.debt-chip-del` 14px→17px, and the Finance transaction list's pencil/trash (`.tx-del`) 19px→22px. The `.tx-actions` gap between the adjacent pencil and trash buttons was also bumped 2px→10px — this is the actual fix for "неможливо видалити операцію зарахування коштів (натискаю кошик, відкриває редагувати)": traced with a real reproduction script (stubbed-Firebase Playwright, explicit income-type transaction, programmatic click on the trash button) and the delete flow itself works correctly and always did — the two 45px-tall buttons sat only 2px apart, an easy real-thumb mis-tap onto the adjacent pencil button, not a logic bug. No code path was actually broken.
  - **Settings-row chevrons removed**: all 17 `<span class="settings-row-chevron">` (the rotated `>` glyphs) removed from `index.html`'s Settings tab — every row already opens its manager modal via a `data-action` on the *entire* row (`cursor:pointer`), so the chevron was purely decorative and implied a second tap was needed when it never was. Dead `.settings-row-chevron` CSS rule and the `classic-globals.js` icon-setting loop for it removed too.
  - **"Налаштувати екран" ghost button removed** from the top of the Finance tab (it opened the same widgets-manager modal as Settings → Віджети — pure duplication of an existing entry point, not a new one added elsewhere).
  - **Курси валют de-duplicated**: removed the standalone "Курси" quick-action button from the Finance tab (it opened the rates manager directly) since the exact same rates widget already lives inside "Інструменти" (`#tools-modal`'s `fx-widget-section`), and Settings → Курси валют remains as the one settings-level entry point. Three entry points down to two, both intentional.
  - **Swipe-down-to-close gesture**: turned out to already be implemented (`js/ui-widgets.js`'s `initSheetDrag()`, wired to every `.modal-overlay` except `#shift-modal` at settings-managers.js's init) but scoped only to the 36×4px `.sheet-grabber` handle bar — technically present but too small a target to reliably grab on a real phone, which is why "I open Інструменти and can't just swipe it down" was a real complaint despite the mechanism existing. Extended `initSheetDrag()` to also bind the same drag/dismiss behavior to `.modal-header` (the title bar right below the grabber, which was already `cursor:grab`-styled in a stale comment describing this as already-implemented behavior it wasn't) — a much bigger, easier-to-hit swipe zone, still never touching `.modal-card-body` so it can't fight the body's own scroll. Verified with directly-dispatched `PointerEvent`s (Playwright's coordinate-based `page.mouse` drag proved unreliable for hitting the exact header target in-test; the app itself listens for real `PointerEvent`s regardless of input source, so this is a faithful reproduction) — dragging the Tools-modal header down past the threshold now closes it.
  - **Budget amounts now respect "Сховати суми" + gained a pencil-to-edit toggle**: `renderBudgetsManagerList()` (`js/settings-managers.js`) previously rendered every category's limit as an always-visible, always-editable raw `<input type=number">` — the one amount in the whole app *not* covered by the `body.amounts-hidden` privacy toggle, since a live input can't be blurred. Converted to the same compact-row pattern already used by auto-rules/recurring (icon badge + `.cat-row-body` summary line showing the masked limit as text, or "Без ліміту"/"No limit" — new `budgets_no_limit` i18n key — plus a `.mgr-edit` pencil that toggles a `AppState.expandedBudgetCat`-gated inline input, mirroring `expandedRecurringId`). `.budget-row-limit` added to the `body.amounts-hidden` blur-selector list. `updateBudget()` deliberately still doesn't re-render its own list on every keystroke (same reason `updateWallet`/`updateRecurring` don't — `FIELD_ACTIONS` fires on both `input` and `change`, so re-rendering on `input` would tear down the focused element mid-type).
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v41→v42 (every `js/*.js` file above changed, plus `index.html`'s CSS/markup).
  - **Verified**: `node --check` on every touched `js/*.js` + `functions/index.js`, full local suite (`tests/unit.mjs`, `tests/functions-sweep.mjs`, `tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs`, `tests/e2e-modals.mjs`, `tests/stress-tx-list.mjs`, `tests/tx-list-targeted-update.mjs`, `tests/pull-to-refresh.mjs`) — all pass. `tests/smoke.mjs` and `tests/e2e-modals.mjs` updated for the removed `#nav-settings` (now drive Settings via `#btn-settings`). Plus a one-off Playwright verification script (not committed, matching this repo's established convention) covering everything not already in the persisted suite: raw-HTML lock-screen-checking presence, 4-tab nav count, `#btn-settings` opening Settings, zero remaining chevrons, zero standalone rates quick-actions, budget-row pencil-reveals-input + amounts-hidden masking, and the Tools-modal header swipe-close — all passed. Not merged into `main`; pushed to `claude/ui-improvements-gestures-q6gkba` only, per this session's branch-develop instructions.

- **Follow-up fix on PR [#188](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/188): a stale-service-worker split-state bug the Codex review bot (P1) caught, missed by this session's own testing** (2026-07-15, same branch). `sw.js` serves `js/*.js` cache-first but `index.html` network-first (see Layout above), so right after this PR deploys, any client whose service worker hasn't updated yet (an already-open tab, or any returning visitor whose old SW is still "activated" and controlling the page — i.e. basically everyone who'd used the app before this deploy) can load the fresh `index.html` from this PR while still serving *old cached* `js/app-init.js`/`js/auth.js` for a real, non-trivial window (until the new SW installs, activates, and `clients.claim()`s — a multi-file `cache.addAll()` that takes real time, not instant). Confirmed two concrete symptoms, not just a theoretical race, by literally re-serving the pre-PR (`823b8f5`) `app-init.js`/`auth.js` alongside the new `index.html` in a Playwright repro:
  - **Signed-in users**: old `app-init.js`'s unguarded `document.getElementById('nav-settings').classList.toggle(...)` inside `switchTab()` (this PR removed `#nav-settings` from the DOM entirely) throws a `TypeError`, aborting `init()` partway through — `fbLoadNow()` and everything after it in `init()` never runs, so the user's real data silently never loads even though the lock-screen already hid successfully (that happens earlier, before `init()`).
  - **Signed-out users**: old `auth.js` has never heard of the new `lock-screen-checking` class this PR added and never removes it, so the CSS rule hiding `.auth-card` while "checking" stays in effect forever — the user sees only the brand+spinner splash with no way to actually reach the sign-in form, until they happen to hard-refresh again later (once the new SW has taken over).
  - **Fix 1 (crash)**: `#nav-settings` kept in the DOM (`index.html`) instead of deleted — now `style="display:none" tabindex="-1" aria-hidden="true"`, inert and invisible, purely so old cached JS's `getElementById` calls keep finding a real (harmless) element instead of `null`. `#btn-settings` in the topbar remains the one real, reachable entry point; nothing about the intended UX changed.
  - **Fix 2 (stuck spinner)**: a pure-CSS force-reveal safety net on the `lock-screen-checking` hide rule — after a 4s delay, `.auth-card`/the lang-toggle row become visible regardless of whether any JS ever removed the class, so a signed-out user on stale JS is unblocked within a few seconds instead of indefinitely. No JS involved deliberately: `js/*.js` is exactly the stale layer that can't be trusted to have this fix yet, but CSS embedded directly in `index.html` is always fresh (network-first document). **Hit and fixed a genuine CSS gotcha getting this to actually work**: a `display:none` declared as a *separate static property* alongside a delayed `animation:...forwards` whose keyframes only define `to{display:block}` never fires at all (`animationend` never even dispatches) — confirmed by an isolated repro, not assumed. The working pattern needs `display` to be part of the animation's own keyframes from `from{}` through `to{}`, with `animation-fill-mode:both` (not `forwards`) so the `from` value governs during the delay — verified both the broken and working variants directly in this sandbox's actual Chromium 141 before trusting either one.
  - Also fixed **`js/core.js`'s `currentTabName()`** (used only for error-log tagging) in the original PR to read the visible `.tab-content` directly rather than any `#nav-*.active` element, specifically so it wouldn't have this same class of dependency on `#nav-settings` existing — no changes needed there for this follow-up.
  - **Verified**: a new throwaway Playwright regression script (not committed) that serves the real new `index.html` but intercepts `js/app-init.js`/`js/auth.js` requests with the actual pre-PR (`823b8f5`) file contents fetched via `git show` — reproduces the split-state exactly rather than guessing, confirms the old crash no longer happens for a signed-in user and the CSS safety net actually reveals the sign-in form ~4s in for a signed-out one. Full persisted suite (`tests/unit.mjs`, `tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs`, `tests/e2e-modals.mjs`) re-run and still green.
