Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add` off `origin/main` — succeeded on the first attempt, "found 46 files in .", "uploading new files [0/9]" (matches this PR's 12 changed files). No `functions/`/`firestore.rules` changes in this PR, nothing else to redeploy. GitHub Pages auto-deploys on push to `main`. **Standing authorization reaffirmed by the account owner this session, explicitly**: merge and deploy autonomously once checks pass, for both this kind of PWA change and any future one — no need to ask each time. Also reconfirmed the standing exception stays in force: this does *not* extend to `claude/native-applications-638ap0` (native Android), which stays unmerged regardless of any CI until a real local build succeeds (see that branch's dedicated entries above) — the two are separate, deliberately different gates. Logged in a tiny follow-up, PR [#189](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/189), squash-merged as `7ef37bb`.

- **Post-merge branch cleanup attempted, partially blocked — new standing convention + a real environment limitation, both now recorded in `CLAUDE.md`.** The account owner asked, after the #188/#189 merges above, to always clean up merged branches "so audits don't complain." Deleted the two local branches (`claude/ui-improvements-gestures-q6gkba`, `claude/log-pr188-outcome`) and the scratch `git worktree` used for the hosting deploy without issue. **Remote deletion failed**: `git push origin --delete <branch>` 403'd (`RPC failed; HTTP 403`) for both branches — this sandbox's git remote is routed through a local proxy (`http://local_proxy@127.0.0.1:.../git/sudak666/Maxtr`, not raw `github.com`), and ref deletion specifically is blocked there even though ordinary pushes work; the GitHub MCP server available in this session has no `delete_branch`/`delete_ref` method either (checked — only `create_branch` exists). Confirmed via `list_branches` that both branches are still present on GitHub, and that "Automatically delete head branches" is not enabled for this repo (neither PR's branch was auto-removed on merge). **This means remote branch deletion cannot currently be done from an agent session in this repo at all** — recorded as a known limitation in `CLAUDE.md`'s Operating conventions, with the real fix (flip that one repo setting) flagged to the account owner as a to-do. Also surfaced, while checking: a pre-existing backlog of ~50+ stale branches from many earlier sessions (`claude/app-design-review-yqcj0o`, `log-mini-stats`, `window-onclick-phase4-color-picker`, etc.) that were never cleaned up for the same underlying reason — flagged as a one-time manual GitHub-UI sweep for the account owner, not something to attempt piecemeal from here given the number and the same deletion limitation.
  - **Logged in a tiny follow-up, PR [#190](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/190), squash-merged as `6a65263`.** Local branch for that PR cleaned up the same way (`git branch -D`); remote deletion attempted again for completeness and 403'd again, exactly as expected/documented above — not a new finding, just confirming the limitation is consistent.

- **"Automatically delete head branches" enabled by the account owner, same day, right after the above.** Closes the actual gap — GitHub now deletes a PR's branch itself on merge, so the remote-deletion limitation above no longer needs any agent-side workaround or repeated flagging going forward. `CLAUDE.md`'s Operating conventions updated to reflect this as resolved rather than outstanding. The pre-existing ~50-branch backlog (all predating this setting) is unaffected and still needs its own one-time manual sweep whenever the account owner gets to it.

- **Two real bugs from a user-submitted screenshot pair, both fixed and verified — plus a chunk of generic/off-stack UI advice pasted alongside them deliberately not acted on.** The account owner shared two phone screenshots: an Android notification shade showing two textually-identical "Zminka — Не забудь записати сьогоднішні операції" pushes at once, and the Розрахунки (Debt) tab's payment-history list with several cards showing an empty value under the "ДАТА" label. A large block of external AI-generated recommendations came with the screenshots (React/`lucide-react`, OneSignal, Vercel-style branding advice) — none of that applies to this repo's actual stack (vanilla JS, Firebase Cloud Messaging, no bundler), so it was explicitly not followed; only the two concrete, screenshot-backed observations were investigated against the real code.
  - **Duplicate daily-reminder push, root-caused and confirmed with the account owner before fixing**: `functions/lib/sweep.js`'s `sweepToken()` sweeps every profile on an account independently (see CLAUDE.md's Multiple-profiles section), and the daily reminder's push text (`'Не забудь записати сьогоднішні операції.'`) never varied by profile — so an account with 2+ profiles enabled on the *same device* (confirmed via `AskUserQuestion`: this account has exactly that) gets one push per profile, all identical, landing in the notification shade as what reads like a broken duplicate rather than two distinct reminders. Budget/recurring/debt-due pushes don't have this problem — their text already names a specific category/amount/debt, so two profiles triggering those still produce visually distinct pushes — so only the daily reminder needed consolidating.
    - **Fix**: new `dailyReminderNeeded(financeSnap, transactionsSnap, prevState, now)` pure helper in `sweep.js` — determines whether a profile's daily reminder should fire *without* sending anything, factored out so `sweepToken()`'s new pre-pass and `sweepProfile()`'s own per-profile step 1 always agree on what "needed" means (one shared implementation, not two that could quietly drift apart). `sweepToken()` now runs this pre-pass across every profile on the token first, and if 2+ profiles need it, sends **one** consolidated push naming each profile (e.g. "Не забудь записати сьогоднішні операції: Я, Дружина.", using each profile's `profiles_meta` name — falls back to the original generic text if any name is missing, or if only one profile needs it, so single-profile accounts — the overwhelming majority — see zero behavior change). `sweepProfile()` gained a trailing `skipDaily` parameter (default `false`, so every existing direct call — including every pre-existing test — is unaffected) that `sweepToken()` sets for any profile already covered by the consolidated push, so its own per-profile step 1 doesn't re-send. A non-fatal send failure marks nothing sent for any profile (consistent with how every other check in this file already handles a failed send — next hour's sweep just retries).
    - **Verified**: 2 new `tests/functions-sweep.mjs` tests (28 total, up from 26) — one confirms exactly one push fires and names both profiles when both are due on the same device, one confirms the generic-text fallback when a profile has no `profiles_meta` name to list. All 26 pre-existing tests still pass unmodified, including the one exercising a *different* 2-profile scenario (only one of the two actually due) that predates this fix and would have caught an accidental regression to single-profile-only sweeping.
  - **Empty debt-payment-history dates**: `js/debt.js`'s read-only entry row rendered `entry.date` directly (`escapeHtml(entry.date??'')`) — for entries where `date` is a genuinely empty string (not `null`/`undefined`, so the `??` fallback never engaged), this left nothing visible under the "ДАТА" label, exactly matching the screenshot. `addDebtEntry()` already defaults new entries' date to `todayLabel()` when the field is left blank, so this only affects older entries predating that fallback (or entries added via some other path) — a display-only fix, not a data backfill. Changed to `entry.date?escapeHtml(entry.date):'—'` — a dash placeholder instead of blank, matching how every other "no value" spot in this app is shown. Verified with a throwaway Playwright script (not committed) that seeds one entry with a real date and one with `date:''` directly into `AppState` and calls `renderDebt()`, confirming the real date still renders unchanged and the empty one now shows exactly one "—".
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v42→v43 (`js/debt.js` behavior changed).
  - **Verified overall**: `node --check` on every touched file, full local suite (`tests/unit.mjs`, `tests/functions-sweep.mjs` — 28/28, `tests/smoke.mjs`) — all pass.

- **Merged and deployed the push-consolidation/debt-date PR above.** PR [#192](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/192), squash-merged as `f52a9f7` after both CI jobs (`smoke`, `firestore-rules`) went green with no review comments. Deployed via `firebase deploy --only functions,hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add` off `origin/main` (`cd functions && npm install` first, a fresh worktree has no `node_modules` of its own) — both this repo's Cloud Functions this time, not just hosting, since `functions/lib/sweep.js` changed: `notificationSweep` and `privatRates` both updated successfully, hosting released "found 46 files in .". Local branch/worktree cleaned up afterward (`git branch -D`, `git worktree remove`); remote branch deletion needs no manual step anymore now that "Automatically delete head branches" is on. **Not yet re-tested live**: the actual duplicate-push fix needs the account owner's own device to confirm only one consolidated notification arrives at the next daily-reminder time — this sandbox's stubbed-Firebase test coverage confirms the *logic* is correct (28/28 `functions-sweep.mjs` tests) but can't observe a real FCM delivery, same category of "needs a real device" gap as prior push-related entries in this file.

- **Follow-up from the same screenshot pair above: modernized the trash/pencil glyphs and added swipe-to-delete to the transaction list — the "compromise" option the account owner picked over a `lucide-react`/Material-Symbols swap (doesn't fit this stack, see the earlier entry) or shrinking the just-enlarged touch targets back down (would have undone PR #188's own accessibility fix).**
  - **New `trash`/`pencil` glyphs** (`js/classic-globals.js`'s `ICON_PATHS`) — simpler, flatter silhouettes (trash: no internal vertical lines; pencil: a cleaner diagonal nib) in the same monochrome stroke style as every other icon here, not a swap to an external icon set.
  - **Transaction rows: pencil dropped entirely, delete moved behind a swipe-to-reveal panel (Telegram/Gmail-style), buttons no longer always-visible.** Tapping a row already opened edit (`js/analytics-csv.js`'s existing `.tx-item` click listener) — the always-visible pencil button was pure duplication of that, and was also *why* the too-small-gap mis-tap-into-edit bug (fixed in PR #188) could happen in the first place. `txItemInnerHtml()` now wraps the row's visible content in `.tx-item-inner` (the part that visually moves) with a single `.tx-swipe-delete` button as a sibling behind it. New `setupTxSwipe()` (mirrors `js/ui-widgets.js`'s `initSheetDrag()` pointer-event pattern, horizontal instead of vertical) handles the actual touch drag; mouse/keyboard users reach the same button via CSS `:hover`/`:focus-within` on the row instead, since neither has a swipe gesture available. A swiped-open row's *first* tap just closes it rather than also opening edit (a touchend can register as a click on the same element); tapping anywhere else, or opening a different row, closes any currently-open one.
  - **Real bug caught by screenshot, not by reading the CSS**: the first working version *translated* `.tx-item-inner` left to reveal the delete button — reveals the right side correctly, but also pushes the category icon on the *left* edge past `.tx-item`'s own `overflow:hidden` boundary, clipping it off completely once swiped open. Fixed by animating `.tx-item-inner`'s own `width` (shrinking the box from its right edge) instead of `transform`-ing it — the left edge then never moves, so nothing on that side can clip. Documented in both `index.html`'s CSS comment and `analytics-csv.js`'s drag handler, specifically so a future translateX "optimization" doesn't reintroduce the same clipping bug.
  - New `tests/tx-swipe-delete.mjs` (added to `.github/workflows/smoke-test.yml` too) dispatches synthetic `PointerEvent`s directly on a `.tx-item` (Playwright has no built-in touch-drag API) to cover: a short swipe snaps back, a long swipe reveals delete, tapping an open row closes it instead of opening edit, tapping outside closes it, and deleting via the revealed button actually removes the row. `tests/e2e-crud.mjs`/`tests/tx-list-targeted-update.mjs` updated for the removed pencil button and the new `.tx-swipe-delete` selector (the CRUD test's delete step now `.hover()`s the row first, matching how a real mouse user would reveal it, before clicking).
  - `js/finance.js`'s `window.editTransaction` export removed — its one remaining caller (`.tx-item`'s click listener) is a real `addEventListener` callback now, not an inline-onclick string, so the real ES-module import is enough; `window.deleteTransaction`/`window.openNewTxModal` stay (still referenced by literal onclick strings).
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v43→v44.
  - **Verified**: full local suite including the new test (`tests/unit.mjs`, `tests/functions-sweep.mjs`, `tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs`, `tests/e2e-modals.mjs`, `tests/stress-tx-list.mjs`, `tests/tx-list-targeted-update.mjs`, `tests/tx-swipe-delete.mjs`) — all pass. Plus one-off Playwright screenshots (not committed) of the resting list, the swiped-open state, and a settings-manager pencil icon, confirming both the new glyphs and the clipping fix actually look right, not just pass assertions.
  - **Native Android, same pass, per the standing "keep android/ in lockstep" convention**: `FinanceScreen.kt`'s `TransactionRow` took an `onDelete` callback that was never actually wired to any UI element — no delete affordance existed there at all, a real gap this pass closed using Compose Material3's own `SwipeToDismissBox` (the idiomatic native equivalent, not a hand-rolled pointer-drag port of the web version) rather than leaving it silently unaddressed. See the dedicated entry below for details — still unverified by an actual build, same standing gap as every other Android commit in this file.

- **Debt tab payment history: still-broken delete + oldest-first ordering, reported directly by the account owner after using the app on a real phone** (2026-07-15, PR #196). Two distinct complaints in one message: (1) "видалення досі не працює, відкривається редагування" (delete still doesn't work, edit opens instead) — this was about the **Debt tab's payment-history rows**, not Finance transactions (those already got swipe-to-delete in the PR #194/#195 pass above); (2) "поміняй місцями щоб останні платежі і разрахунки були з верху списку" (swap so the latest payments/calculations are at the top).
  - **Root-cause investigation before touching code**: wrote a throwaway Playwright repro (`elementFromPoint` hit-testing + `page.touchscreen.tap()` at exact button centers, at both 390px and 360px viewports, with 1-2 entries) against the *existing* `.debt-row-del`/`.debt-row-edit` pair. Every precise synthetic tap landed correctly — no logic bug, `document.addEventListener('click', ..., true)` with `e.target.closest('[data-action]')` resolves correctly regardless of capture phase. So this isn't reproducible as a hit-test/geometry bug the way headless testing can catch. The one concrete, verifiable UX defect found instead: `.debt-row-del` and `.debt-row-edit` were both plain `var(--muted2)` grey by default, only turning red on `:hover` — a state that never fires on a touch device — so on a real phone the delete button gave **no visual "this is destructive" cue** and was easy to confuse with the adjacent, identically-styled edit button at a glance. Given that plus the account owner's own earlier-approved compromise for the *identical* Finance-tab complaint ("Компроміс: swipe-to-delete + приховати кнопки за замовчуванням"), applied the same proven pattern here rather than re-litigating a fix that already didn't hold up once (small icon enlarge + gap increase, done earlier this session, evidently wasn't sufficient).
  - **Fix**: `.debt-row` restructured into the same outer-shell/`-inner`/swipe-delete-sibling shape as `.tx-item` (`js/debt.js`'s `setupDebtRowSwipe()`, closely mirrors `js/analytics-csv.js`'s `setupTxSwipe()` — pointer-event drag, width-based reveal not `transform` for the same left-edge-clipping reason documented above, `DEBT_ROW_SWIPE_REVEAL_PX`/`_OPEN_THRESHOLD` constants, a document-level `pointerdown` listener closing any open swipe on an outside tap). Deliberately **not** extracted into a shared helper with `setupTxSwipe()` — different outer/inner class names, and this repo's established style keeps per-file render logic self-contained (same reasoning already documented for the `tests/*.mjs` stub duplication). Unlike the transaction row, the pencil (edit) button stays **always visible** inside `.debt-row-inner` rather than joining the swipe reveal — a debt entry has no "tap the row to edit" affordance to deduplicate against (editing is inline, not a modal), so only the one genuinely ambiguous/destructive action (delete) needed hiding.
  - **Reorder fix**: `cd.entries` itself is left in its original `push()`/chronological order — `debtCurrentBalance()` (`cd.entries[cd.entries.length-1].balance`) and the in-loop running-balance/discrepancy-hint math both depend on that array order, unlike Finance's `AppState.transactions` which is genuinely `unshift()`-ordered newest-first. Only the *rendered* row order flips: `renderDebt()`'s entry loop still iterates oldest→newest (to keep the balance chain correct) but now does `lc.prepend(row)` instead of `lc.appendChild(row)`, so the last-processed (newest) entry ends up as the first DOM child. Verified with a dedicated assertion that reversing display order doesn't disturb the discrepancy-hint calculation.
  - New `tests/debt-swipe-delete.mjs` (added to `.github/workflows/smoke-test.yml`): adds 3 debt-payment entries and asserts newest-first DOM order, asserts the balance-chain/discrepancy math is unaffected by the display reorder, then covers the same swipe matrix as `tests/tx-swipe-delete.mjs` (short swipe snaps back, long swipe reveals delete, delete-via-revealed-button actually removes the row) plus confirms the always-visible pencil button still enters inline edit mode directly, unaffected by the change.
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v45→v46 (from PR #195's quick-actions polish, itself already v44→v45).
  - **Verified**: full local suite (`tests/unit.mjs`, `tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs`, `tests/e2e-modals.mjs`, `tests/tx-swipe-delete.mjs`, `tests/tx-list-targeted-update.mjs`, new `tests/debt-swipe-delete.mjs`) — all pass.

- **Started the UX audit action plan with a low-risk Finance quick-actions polish** (2026-07-15): based on the follow-up audit/plan, made the first concrete UI change instead of another report-only pass. The Finance tab now exposes the primary user task directly in the quick-actions row via a new prominent `Операція` / `Transaction` action (`data-action="open-new-tx-modal"`) before the secondary Tools/Budgets/Goals actions, so adding a transaction is visible in the content flow rather than relying only on the floating FAB. The old round quick-action buttons were replaced with calmer card-like actions: secondary actions now use subtle bordered surfaces and smaller icon wells, while the primary transaction action keeps the gradient. Also reduced the global purple glow intensity on raised surfaces, accent buttons, FABs, and active tab ripples in both dark and light themes so the interface keeps depth but reads less noisy. Added the new quick-action icon/i18n keys in `js/classic-globals.js`, and bumped `sw.js` cache `v44→v45` because that cached JS file changed. Verified locally with `node --check js/classic-globals.js`, `node --check sw.js`, and `node tests/unit.mjs`. Attempted the usual Playwright-backed `node tests/smoke.mjs` / `node tests/e2e-crud.mjs` and the follow-up screenshot pass, but this sandbox had no global Playwright install at either path the repo test resolver checks; trying to install it with `npm install -g playwright` hit the environment's `403 Forbidden` npm registry policy, so browser verification is blocked by tooling availability rather than by an app failure.

- **Two more real bugs from the account owner, reported minutes after the Debt swipe-to-delete deploy above, this time via two screenshots** (2026-07-15, PR #198): (1) a screenshot of Finance's transaction list showing dates in *ascending* order (oldest at top) — "платежі у фінансах треба зверху нові!" (Finance's payments need newest on top too); (2) a screenshot of the just-deployed Debt payment-history list showing every row collapsed to a single word ("Поточний", the account owner's own text in the amount field for many of their real entries) with a sliver of red visible at each row's corner — a **real visual regression** introduced by the PR #196 swipe-to-delete change, not a duplicate of the delete-vs-edit report.
  - **Finance newest-first**: `AppState.transactions` was assumed to already be newest-first because `addTransaction()` (`js/finance.js`) does `unshift()` for a transaction added *during the current session* — true, but irrelevant for everything loaded from Firestore: `loadTransactionsFromSubcollection()`'s `getDocs()` call has no `orderBy`, so a loaded account's history arrives in Firestore's own unspecified document order, confirmed by the account owner's screenshot to not be date-sorted at all. Fixed at two layers: `js/color-picker.js`'s `fbLoadNow()` now explicitly sorts `AppState.transactions` (date descending, `id` descending as a same-date tiebreaker) right after either load branch (migration or subcollection), before caching it to `localStorage` — so the canonical in-memory order and the cold-start cache are both correct; `js/analytics-csv.js`'s `renderFinance()` *also* sorts a copy of `filtered` the same way at render time, independent of `AppState.transactions`' own order, so a backdated edit mid-session (no reload in between) still displays correctly without needing every mutation site to maintain a sorted-array invariant by hand.
  - **Debt row content-collapse regression, root cause found via live Playwright screenshot repro (not from reading the CSS)**: `.debt-list` is a column flexbox (`display:flex;flex-direction:column;max-height:560px;overflow-y:auto`). Per the CSS flexbox spec, a flex item with any `overflow` other than `visible` gets an **automatic minimum size of 0** instead of "the size of its content" — `.debt-row` (a flex item) needs `overflow:hidden` for the swipe-clip added in PR #196, and without an explicit `flex-shrink:0` to override that, the browser was free to shrink every row down to a sliver (measured: 25px tall vs. its actual ~133px content) once the list's total content height exceeded `.debt-list`'s 560px cap — which any account with more than ~4 payment entries hits immediately. `.tx-item` never had this problem because `#tx-list-container` isn't a flex container at all. Fixed with one property: `.debt-row{flex-shrink:0}`. Reproduced with a throwaway script seeding 17 entries (several with a literal "Поточний" amount, matching the account owner's real data) before the fix, confirmed pixel-for-pixel matching the reported screenshot, then confirmed fixed after.
  - New `tests/tx-list-sort-order.mjs` (added to `.github/workflows/smoke-test.yml`): seeds 4 transactions directly into the stubbed Firestore *oldest-first* (mimicking Firestore's real unordered `getDocs()`), including two sharing the same date, and asserts the rendered list is newest-first with `id` correctly breaking the date tie. Extended `tests/debt-swipe-delete.mjs` with a geometry regression check: adds enough entries to overflow `.debt-list`'s `max-height`, then asserts `.debt-row`'s rendered height still matches its content's height (would have caught the `flex-shrink` regression directly).
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v46→v47.
  - **Verified**: full local suite (`tests/unit.mjs`, `tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs`, `tests/e2e-modals.mjs`, `tests/tx-swipe-delete.mjs`, `tests/tx-list-targeted-update.mjs`, `tests/stress-tx-list.mjs`, `tests/pull-to-refresh.mjs`, `tests/debt-swipe-delete.mjs` (with the new geometry check), new `tests/tx-list-sort-order.mjs`) — all pass.

- **Two small polish reports, right after the previous deploy, this time in the same message rather than separate screenshots** (2026-07-15, PR #200): "не плавная кнопка свайпа (красная корзинка) гострі кути" (the swipe-delete red trash button isn't smooth, sharp corners) and "свайп вниз дуже погано працює десь там трохи якщо потягнути за уголок" (swipe-down works badly, a little, if you drag from the corner).
  - **Sharp corners, confirmed via live screenshot**: `.tx-swipe-delete`/`.debt-row-swipe-delete` had no `border-radius` of their own. The outer row's `overflow:hidden` clip already rounds the button's *far* (right) edge for free, matching the row's own 18px radius — but the *near* (left) edge, revealed flush against the shrunk inner card once swiped open, stayed sharp-cornered, since nothing rounds a straight internal edge that isn't at the clipping boundary. Read as a red rectangle with only two rounded corners stuck onto an otherwise fully-rounded card. Fixed with one property on each: `border-radius:18px`, rounding all four corners (the right side was already effectively rounded, so this only changes the left).
  - **"Swipe down bad at the corner", root cause found by reproducing the exact drag geometry**: `initSheetDrag()` (`js/ui-widgets.js`) listens for drags on `.sheet-grabber`/`.modal-header`, but `.sheet-grabber`'s hit-box used to be *exactly* its visible 36×4px bar, centered in its row — touching the sheet's actual top-left/top-right corners (where a thumb naturally lands, drawn there by the sheet's own rounded top corners) missed that narrow bar entirely and fell through to `.modal-card-body`'s bare padding, which has no drag listener at all. No visual cue marked where the dead zone started, so it read as an unreliable gesture ("sometimes works") rather than a clean boundary. Fixed by making `.sheet-grabber` a full-width, 28px-tall flex-centered hit-box, with the visible bar redrawn as a `::after` pseudo-element (unchanged in size) so nothing about the sheet's appearance changed, only where a drag can start.
  - New `tests/sheet-drag-dismiss.mjs` (added to `.github/workflows/smoke-test.yml`): opens the Tools modal at mobile viewport and asserts a short drag from the grabber center snaps back, a long drag from the center dismisses, and — the actual regression check — long drags starting from the far-left and far-right edges of the grabber's row *also* dismiss (previously did nothing).
  - **Follow-up from a Codex review on this same PR, P2**: the fix above still only made `.sheet-grabber` span `width:100%` of `.modal-card-body`'s own *content* box — but that box keeps its `padding:22px 24px`, so the grabber's hit-box still stopped 24px short of the card's actual left/right edges, i.e. still a dead zone in exactly the spot ("the corners") the bug report was about, just narrower than before rather than gone. The review's point was concrete and correct — caught something the "far-left/far-right of the grabber's *own* row" test above didn't, since that test measured `.sheet-grabber`'s own (already-too-narrow) `boundingBox()`, not the card's. Fixed by bleeding `.sheet-grabber` past that padding entirely: `width:calc(100% + 48px)` with `-24px` left/right margins cancels the parent's padding out, so the hit-box now reaches `.modal-card`'s own rounded-corner edge (still correctly clipped to that rounded shape by `.modal-card`'s `overflow:hidden`, it just no longer stops short of it). Added a dedicated regression case to `tests/sheet-drag-dismiss.mjs` that starts the drag from a point 8px inside the *card's* own bounds (not the grabber's) — confirmed via `elementFromPoint` that it actually hits `.sheet-grabber` before dispatching, so the test exercises the real CSS geometry instead of trivially passing regardless of it.
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v47→v48.
  - **Verified**: full local suite (`tests/unit.mjs`, `tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs`, `tests/e2e-modals.mjs`, `tests/tx-swipe-delete.mjs`, `tests/debt-swipe-delete.mjs`, `tests/sheet-drag-dismiss.mjs` (with the padding-bleed regression case)) — all pass. Corner-rounding fix confirmed via a live Playwright screenshot before/after (the reported jagged red block, then a clean rounded pill shape); geometry-checked (`getBoundingClientRect()`) that the row/inner/delete-button boxes still align exactly with no gap.

- **Extended-FAB expand/collapse-on-scroll, requested via two screenshots of a different app's (Claude Code mobile) session-list UI** (2026-07-15, branch `claude/expandable-swipe-button-03kdh5`): the account owner pointed at that app's "+ New session" floating button — a pill with an icon+label at rest that shrinks to a plain icon-only circle while the list is scrolled, re-expanding once scrolling settles — and asked for the same behavior here. Clarified scope via `AskUserQuestion` first (two questions: expand/collapse-on-scroll vs. a static pill+animation-only; and whether the reference screenshot's swipe-revealed "..."/scissors row-action buttons should also be replicated) — confirmed scope is the FAB expand/collapse only, existing swipe-to-delete on transaction/debt rows already covers the "action buttons on a row" need.
  - **Scope**: both `.fin-fab` buttons in the app (Finance tab's "Нова операція", Debt tab's "Новий платіж" — `index.html`), the only two FABs that exist; the Shopping tab's add action is an inline form, not a FAB, so untouched.
  - **CSS approach**: kept `.fin-fab`'s `border-radius` a constant `28px` in both states rather than transitioning it — on the 56px-tall collapsed circle that's exactly 50% (a circle), and on the wider expanded pill it's exactly `height/2` (fully-rounded ends), so the shape morphs correctly for free with no radius animation needed. The width itself is never animated directly (CSS can't reliably transition to/from an unset/auto width) — instead the button's `padding` transitions (`0 20px 0 16px` expanded → `0 16px` collapsed) and the new `.fin-fab-label` span's `max-width`/`opacity` transition from `200px`/`1` to `0`/`0`, so the button's flex-row content width animates smoothly and the collapsed total (`16+24(icon)+16=56px`) matches the FAB's original fixed circle size exactly. `prefers-reduced-motion` disables all three transitions.
  - **JS**: new `setupFabExpandCollapse()` (`js/app-init.js`, called once from `init()`'s cold-init block alongside `setupPullToRefresh()`/`setupModalAccessibility()`) — one `window` `scroll` listener (`{passive:true}`) toggles a `.fab-collapsed` class on every `.fin-fab` on the page (both buttons share one listener; only one is ever visible at a time since `switchTab()` hides the other tab's whole section) on every scroll event, with a 600ms debounce timer that removes the class once scrolling has actually stopped.
  - Reused the existing `finance_new_tx`/`debt_new_payment` i18n keys (already defined for uk/en, used elsewhere for the same two actions) for the new `.fin-fab-label` spans rather than adding new ones.
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v48→v49 (`index.html` and `js/app-init.js`, both precached, changed).
  - **Verified**: full local suite (`tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs` — confirms the FAB's `data-action="open-new-tx-modal"` click still opens the modal correctly with the label span now inside it, `tests/e2e-modals.mjs`, `tests/pull-to-refresh.mjs` — confirms the new scroll listener doesn't interfere with the existing touch-based pull-to-refresh gesture) all pass. Also wrote a one-off (uncommitted, per this repo's convention for one-off manual verification) Playwright script seeding 8 transactions and measuring `.fin-fab`'s `boundingBox()` at rest (168.6px wide pill), 400ms into a scroll (56px circle, confirmed fully collapsed), and 900ms after scrolling stopped (back to the 168.6px pill) — screenshots visually confirmed the pill-with-label-text at rest and the plain "+" circle mid-scroll, matching the reference screenshots' behavior.

- **Fixed a real bug in the FAB expand/collapse feature above, reported directly by the account owner right after the deploy: "не поацює завжди розгорнута" (doesn't work, always expanded)** (2026-07-15, branch `claude/fab-nested-scroll-fix`). Root cause: `setupFabExpandCollapse()` (`js/app-init.js`) listened for `scroll` on `window`, but `#tx-list-container`/`.debt-list` (`index.html`) are each a fixed-`max-height` `overflow-y:auto` container — on any real account with more than a handful of rows, the user's actual scrolling happens *inside* that container, not on the page/window itself (confirmed the PR's own verification script never actually exercised this: it added only enough transactions to overflow the *page*, which masked the bug entirely). `scroll` events never bubble (not even from an element up to `document`/`window`), so a window-level listener silently never saw those scrolls — the FAB just never collapsed on a real device with real data. Fixed by moving the listener to `document.addEventListener('scroll', ..., {capture:true})` — the capture phase still traverses top-down through every ancestor regardless of bubbling, so one listener now catches scrolling inside any current or future nested scroll container, not just the page itself. Same technique this repo already uses for click delegation past a `stopPropagation()` (see the `closeManagers`/phase-3-6 `window.*` cleanup entries above), applied here to a different bubbling gap (no-bubble-at-all, not stopped-mid-bubble).
  - **Verified** with a dedicated one-off Playwright script (uncommitted, per this repo's convention): seeded 15 transactions, confirmed `.fin-fab`'s `boundingBox()` stays a 168.6px pill when idle, programmatically scrolled `#tx-list-container` directly (not the page) via `el.scrollTop=200` + a synthetic `scroll` event, and confirmed the FAB now correctly collapses to a 56px circle mid-scroll and re-expands ~600ms after it stops — the exact scenario the original verification missed. Also re-ran the full existing suite (`tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs`, `tests/e2e-modals.mjs`, `tests/pull-to-refresh.mjs`, `tests/tx-swipe-delete.mjs`, `tests/debt-swipe-delete.mjs`, `tests/sheet-drag-dismiss.mjs`) to confirm the capture-phase listener (passive, no `preventDefault`/`stopPropagation`) doesn't interfere with any of the other scroll-adjacent gestures (pull-to-refresh's touch-based drag, swipe-to-delete, sheet drag-to-dismiss) — all pass.
  - **Lesson for next time**: a scroll/resize-adjacent feature's own manual verification script needs to specifically overflow *whichever* container the real feature targets, not just "the page" in general — this repo has several independently-scrolling containers (`#tx-list-container`, `.debt-list`, `.modal-card-body`, `.cs-panel-scroll`, several manager-modal lists), and a script that only pushes the outer page past viewport height can pass cleanly while missing the one that actually matters in production.
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v49→v50 (`js/app-init.js`, precached, changed).

- **Merged and deployed the FAB nested-scroll fix above.** PR [#203](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/203), squash-merged as `8695152` once both CI jobs (`smoke`, `firestore-rules`) went green with no review comments. Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach` — succeeded on the first attempt, "found 46 files in .", "uploading new files [0/2]" (`js/app-init.js`, `sw.js`). - **Three more real bugs from the account owner, reported in one message right after the previous deploy** (2026-07-15, branch `claude/fab-fixed-position-and-ptr-fix`): (1) "свайп в модалке ... якщо я всередині екрану свайпну йде оновлення сторінки" (swiping in the modal — or on screen generally — triggers a page refresh); (2) "кнопки фаб зависоко" (the FAB buttons are too high); (3) "фаб кнопка у фінансах не зафіксована на місті вона скролиться з екраном" (the Finance FAB isn't fixed in place, it scrolls with the screen). Investigated (2) and (3) together first since they sounded related, and a live `boundingBox()` measurement confirmed it: right after switching to the Finance tab, `.fin-fab`'s rect had `top:1052` while the viewport was only 844px tall — the button wasn't `position:fixed` to the viewport at all.
  - **Root cause of (2)+(3), one bug**: `.tab-content.tab-in` (index.html) plays a one-shot entrance animation with `animation-fill-mode:both`, which — by design — keeps the animation's *end-state* styles applied forever once it finishes, not just during playback. The end state includes `transform:translateY(0)` — visually a no-op, but per the CSS spec **any** non-`none` transform value (including an identity translate) establishes a new containing block for `position:fixed` descendants. `#tab-finance`/`#tab-debt` (both `.tab-content`) each host a `.fin-fab`, so once the entrance animation finished playing (every single tab switch, `.tab-in` was never removed again until the *next* switch), the FAB silently stopped being fixed to the viewport and became `position:fixed`-inside-`#tab-finance` instead — which behaves like `position:absolute` relative to that section's own (content-height-dependent, not viewport-height) box. That explains both reports at once: "scrolls with the screen" (it moves whenever the section's height/scroll position changes, since it's no longer anchored to the viewport) and "too high" (its resting screen position became whatever `bottom:104px`-from-the-section's-own-bottom-edge happened to land on, unrelated to where the actual bottom nav bar sits — sometimes far above it, sometimes off-screen entirely). **Fix**: `switchTab()` (`js/app-init.js`) now removes `.tab-in` again via a `{once:true}` `animationend` listener right after the entrance animation finishes playing, restoring `transform:none` with no visible change (the animation has already completed by then). Verified via the same `boundingBox()` measurement: `.fin-fab`'s rect now stays byte-for-byte identical (both `x` and `y`) whether the page is scrolled to `0` or to `300`, landing at `y:684` on a 844px-tall viewport with only an 8px gap above the nav bar — matching the values CLAUDE.md's "Floating pill bottom nav" note already documented as the deliberately-tuned offset (`.fin-fab`'s 104px vs. `.app`'s 112px bottom padding), confirming (2) was fully a symptom of this same bug rather than a separate spacing request — no CSS offset value needed changing once position:fixed actually worked again.
  - **Root cause of (1), a different bug**: `setupPullToRefresh()`'s touchstart guard (`js/app-init.js`) only ever checked `document.scrollingElement.scrollTop` — it had no way to tell "the user is scrolling a nested list" apart from "the user is pulling the whole page down from its top", because several containers in this app (`#tx-list-container`, `.debt-list`, and every `.modal-card-body`) are independently scrollable (`overflow-y:auto` with their own `max-height`) while the *page* itself often never needs to scroll at all — the exact same blind spot documented in the FAB expand/collapse nested-scroll fix two entries above, showing up here as the opposite failure mode (there, the page-level listener didn't *see* a nested scroll; here, the page-level pull-gesture logic didn't know to *ignore* one). Swiping down inside the transaction-form bottom sheet, or a long transaction/debt list, could therefore start tracking a pull-to-refresh gesture that was never meant to be one. **Fix**: added `closestScrollableAncestor(el)` (`js/app-init.js`) — walks up from the touch's target looking for a nested `overflow-y:auto`/`scroll` container that actually has overflow content, stopping at `body`/`documentElement` — and the touchstart guard now bails whenever the touch started inside one, in addition to the pre-existing `AppState.openModalStack.length` check (which, on inspection, never actually covered this case on its own — `.modal-card-body`'s own scroll is a separate mechanism from "is a modal open", it just happened to co-occur in the account owner's specific in-modal report).
  - **Verified**: a dedicated one-off Playwright script (uncommitted, per this repo's convention) dispatching synthetic multi-step `TouchEvent` sequences (Playwright has no built-in touch-drag API, same reasoning as `tests/pull-to-refresh.mjs`'s own approach) confirmed a downward drag starting inside `#tx-list-container` and inside an open `#tx-form-modal`'s body no longer sets the `#ptr-indicator`'s `ptr-loading` class, while the FAB stays viewport-pinned across a page scroll. Re-ran the full existing suite (`tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs`, `tests/e2e-modals.mjs`, `tests/pull-to-refresh.mjs` — confirms the legitimate page-top pull still works and still correctly declines mid-scroll, `tests/tx-swipe-delete.mjs`, `tests/debt-swipe-delete.mjs`, `tests/sheet-drag-dismiss.mjs`, `tests/stress-tx-list.mjs`) — all pass, confirming neither fix broke any existing swipe/drag/scroll interaction.
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v50→v51 (`js/app-init.js`, precached, changed).

- **Merged and deployed the FAB position:fixed + pull-to-refresh fix above.** PR [#204](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/204), squash-merged as `37ad359` once both CI jobs (`smoke`, `firestore-rules`) went green with no review comments. Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach` — succeeded on the first attempt, "found 46 files in .", "uploading new files [0/2]" (`js/app-init.js`, `sw.js`). - **Three items from one account-owner feedback message (screenshot of a broken finance list + two feature asks), 2026-07-15, branch `claude/list-fix-calendar-debt`:**
  - **(bug, critical) Transaction rows collapsed to ~12px slivers when "view all" was expanded, and swiping over the list triggered pull-to-refresh.** Both were the *same* root cause. `#tx-list-container` (`.tx-list`) is a `display:flex;flex-direction:column;max-height:500px;overflow-y:auto` container, and `.tx-item` carries `overflow:hidden` for its swipe-clip — a flex item with non-visible overflow gets an automatic min-size of 0 (CSS flexbox spec), so without `flex-shrink:0` the flex algorithm crushed every row to fit the 500px cap instead of letting the container scroll (reproduced: rows 12px, `scrollHeight===clientHeight===500`). This is the *exact* bug already documented+fixed on `.debt-row`; CLAUDE.md wrongly claimed `.tx-item` was immune because "the container isn't a flex container" — it is now. The collapse also disabled the pull-to-refresh nested-scroll guard (PR #204): a non-overflowing container reads as non-scrollable, so `closestScrollableAncestor()` returned null and PTR fired on every swipe over the list. Fixed with one property — `.tx-item{flex-shrink:0}` (`index.html`) — which restored 61px rows, real internal scrolling (`scrollHeight 1734 > 500`), and therefore the PTR guard. Added a geometry regression assertion to `tests/stress-tx-list.mjs` (asserts a row keeps full height and the container overflows) that fails on the 12px-sliver state.
  - **(feature) Calendar shift markers: wide word-badges → compact colored letter tokens.** The account owner asked for short recognizable marks ("Д"/"Н") instead of words. Added an explicit `code` field (1-2 chars) to the built-in shift types (`js/core.js`: День→Д, День+→Д+, Ніч→Н, НічР→Нр, НічП→Нп, Вих→В — explicit because several share a first letter). `renderCalendar()` (`js/calendar.js`) now renders each shift as a `.shift-token` colored keycap (`index.html` CSS, `.day-tokens` flex-wrap row) showing `shiftCode(t)`: the explicit `code`, else a derived first-letter (with a smart fallback that keeps the legacy `short` distinguishers — `День+`→Д+, `НічР`→Нр — so existing testing-device configs saved before `code` existed still render distinct tokens with no migration). A month now reads as a tidy grid of colored letters. `short`/`name` unchanged (legend still shows full names).
  - **(feature) Debt tab payoff forecast.** A competitor-inspired (loan-payoff-tracker) addition: a new `#debt-forecast` card (`index.html`) with an inline-SVG **balance-burndown mini chart** (built from each entry's remaining `balance`, purple area+line, no chart lib) plus a plain-language pace estimate — `renderDebtForecast()` (`js/debt.js`) computes the average paydown-per-payment (counting only balance-reducing payments) and shows "≈ N payments to go at this pace" + the average payment. Shown only with enough signal (startAmount set, ≥2 payments, positive balance and downward trend); handles the fully-paid and no-downward-trend edge cases. By payment *count*, not date, on purpose — `entry.date` is free-form text. New `trendDown` icon (`js/classic-globals.js` ICON_PATHS/ICON_NAMES) + `debt_forecast_*` i18n (uk/en). Verified the math live: start 10000, payments 2000/1500/2500/1000 → avg 1750, balance 3000 → "≈ 2 payments to go".
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v51→v52 (index.html + js/core.js/calendar.js/debt.js/classic-globals.js changed).
  - **Verified**: full local suite (`tests/unit.mjs`, `smoke`, `e2e-crud`, `e2e-modals`, `tx-swipe-delete`, `debt-swipe-delete`, `tx-list-targeted-update`, `tx-list-sort-order`, `pull-to-refresh`, `sheet-drag-dismiss`, `stress-tx-list` with the new flex-shrink regression check, `functions-sweep`) — all pass. - **CRITICAL: the deployed CSP silently disabled every remaining inline `onclick=""` handler — "delete opened edit" in Finance and "add doesn't work" in Shopping** (2026-07-15, branch `claude/csp-inline-handlers-fix`). Reported by the account owner: the red-trash delete on transactions opened the edit modal instead of deleting (narrowed by a follow-up message to Finance income/transfer rows), and the Shopping add button did nothing.
  - **Root cause**: `firebase.json`'s hosting `Content-Security-Policy` has `script-src 'self' https://www.gstatic.com https://apis.google.com` with **no `'unsafe-inline'`** (and no `'unsafe-eval'`). Under that policy, inline event-handler attributes (`onclick=""` baked into rendered HTML via innerHTML) **never execute** on the live site (Firebase Hosting / `.web.app` TWA) — but the sandbox's `python3 -m http.server` sends no CSP, so they work in every local test and no-op only in production. The tx-list delete button was `onclick="event.stopPropagation();deleteTransaction()"` — no-op under CSP, so the tap bubbled to the row's own click→`editTransaction` listener ("delete opened edit"). `emptyStateHtml`'s action button baked an arbitrary JS string into `onclick=""` — dead too, so every empty-state "add first item" CTA (Shopping's included, when the list is empty) did nothing.
  - **Fix**: converted all 8 remaining inline-`onclick` sites (the only ones left, all in `js/*.js` template strings — `index.html` already had zero) to `data-action` dispatched by the existing delegated capture-phase listeners, which CSP allows: `analytics-csv.js` tx-delete (`delete-transaction`, with `e.stopPropagation()` in the handler so it doesn't reach the row edit listener) + the 3 onboarding start-guide buttons; `finance.js`/`settings-managers.js` the 3 color swatches (`open-color-picker` + `data-kind`/`data-id`, one handler registered in settings-managers.js, `openColorPicker` now `export`ed from color-picker.js); `ui-widgets.js` `emptyStateHtml` (`onClick` JS-string param → `actionName` data-action param; its 5 callers switched to action names — `open-new-tx-modal`/`toggle-quick-fill`/`add-new-debt`/`open-new-debt-entry-modal`/`focus-shopping-name`, the last two newly registered in debt.js/shopping.js). `el.onclick=`/`cell.onclick=` DOM-property assignments were left alone — CSP doesn't block those, only inline HTML attributes.
  - **New `tests/csp-handlers.mjs` (added to CI)**: the whole reason this shipped is that no test ran under the CSP header. This one fulfills the top-level document with the exact CSP read live from `firebase.json`, then asserts the tx-list delete opens the confirm dialog (not the edit modal) and actually deletes, the Shopping empty-state CTA focuses the input, and the Shopping add button adds — all under CSP — plus that the app emits no inline-script/handler CSP violations. Updated `tests/debt-swipe-delete.mjs`'s empty-state selector from `[onclick*="addNewDebt"]` to `[data-action="add-new-debt"]` to match the conversion.
  - Promoted the CSP-inline-handler gotcha into CLAUDE.md (the `index.html` script-structure section) — it's an architectural, recurring trap (local tests are blind to it), not a one-off. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` v52→v53.
  - **Verified**: the new CSP test + full local suite (`unit`, `smoke`, `e2e-crud`, `e2e-modals`, `tx-swipe-delete`, `debt-swipe-delete`, `tx-list-targeted-update`, `stress-tx-list`, `pull-to-refresh`, `sheet-drag-dismiss`) all pass.

Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach` — succeeded on the first attempt, "found 46 files in .", "uploading new files [0/10]" (the 8 changed js files + sw.js + index-adjacent test/workflow assets that count as hosting files). No `firestore.rules`/`functions` changes, nothing else to redeploy. GitHub Pages mirror auto-deploys on push to `main`. Local branch `claude/csp-inline-handlers-fix` and the deploy worktree were cleaned up after; remote branch deletion is automatic (repo setting, see CLAUDE.md).

  - **Gotcha hit while syncing back up afterward**: this session's own working directory (`/home/user/Maxtr`, distinct from the scratch worktree the actual PR #239 fixes were made in) was still checked out at an older commit from earlier in the session. `git reset --soft origin/main` moved `HEAD` to the new tip but left the working tree/index at the old content, which made `git status` show 10 files as "modified" — actually a stale-checkout artifact (comparing old checked-out bytes against the new `HEAD`), not real uncommitted work; committing it as-is would have silently reverted PR #239's changes back out of `main`. The auto-mode permission classifier correctly declined a `git reset --hard origin/main` here (staged-looking changes with no explicit user go-ahead to discard them) — resolved instead with `git checkout HEAD -- .`, which restores the working tree from the (already-correct) `HEAD` without needing the "discard changes" framing. **Lesson**: after doing PR work in a separate scratch worktree, don't `reset --soft` the main session directory onto the new `origin/main` — either `git checkout HEAD -- .` right after, or just avoid touching the main session directory's branch state until there's an actual commit to make from it.

- **Formalized the two-agent (Codex + Claude) coordination convention in `CLAUDE.md`** (2026-07-16), prompted directly by the account owner ("мені треба щоб ви працювали над кодом по черзі... як зробити так щоб не було плутанини?" — I need you two to work on the code in turns, how do we avoid confusion). Clarified via `AskUserQuestion` first: both agents are triggered **manually, one at a time**, never concurrently — so there's no real race condition to design around, just state-staleness and duplicate-effort risks, both of which this same session had already hit firsthand a few entries above (`js/privacy-cache.js` independently added by two different Codex PRs before either merged; repeated false "dirty" `mergeable_state` from branches built on a since-squash-merged commit). Added a new bullet to CLAUDE.md's Operating conventions spelling out: Codex writes feature/review PRs, a Claude session owns reviewing/CI-fixing/merging/deploying/logging them (pushing fixes directly to a Codex PR's own branch rather than opening a competing one — the PR #239 precedent a few entries above); always re-fetch `origin/main` fresh rather than trusting cached context from earlier in a session; always rebase (or `git reset --soft origin/main` on a session's own branch) onto current `main` before every new commit, not reactively only when GitHub flags a conflict. No code change — `CLAUDE.md` only, since that's the one document both agents have independently demonstrated they read (Codex's own PR bodies/comments already reference "see CLAUDE.md" unprompted).
  - **A Codex review-agent run left behind a large, unmerged, code-review audit report** (read-only — its own transcript shows `git status --short` was clean, no commits/PR made) covering the whole app's design/UX/architecture/security. The account owner asked this session to pick up its actionable findings instead of leaving them to a future Codex run. Triaged the report's 7-item priority list against actual current code (not the report's claims, several of which had already been fixed by earlier-merged PRs in this same session — same "stale finding" pattern already seen with Codex's own automated PR reviews above) before doing anything: **already resolved, no action needed** — (1) "Firestore rules too weak for transaction docs" (the `validTransaction()`/`validTxTags()`/`validTransferFields()` helpers already enforce a type enum, amount range, date format, currency whitelist, comment/tag length limits, and transfer-specific fields — this was PR #238/#239's own "tightened Firestore validation" work); (5) "interactive `div.filter-chip` needs accessibility review" (`setupAccessibleClickableDivs()` in `js/ui-widgets.js` already applies `role="button"`, `tabindex`, Enter/Space keyboard activation, and `aria-pressed` sync generically to every `[data-action]` pseudo-button, re-run after every dynamic re-render — a static HTML read (which is how the report was produced) can't see this JS-applied behavior).
  - **Genuinely still valid, fixed this session**: (7) modal `aria-labelledby` — `setupModalAccessibility()` (`js/settings-managers.js`) already applied `role="dialog"`/`aria-modal="true"` programmatically, but never `aria-labelledby`, so a screen reader announced every modal as an unnamed "dialog." Added `findModalTitleEl()` (matches `.modal-date`/`.fin-form-title`/`.dlg-title`, covering every current modal including `#ui-dialog`'s differently-shaped `.dlg-card`) and wired an auto-generated id + `aria-labelledby` onto the card. New assertion in `tests/e2e-modals.mjs` locks in `role`/`aria-modal`/`aria-labelledby` pointing at real title text, not just the pre-existing focus-trap/Escape coverage. (3) `addTransaction()` mixing form-parsing/validation/persistence — `readTransactionForm()`/`validateTransactionDraft()` were *already* split out as separate functions inside `js/finance.js` by the PR #239 work, but not far enough to be unit-testable: `js/finance.js` transitively imports `firebase-sync.js`, which statically imports the Firebase SDK from a `https://` URL, so plain Node can't import it at all (`Only URLs with a scheme in: file and data are supported`) without the same Playwright-route-stubbing every other UI test already needs. Extracted `validateTransactionDraft()` (plus `TX_AMOUNT_MAX`/`TX_COMMENT_MAX`/`TX_DATE_RE`) into a new zero-import `js/tx-validation.js` — same reasoning as `functions/lib/pure.js` (see Commands section) — with `isTransfer` now passed in explicitly instead of read off `AppState`, so the module needs nothing but its own inputs. New `tests/tx-validation.mjs`: 12 plain-Node cases (bad amount/date/wallet/comment-length/category-length, transfer-specific wallet checks) with zero Firebase/DOM/Playwright involved.
  - **A genuinely separate bug found while wiring the new test into CI**: `tests/privacy-cache.mjs` (added alongside `js/privacy-cache.js` back in PR #238/#239) had never actually been added to `.github/workflows/smoke-test.yml`'s job list — it existed, passed locally every time it was run by hand in this session's own PR #239 work, but CI itself was never once exercising it. Added both `tests/tx-validation.mjs` and the previously-missing `tests/privacy-cache.mjs` to the `smoke` job. While in there, also re-synced CLAUDE.md's CI paragraph, which had independently drifted stale (missing `tx-swipe-delete`/`debt-swipe-delete`/`tx-list-sort-order`/`sheet-drag-dismiss`/`csp-handlers` from its own description of the job list).
  - **Deliberately not implemented, flagged back to the account owner as needing a real decision rather than done blind**: (2) the report called swapping transaction ids from `Date.now()` to `crypto.randomUUID()` a "low-risk refactor" to avoid collisions — checked this against `compareTransactionsNewest()` (`js/core.js`) first and it's not low-risk: same-date transactions with no `createdAt` (still common — `createdAt` was only added for transfer bookkeeping, not universally) fall through to `String(b.id).localeCompare(String(a.id))` as the *effective* chronological tiebreaker, which only produces correct newest-first ordering because `Date.now()`-based ids happen to sort both numerically and lexicographically by creation time. Swapping to non-chronological UUID strings there would silently randomize same-day transaction order — exactly the kind of "quiet financial-calculation bug" the report's own item (3) warned about, just introduced by following item (2) uncritically. Needs either always setting `createdAt` on every transaction (not just transfers) or a different collision-avoidance approach that preserves sortability — a call for the account owner, not a blind swap. (4) encrypted/threat-modeled local cache — the report is right that plaintext `localStorage` is a real exposure surface, but this repo already shipped a *toggle-based* mitigation for exactly this (`js/privacy-cache.js`'s per-device `mxSensitiveCache` setting, PR #238/#239) rather than encryption; going further to actual Web-Crypto encryption is a real feature-design decision (key derivation from PIN/passphrase, key storage, UX for a forgotten passphrase locking out local data) that needs the account owner's input, not something to bolt on unprompted. (6) optimistic-save sync-status/retry UX — a genuine, reasonably-scoped feature idea, left for a dedicated future pass rather than folding into this already-large one.
  - **Verified**: full local suite (`unit`, `tx-validation` with its 12 new cases, `privacy-cache`, `functions-sweep`, `smoke`, `e2e-crud`, `e2e-modals` with its new a11y assertion, `csp-handlers`, `stress-tx-list`, `tx-list-targeted-update`, `pull-to-refresh`, `tx-swipe-delete`, `debt-swipe-delete`, `sheet-drag-dismiss`, `tx-list-sort-order`) — all pass. `firestore.rules` had zero diff (nothing here touched it), so the emulator test wasn't re-run. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped `rytm-v59`→`rytm-v60` (new `js/tx-validation.js` added to `STATIC_ASSETS`).
