- **Full audit-followup session (2026-07-16)**: implemented all 9 items from a fresh full-app audit (design/UX, architecture/security, functionality-vs-niche comparison, 2026 web trends, prioritized roadmap — the audit itself was published as a standalone artifact in-session, not committed to the repo). In priority order:
  1. **Centralized error logging**: `logAppError()` (`js/core.js`) now also best-effort mirrors its capped local error list to a new `error_reports/{uid}` Firestore doc (rate-limited to once per 30s), so a crash on a real device is visible via the Firebase console without a screenshot report. New `error_reports/{uid}` firestore.rules match block, emulator-verified (8 new cases).
  2. **PWA shortcuts + Web Share Target**: `manifest.json` gained a "Нова операція" home-screen shortcut and a GET-based `share_target`; both handled by `js/app-init.js`'s new `handleLaunchParams()`. New `tests/pwa-launch-params.mjs`.
  3. **WCAG pass**: raised all 46 remaining sub-12px `font-size` declarations to 12px (verified via a horizontal-overflow scan across Finance/Shifts/Debt/Settings at 390px, both themes, not just eyeballed). Recomputed the prior accessibility pass's "left out" touch-target list against the real WCAG 2.2 AA floor (24×24px, not the 44px Apple HIG figure it had mistakenly used) — only `.subchip` delete button actually failed; fixed via an asymmetric hit-slop pseudo-element.
  4. **CSV import** (`js/analytics-csv.js`): round-trips `exportTransactionsCSV()`'s own dialect back in, columns matched positionally (not by localized header text), each row revalidated through the same `validateTransactionDraft()` a manual add uses. New `upload` icon glyph (none existed). New `tests/csv-import-export.mjs`.
  5. **On-device AI category suggestion** (`js/finance.js`'s `maybeSuggestCategoryWithAI()`): Chrome's Prompt API (`self.LanguageModel`), feature-detected, on-device, no network/API-key/cost. Keyword rules always win; comments under 8 chars never trigger a call; the model's answer is only applied if it exactly matches a real category name. New `tests/ai-category-suggestion.mjs` stubs `self.LanguageModel` via `page.addInitScript`.
  6. **Decorative glow/gradient**: investigated before touching anything — found a prior session had already done deliberate per-theme shadow/glow tuning (a whole "3-tier surface system" with its own light-theme retune batch), so the audit's "too much 2023-2024-style glow" finding mostly didn't hold up. Scoped down to the one real complaint (ripple+pop+glow firing at once on tab tap): trimmed only `--tab-glow-ripple-alpha` (.42→.34 dark, .24→.19 light), left the persistent glow and every gradient token alone.
  7. **Firebase App Check**: provisioned fully from this sandbox via REST calls under `claude-deploy@maxtr-c238f.iam.gserviceaccount.com` (no `gcloud` installed here) — confirmed `recaptchaenterprise.googleapis.com`/`firebaseappcheck.googleapis.com` already enabled, self-granted `roles/recaptchaenterprise.admin` + `roles/firebaseappcheck.admin` (kept permanently, same as this SA's other standing infra roles), created a reCAPTCHA Enterprise SCORE key (`projects/311094677098/keys/6LdDGlctAAAAAB3lX0HQS9ao_B4Bn8w0O_KFJDYk`) scoped to `maxtr-c238f.web.app`/`maxtr-c238f.firebaseapp.com`/`sudak666.github.io`, registered it with the web app's App Check config. Hit the usual IAM-propagation-delay gotcha (first `recaptchaEnterpriseConfig` PATCH 403'd, succeeded ~45s later with no other change). `js/core.js` now calls `initializeAppCheck()` right after `initializeApp()`. **Left both Firestore's and Auth's enforcement at `UNENFORCED`** (checked live) — a deliberate monitor-first rollout; SETUP.md §8 documents the one remaining manual step (flip to Enforced after checking the App Check metrics tab). Chased down every one of this repo's 14 stubbed-Firebase Playwright tests needing a matching `firebase-app-check.js` stub, or the whole module graph fails to load and every test hangs on a blank lock-screen.
  8. **Google Play launch checklist**: SETUP.md §9 — a sequential checklist (account creation → App content → store listing → the existing PWABuilder rebuild recipe → internal testing → production) for the one part that genuinely needs the account owner (the $25 fee + identity verification, which no agent session can do).
  9. **Shared profiles** — the largest, highest-risk item: a second Firebase Auth account can be invited (short-lived single-use code) to read/write one of this account's existing profiles. Reuses the existing `users/{uid}/max_tracker/{doc}@{profileId}` tree (no parallel data model) via a new `AppState.activeProfileOwnerUid` that `userDoc()`/`lsKey()` redirect through. Membership lives in a new `shared_members@{profileId}` doc; joining is a genuine two-step rules-enforced sequence (redeem the invite first, only then can `shared_members` be joined, verified via a `get()` on the now-used invite) — verified this whole design against a real local Firestore emulator with three standalone probe scripts *before* writing any client code, confirming dynamic `get()` paths built via string concatenation, `arrayUnion`/`arrayRemove` resolution in `request.resource.data`, and `list.removeAll()` all actually work as assumed, none of it taken on faith. 25 new emulator-verified test cases cover the full invite→redeem→join→leave lifecycle plus every rejection path (unknown/used/expired/own-profile code, can't remove someone else, delete stays owner-only, isolation from unrelated docs). New `tests/shared-profiles-ui.mjs` for the client wiring (single-stubbed-uid, so only proves a real code generates and both rejection paths show visible feedback — the security enforcement itself is the emulator suite's job). Deliberately out of scope for v1 (documented in CLAUDE.md, not oversights): no granular permissions, no push-sweep support for shared profiles yet (confirmed safe no-op), `notifSettings` is effectively shared too since it lives in the shared `finance` doc, no `shared_members`/`profile_invites` cleanup on account deletion.
  - **A latent test-hygiene bug found while re-running `tests/firestore-rules.mjs` twice in a row**: the local Firestore emulator process persists data across separate `node tests/firestore-rules.mjs` invocations (unlike CI, which spins up a fresh emulator every run), so a second local run saw the first run's `profile_invites` doc already `usedBy`-set and failed 4 single-use-code assertions for reasons that had nothing to do with `firestore.rules` itself. Fixed by adding `await testEnv.clearFirestore()` right after `initializeTestEnvironment()` — confirmed idempotent across 3 consecutive local runs afterward.
  - **A session-working-directory gotcha hit again, despite being previously logged**: after merging, ran `git checkout main` (a *local* branch that was still 113 commits behind, from before this session started) before `git fetch`+`git reset --soft origin/main` — `git checkout` to a stale local branch actually overwrites the working directory with that stale branch's old file contents (unlike `git reset --soft`, which only moves `HEAD`/the index and never touches the working tree). The subsequent `git reset --soft origin/main` then left `HEAD` pointing at the fully-merged new commit while the working directory still held the old pre-session files underneath it — caught immediately via `git status` showing a huge stale diff, fixed with `git checkout HEAD -- .` (syncs the working tree to whatever `HEAD` now points at) before anything got re-committed on top of the stale state. No actual data loss (the deploy itself was already done from a separate, correctly-checked-out `git worktree`, unaffected by this), but a reminder for next time: prefer `git fetch origin <default-branch> && git checkout -B <branch-name> origin/<default-branch>`-style patterns that never checkout a possibly-stale local branch name in between, exactly as CLAUDE.md's own merged-PR-follow-up guidance already says — this session just didn't follow it to the letter on the *return-to-main* step specifically (as opposed to the feature-branch-restart case it was written for).
  - **Verified**: full local suite — `unit`, `tx-validation`, `privacy-cache`, `functions-sweep` (all plain-node), plus all 15 stubbed-Firebase Playwright files (`smoke`, `e2e-crud`, `e2e-modals`, `stress-tx-list`, `tx-list-targeted-update`, `pull-to-refresh`, `tx-swipe-delete`, `debt-swipe-delete`, `tx-list-sort-order`, `sheet-drag-dismiss`, `csp-handlers`, `pwa-launch-params`, `csv-import-export`, `ai-category-suggestion`, `shared-profiles-ui`), plus `tests/firestore-rules.mjs` against a real local emulator (73/73, including all 33 new cases from items 1 and 9) — all green before the PR was opened. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped `rytm-v60`→`rytm-v64` across the session's several precached-asset changes (new `firebase-app-check.js` SDK module, `manifest.json` shortcuts/share_target, misc).
  - **Merged and deployed**: PR [#245](https://github.com/sudak666/Maxtr/pull/245), squash-merged as `89154dd` once both CI jobs (`smoke`, `firestore-rules`) went green. Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting,firestore:rules --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach` — succeeded first attempt ("found 48 files in .", 14 uploaded). No `functions` changes this session (App Check/IAM provisioning went through direct REST calls, not a Cloud Function deploy), so functions weren't redeployed. GitHub Pages mirror auto-deploys on push to `main`. Local feature branch and deploy worktree cleaned up after (remote branch deletion is automatic, per repo setting).
- **Follow-up on PR #245's own left-open item, "централізований логер замість 35 порожніх catch"**: individually reviewed all 34 (one fewer than the original count — a `switchProfile()`-adjacent one got rewritten with real fallback logic during the shared-profiles work) empty `catch(e){}` blocks in `js/*.js` against the `logAppError()` mechanism PR #245 already built. Conclusion: none were masking a real bug — every one falls into localStorage/sessionStorage best-effort access, `setPointerCapture` in swipe gestures, timezone/context feature-detection, or an already-feature-guarded `navigator.vibrate()`. No code changed; documented the categorization and the "new catches should call `logAppError()` unless they're genuinely one of these four categories" convention directly in CLAUDE.md so this doesn't need re-deriving next time an audit flags empty catches. Docs-only, no deploy needed.
- **Real-device console-error triage (found by the account owner)**: three console errors reported from a real browser session against the deployed PR #245 build. Of the three, only one was fixable from this repo's code: `Manifest: Enctype should be set to either application/x-www-form-urlencoded or multipart/form-data` — `manifest.json`'s new `share_target` (PR #245) didn't set `enctype` explicitly; Chrome's manifest linter flags this even for GET-method share targets where it isn't functionally required. Added `"enctype": "application/x-www-form-urlencoded"` (the correct default for GET). The other two are not app bugs: `requestStorageAccess: Permission denied` on a URL containing the reCAPTCHA Enterprise site key is App Check's own script attempting third-party storage access and being denied by the browser's storage-partitioning policy — expected, non-fatal, reCAPTCHA still scores without it; two `POST .../firestore.googleapis.com ... net::ERR_BLOCKED_BY_CLIENT` are Chrome's own error code for "blocked by a browser extension" (an ad-blocker/privacy extension on that specific device), not a server or app-side failure. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped `rytm-v64`→`rytm-v65` so already-installed PWAs pick up the corrected manifest.
- **Duplicate × in the Finance transaction search field (found by the account owner via screenshot, 2026-07-17)**: `#tx-search-input` is `type="search"` and already has its own custom `.search-clear-btn` (`data-action="clear-tx-search"`) rendered right next to it — Chrome/Safari also render their own native ×-in-a-circle clear button for any `type="search"` input once it has text, so both showed at once, stacked together. Fixed with a single scoped rule: `#tx-search-input::-webkit-search-cancel-button{-webkit-appearance:none;appearance:none}` (`index.html`). Deliberately scoped to this one input's `id`, not a blanket rule for every `type="search"` field — `#settings-search-input` has no custom clear button of its own and still needs the native one to remain clearable. Verified visually with a scratch Playwright script (stubbed-Firebase recipe, seeded a transaction, typed into the search field, screenshotted a crop around the input) confirming only one × renders post-fix; no existing test references `tx-search`, so no test file needed updating. `node tests/smoke.mjs` re-run green. Committed directly to `main` (`e5ced73`) and deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach` — succeeded first attempt, "found 48 files in .", 1 uploaded. No `firestore.rules`/`functions` changes. GitHub Pages mirror auto-deploys on push to `main`.
- **Receipt scanning (OCR) — a new feature request from the account owner (2026-07-17), asked about after reading it as an item in the original audit's competitor-comparison section (it was never part of the audit's own prioritized 9-item roadmap already shipped in PR #245).** Full design/implementation/verification/deploy writeup lives in CLAUDE.md's new "Receipt scanning (OCR)" section — summary here:
  - Self-hosted **Tesseract.js** (WASM OCR) under `js/vendor/tesseract/` (~9MB: library + WASM core + uk/en language packs), since the app's CSP has no CDN allowance Tesseract.js's own defaults rely on. Pulled via `npm pack` (registry.npmjs.org reachable from this sandbox; jsdelivr/unpkg are not).
  - New `js/receipt-ocr.js` (`parseReceiptText()` — pure, zero-import text parsing; `scanReceiptImage()` — the actual OCR call), wired into `js/finance.js`'s new-transaction form via a "Сканувати чек" button (hidden for transfers) that opens the device camera/photo picker and prefills amount + date on success, never blocking manual entry on failure.
  - `firebase.json` CSP gained one addition, `'wasm-unsafe-eval'` on `script-src` (required for `WebAssembly.instantiate()` under a strict CSP; does not enable JS `eval`). No other CSP directive needed changing.
  - **Verified twice, deliberately**: a real (non-stubbed) end-to-end OCR run against a synthetic receipt image, under the actual deployed CSP header, via Playwright — this caught two real things a written-in-advance unit test wouldn't have: (1) confirmed the self-hosted worker/WASM/CSP chain genuinely works, and (2) found and fixed a real amount-extraction bug (the fallback "largest number in the text" heuristic was picking up the year from the receipt's own date, e.g. `2026` from `16.07.2026`, over the real total) — fixed by masking the matched date span before amount extraction and preferring decimal-formatted numbers over bare integers in the fallback. Also discovered via the real run that the vendored `tesseract-core-lstm.wasm` binary (2.8MB) is dead weight — the `.wasm.js` wrapper already embeds it as base64 and never fetches the separate file — deleted it, cutting the vendored footprint from ~12MB to ~9MB.
  - New tests: `tests/receipt-ocr-parse.mjs` (13 plain-node cases for `parseReceiptText()`, including the date-vs-amount regression above) and `tests/receipt-scan-ui.mjs` (stubs the one dynamic-`import()` boundary, `js/vendor/tesseract/tesseract.esm.min.js`, via `page.route()`, then exercises the real button/file-input/prefill wiring against a fake OCR backend). The UI test needed `browser.newContext({serviceWorkers:'block'})` — the first test in this suite whose stubbed fetch happens late enough (after a user interaction, not immediately on page load) to lose the race against `sw.js`'s `clients.claim()`, which otherwise intercepts the request before Playwright's `page.route()` sees it and silently loads the real ~9MB library instead of the stub. Both added to `.github/workflows/smoke-test.yml`.
  - `sw.js`: `js/receipt-ocr.js` added to `STATIC_ASSETS` (it's a static import in the core module graph, same as every other `js/*.js` file); `js/vendor/tesseract/*` deliberately left out of `STATIC_ASSETS` (only reached via a dynamic import when a user actually scans a receipt — eagerly precaching ~9MB on every install for an opt-in feature most sessions won't touch would be wasteful) and instead caches opportunistically via the existing same-origin cache-first fetch handler. `CACHE_NAME` bumped `rytm-v65`→`rytm-v66`.
  - **Verified**: full local suite — `unit`, `tx-validation`, `privacy-cache`, `receipt-ocr-parse` (new), plus every stubbed-Firebase Playwright file including `receipt-scan-ui` (new) — all green, run individually rather than batched (a batched run hit the harness's own timeout, not a test failure — confirmed by re-running the slow ones standalone). `node --check` on every `js/*.js` file including the two new ones. `firestore.rules` untouched, so the emulator suite wasn't re-run.
  - **Committed directly to `main`** (no PR — matching this session's direct-to-main pattern for the tx-search fix above) and deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach`.
- **Real-device follow-up fix for receipt scanning, reported by the account owner within hours of the feature shipping (2026-07-17)**: on an actual phone, the scan opened the camera and took the photo fine, but then never completed — the processing toast disappeared (its own normal 2.8s auto-hide, unrelated to whether OCR had actually finished) and the button stayed stuck disabled, requiring a full tab close/reopen to use again. Full root-cause writeup in CLAUDE.md's "Receipt scanning (OCR)" section; summary: a real phone photo (3000-4000px, several MB) is a very different input from this repo's small synthetic test image, and feeding it straight into the WASM OCR core is a known way to make Tesseract.js hang on a memory-constrained mobile browser with no catchable error. Fixed with three changes in `js/receipt-ocr.js`/`js/finance.js`: (1) `downscaleImage()` resizes any photo above 1800px on the long side before OCR runs — verified for real against a synthetic 3024×4032 image, confirmed actual downscaling to 1350×1800 and correct recognition in ~20s total; (2) the scan button's own label now stays swapped to "processing" for the whole duration instead of relying on the transient toast as the only feedback; (3) a hard 45s timeout wraps the whole OCR call as a defensive backstop regardless of root cause, so a genuinely stuck call now recovers the UI on its own (button re-enables, dedicated timeout toast) instead of needing a reload — verified for real with a temporarily-shortened timeout and a stubbed hung-forever `recognize()`. Added `tests/receipt-scan-ui.mjs`'s 4th case (fast ~1s regression test for the timeout-recovery path, using a new optional `timeoutMs` param on `scanReceiptImage()` that production code never passes). `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped `rytm-v66`→`rytm-v67`. Verified: `receipt-ocr-parse` (unchanged, still 13/13), `receipt-scan-ui` (now 4/4), `smoke`, `node --check` on all touched files. Committed directly to `main` and deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach`.
- **Blank white circle in push notifications, found by the account owner via screenshot (2026-07-17)**: both `js/notifications.js`'s local notifications and `sw.js`'s FCM `onBackgroundMessage` handler set `badge: 'icon-192.png'` — but `icon-192.png` is a fully opaque RGB image with **no alpha channel at all** (confirmed via Pillow: `im.mode == 'RGB'`, not `RGBA`). Android renders a notification's `badge` using *only* its alpha channel as a white silhouette, ignoring color entirely — fed a fully-opaque image, it rendered the whole icon as one solid white blob with no visible shape, exactly matching the screenshot. Generated a proper badge asset, `badge-96.png` — a real alpha-transparent white bell glyph (rendered from the same SVG path data as the in-app `bell` icon via `cairosvg`, at 96×96, confirmed via Pillow that ~73% of pixels are fully transparent and the rest fully opaque white) — and pointed both `badge:` call sites at it instead. The large `icon` field (the actual per-notification-type themed image on the right of the tray, `NOTIF_ICONS` in `functions/index.js`) was already correct and untouched — only the small badge glyph was broken. `sw.js`'s `STATIC_ASSETS` gained `badge-96.png`; `CACHE_NAME` bumped `rytm-v67`→`rytm-v68`. The screenshot's *second* arrow (pointing at the `maxtr-c238f.web.app` origin text shown next to "Rytm" in the notification header) is **not fixable from app code** — this is Chrome/Android's own trust-indicator label for web-push notifications (so a malicious site can't impersonate a different origin's notifications), with no Notification API or manifest option to suppress it; it will only stop appearing once the app is a genuinely installed Android app via a published TWA (see the Android/Google Play packaging section — not done yet, no Play Console account created). Verified: `smoke`, `functions-sweep`, `node --check` on both touched JS files. Committed directly to `main` and deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach`.
- **Real production bug found while investigating a follow-up screenshot (2026-07-18): the live `notificationSweep` Cloud Function had been sending push notifications titled "Zminka" for two days after the app was renamed to "Rytm".** The account owner shared a screenshot asking about the badge-icon circle color (see entry above); its notification body incidentally showed the title `Zminka`, which no longer exists anywhere in the current source (`grep -rni zminka` across `js/*.js`/`functions/*.js` returns nothing) — so this wasn't a code bug, it was a **stale deploy**. Root-caused via `git log --oneline a60e359..HEAD -- functions/` (empty — zero commits touched `functions/` since the rename commit) plus reading that rename's own merge/deploy log entry in `CHANGELOG.md`, which explicitly reasoned *"functions/ changes are comment/string-only too, so no separate `firebase deploy --only functions` was needed"* — **that reasoning was wrong**. `git show a60e359 -- functions/lib/sweep.js` shows the actual diff: `sendPushFn(token, 'Zminka', ...)` → `sendPushFn(token, 'Rytm', ...)` in two places (the per-profile and consolidated-multi-profile daily reminder) — a real string-literal change to the exact text every daily-reminder push displays as its title, not a comment. Since Cloud Functions run whatever was last *deployed*, not the current git `HEAD`, the live function kept sending `'Zminka'` for every daily reminder from 2026-07-16 (the rename) through 2026-07-18 (this fix) — two full days of incorrectly-branded push notifications to real users. **Fixed by simply redeploying** (`cd functions && npm install && firebase deploy --only functions --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach`) — no source change needed, since the repo's `functions/` content was already correct; both `notificationSweep` and `privatRates` updated successfully on the first attempt. **Lesson, now added to CLAUDE.md's Commands section**: a Hosting-only deploy decision must be based on whether `functions/` content actually changed (checked via diff, not assumed from a commit message's framing like "rename"/"cosmetic"), because Cloud Functions deploys are a separate, easy-to-forget target from Hosting, and a stale function can silently keep serving old behavior — including user-facing strings — for however long nobody notices. No test added for this specific class of gap (it's a deploy-process error, not a code defect this repo's test suite could realistically have caught), but worth checking `git log <last-known-functions-deploy-commit>..HEAD -- functions/` before assuming "no functions changes this session" in any future session, rather than trusting an earlier session's own claim.
- **Redrew `notif-icon-daily.png` to match the app's own bell glyph, prompted directly by the account owner ("а ось ці точно можна поміняти ти ж їх робив" — but these can definitely be changed, you made them yourself, 2026-07-18)**: after confirming the badge-circle color and origin text are OS-controlled (see entries above), the account owner pointed at the large purple bell icon shown twice in their screenshot — a real self-made asset, not a system element. Compared it against `ICON_PATHS.bell` (the in-app SVG glyph, also what `badge-96.png` uses) and found a real inconsistency: the original hand-drawn bell was a different, flatter shape (flat bottom edge + separate circle) than the rounded stroke-based bell used everywhere else in the app. Regenerated it via the same `cairosvg` recipe as `badge-96.png` — identical bell path, white stroke, on the existing purple gradient background (sampled from the original file, `#854bef`→`#9d79f7`, so the background itself didn't need to change). `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped `rytm-v68`→`rytm-v69`. Only `notif-icon-daily.png` touched — the other 3 themed icons (`-budget`/`-recurring`/`-debt`) weren't part of what was shown/asked about this time. No `functions/` change needed (the Cloud Function only references the image's URL path, Hosting serves the actual bytes) — deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach`. Committed directly to `main`.
- **Redrew the other 3 themed push icons (`-budget`/`-recurring`/`-debt`) to match, immediate follow-up in the same session (2026-07-18)**: same inconsistency the daily bell had — each was a custom solid-fill glyph rather than the stroke-based style used everywhere else in the app. Regenerated all three via the identical `cairosvg` recipe/gradient, using the exact `ICON_PATHS.warning`/`.repeat`/`.bank` path data from `js/classic-globals.js`. - **Supersampled the 4 notification icons + badge for smoother lines, and added a subtle drop shadow for depth, per the account owner's direct request ("зроби їх трішки детальними з чіткими гладкими лініями", 2026-07-18)**: the flat 192×192/96×96 `cairosvg` render had visibly jagged stroke edges when zoomed in (confirmed by cropping the rendered PNG, not just glancing at the thumbnail). - **Two precision fixes on the notification icons, spotted by the account owner via a zoomed-in annotated screenshot (2026-07-18)**: (1) `notif-icon-recurring.png`'s two arrowheads were each 1 SVG-unit misaligned from their shaft's actual endpoint — invisible at the ~24px in-app size this path data was designed for, but a visibly stray line poking past the arrowhead once rendered at 192px with anti-aliasing + a drop shadow. - **Implemented the two remaining "deliberately out of scope for v1" shared-profiles gaps, at the account owner's direct request (2026-07-18)**: granular permissions (editor/viewer roles) and push-notification-sweep support for shared profiles. Full design writeup in CLAUDE.md's two new sections ("Granular permissions on shared profiles" / "Push notification support for shared profiles"); summary here:
  - **Granular permissions**: `shared_members` gained a `roles` map (`{uid:'editor'|'viewer'}`, absent = editor, so the rollout needed no migration). Real enforcement is in `firestore.rules` — new `memberRole()`/`isEditorMember()` helpers gate every write branch on the main doc and the transactions subcollection; `isSharedMember()` alone (any role) still gates read, extended to also cover reading `shared_members` itself (so a member's client can look up its own role). 17 new emulator-verified cases in `tests/firestore-rules.mjs` (now 90 total) — freshly-joined defaults to editor, owner downgrades to viewer, viewer rejected on every write path, viewer can still read/leave.
  - Client: `AppState.activeProfileRole` loaded via `loadActiveProfileRole()` on `switchProfile()` and at cold-init; `canEditActiveProfile()` (`js/core.js`) guards the primary mutating entry points (`addTransaction`/`deleteTransaction`, `saveModalSelection`, `addDebtEntry`/`deleteDebtEntry`) with an immediate read-only toast; `applyProfileReadOnlyUI()` hides every "add transaction/payment" entry point via a `body.profile-readonly` CSS class — caught and fixed a real gap during testing: the Finance quick-actions row has its *own* separate "+" tile sharing the same `open-new-tx-modal` action as the FAB, initially missed by a `.fin-fab`-only CSS selector; switched to matching by `data-action` instead, which covers both. New **"Учасники" (Members) manager** (`#shared-members-modal`, `js/color-picker.js`) lets the owner see members (shown by shortened uid — no cross-account display-name lookup exists) and toggle each one's role, following the same list-manager pattern as wallets/categories/tags rather than a single-shot dialog, since a per-row toggle action genuinely needs it. New `tests/shared-profile-permissions.mjs` (client-wiring level, added to CI): members manager shows correct default/stored roles and toggling updates the list; a viewer's client loads the right role, gets the readonly class, has every add-entry-point hidden, and — simulating a bypassed UI via a direct function call — still gets blocked with a read-only toast rather than attempting a doomed write.
  - **Push notifications**: `functions/lib/sweep.js`'s `sweepToken()` used to always read `users/{token holder's own uid}/...` for every profile in `profiles_meta.list`, which doesn't exist for a shared profile someone else owns — a member enabling push silently never got reminders for one (safe no-op via existing `financeSnap.exists` guards, not broken, just incomplete). Fixed by resolving a `dataOwnerByProfile` map (the entry's `ownerUid` for a `kind:'shared'` entry, the token holder's own uid otherwise) before the "other profiles" parallel-fetch block, and threading a new `dataOwnerUid` parameter through `sweepProfile()` (default `= uid`, so no existing call site needed to change). No `firestore.rules` change needed — the Admin SDK bypasses rules entirely, only *which path* is read changed. 2 new `tests/functions-sweep.mjs` cases (now 30), each constructing the token holder's own profile with deliberately different data so a regression back to the same-uid-only read path would fail loudly, not coincidentally pass.
  - **Verified**: full local suite — `unit`, `tx-validation`, `privacy-cache`, `receipt-ocr-parse`, `functions-sweep` (30/30), plus every stubbed-Firebase Playwright file including the new `shared-profile-permissions` (5/5) — all green, run individually rather than batched (harness timeout on a full batch, not a test failure). `tests/firestore-rules.mjs` against a real local emulator, 90/90. `node --check` on every touched `js/*.js` and `functions/` file, plus `sw.js`'s own `new Function(...)` parse check. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped `rytm-v72`→`rytm-v73` (many `js/*.js` files + `index.html` changed content, no new files added to `STATIC_ASSETS`).
  - **Deployed all three targets**: `firebase deploy --only firestore:rules,functions,hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach` (functions needed `cd functions && npm install` first). Committed directly to `main`.

- **New app icon design, supplied directly by the account owner (2026-07-18)**: a glossy 3D-rendered purple squircle (wallet/calendar-grid motif). Delivery took a few attempts — pasted images in chat never landed as an accessible file in this sandbox (no `/root/.claude/uploads/...` path materialized, unlike earlier screenshots in the same session that worked fine via that path), so the account owner committed the two source PNGs (512×512 and 192×192, both already correctly sized, fully opaque/no alpha) directly to the GitHub repo instead, which this session then pulled via `git fetch`/`git pull`. Overwrote `icon-192.png`/`icon-512.png` as-is (the maskable-purpose pair — the new render already has generous padding around the glyph, safely inside any reasonable maskable safe-zone) and regenerated the three "-rounded" derivatives (`icon-192-rounded.png`/`icon-512-rounded.png`/`android-icon-rounded.png`) via the same 20%-corner-radius Pillow squircle-mask recipe documented in CLAUDE.md's Android packaging section. Every reference in the codebase (`apple-touch-icon` in `index.html`/`landing.html`, `manifest.json`'s 4 icon entries + shortcut icon, `sw.js`'s notification-icon fallback and `STATIC_ASSETS`) is by filename only, so overwriting in place needed zero code changes — confirmed by grep before touching anything. Deleted the two temporary source-upload PNGs from the repo root after processing (they were only a delivery vehicle, not meant to stay). `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped `rytm-v73`→`rytm-v74`. Verified: `node -e "new Function(...)"` syntax check on `sw.js`, `tests/smoke.mjs` green, visual before/after preview of all 5 icon variants. Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach`. Committed directly to `main`.
- **Enlarged the new icon's content within its frame, per direct feedback ("щось мені не дуже подобається замалий малюнок на чорному фоні", 2026-07-18)**: measured the actual glyph bounding box against the background color (`numpy`, thresholded pixel-diff from a corner sample) rather than eyeballing — the icon content only filled ~63-67% of the canvas, leaving a wide dark margin on all sides. Fixed by cropping to that bounding box (with a small buffer so soft shadow/reflection edges aren't clipped) and re-scaling so the content fills ~86% of the canvas, re-centered on the same background color — done from the existing source files already in the repo, no new upload needed this time. Verified at both full size and small (48/72/96px) simulated home-screen scale before committing. Regenerated the three `-rounded` derivatives from the new, larger-content base images via the same squircle-mask recipe. `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped `rytm-v74`→`rytm-v75`. - **Fixed scattered action-icon layout on non-active Profiles-manager rows, reported via a mobile screenshot with an arrow (2026-07-18, "дивись як там розкидані іконки олівець, корзина, чи то так треба?")**: the account owner's second (non-active) profile row showed its "Учасники"/pencil/trash icon buttons split across two different lines instead of sitting together — reproduced and confirmed with a real before/after Playwright screenshot + bounding-box dump at the 390px mobile viewport this repo standardizes on, not just read from the CSS. Root cause: `renderProfilesUI()` (`js/color-picker.js`) renders up to three sibling `.mgr-del`-classed buttons directly into `.mgr-row` (a `display:flex;flex-wrap:wrap` container) for a non-active own profile — the shared `.mgr-del` class carries `margin-left:auto` (correct for every *other* manager row in the app, which only ever has one `.mgr-del`), so each of the three buttons independently claimed the row's remaining space and, combined with the wider "Перемкнути" switch button that only renders on non-active rows (vs. the active row's more compact "АКТИВНИЙ" `<span>`), the row ran out of width and `flex-wrap` split the group apart mid-icon rather than keeping it together. Fixed by wrapping the three action buttons in a new `.profile-row-actions` container (`display:flex;flex-wrap:nowrap;gap:2px`) that alone carries `margin-left:auto`, with `.profile-row-actions .mgr-del{margin-left:0}` so the nested buttons no longer compete for space — this is scoped narrowly to the profiles row (the only row in the app with more than one `.mgr-del` per row, confirmed by grepping every `.mgr-del` render call site) so every other manager's single-icon row is untouched. Now the three icons always stay together as one visual group, wrapping to their own line as a unit on narrow rows/long names instead of splitting mid-group. Verified with the same before/after screenshot+bounding-box technique (`row 0` icons went from `top:358` / `top:417` split to all three at the same `top` after the fix) plus `tests/shared-profiles-ui.mjs` and `tests/shared-profile-permissions.mjs` (both still green — neither previously caught this, since neither asserts on row geometry). `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped `rytm-v75`→`rytm-v76`. Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach`. Committed directly to `main`.
- **New feature: "Скинути всі дані" (reset all data / start over), requested directly (2026-07-18, "зроби таку функцію типу скинути/стерти всі данні (почати спочатку)")**: a new red row in Settings → Акаунт, right above "Видалити акаунт". Clarified scope with the account owner before building (`AskUserQuestion`): resets **only the current profile's data**, not every profile on the account, and keeps the account/sign-in intact (distinct from `deleteAccountUser()`, which removes the account itself) — the account owner had no preference on the second point, so this session picked "keep signed in" as the more useful, less-destructive interpretation of "start over," matching that a dedicated "delete account" action already exists for the other case. Implemented as `resetProfileData()` (`js/auth.js`, right after `deleteAccountUser()`): behind a `uiConfirm(...,{danger:true})` gate (same friction level as account deletion), it `deleteDoc()`s the active profile's `shifts`/`finance`/`debt` docs plus every doc in the `transactions` subcollection (`deleteAllTransactionDocs()`, same helper `deleteAccountUser()` already uses), clears the matching per-profile localStorage cache keys, then calls the existing `fbLoadNow()` — which, finding nothing there, runs through `seedConfigFromDocs()`'s existing "no data" path and reseeds true defaults (`DEFAULT_WALLETS`/`DEFAULT_CATEGORIES`/`DEFAULT_SHIFT_TYPES`), exactly the same path a genuinely brand-new profile goes through. Deliberately reused that existing seeding logic instead of duplicating the default-field list by hand, so there's one source of truth for "what a fresh profile looks like." **Blocked entirely for a shared profile this account doesn't own** (`AppState.activeProfileOwnerUid` set) — refused with a toast before the confirm dialog even shows, since wiping a shared profile would destroy data the owner and other members depend on. New i18n keys (`settings_reset_data`/`_sub`, `profiles_reset_*`), a `refresh`-icon settings row (`#settings-reset-data`, toggled visible/hidden alongside the sign-out/delete-account rows in `onAuthStateChanged`), and a `reset-profile-data` `CLICK_ACTIONS` entry. New test `tests/reset-profile-data.mjs` (3 scenarios, all against the stubbed-Firestore-no-rules recipe used by the other shared-profile tests): confirming wipes the finance doc back to the 2 default wallets and deletes the seeded transaction doc; cancelling the confirm dialog leaves a custom wallet untouched; a non-owned shared profile is refused with a toast and the owner's doc is provably untouched — wired into CI (`smoke-test.yml`). `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped `rytm-v76`→`rytm-v77` (no new files added to `STATIC_ASSETS` — only existing `js/auth.js`/`js/classic-globals.js`/`index.html` changed). Verified: `node --input-type=module --check` on the 3 touched `js/*.js` files, `tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/shared-profiles-ui.mjs`, `tests/shared-profile-permissions.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs`, and the new test — all green. Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach`. Committed directly to `main`.
- **New feature: Monobank integration, requested directly (2026-07-18, "давай спробуємо зробити Монобанк привязати")**: "Прив'язати Monobank" in Settings → Фінанси (right after Гаманці) links a user's real Monobank cards/jars and pulls their transactions in. This was architecturally significant enough (a new public Cloud Function endpoint, a live bank credential to store, Monobank's hard rate limit) to clarify scope with the account owner via `AskUserQuestion` before writing any code — see CLAUDE.md's new "Monobank integration" section (under Firebase data model) for the full design, kept here to just the headline decisions and what shipped:
  - **Manual "Синхронізувати" button** (account owner's explicit choice over an automatic real-time webhook) — simpler, no public always-listening endpoint to register/maintain; a webhook is a documented possible future upgrade, not built now.
  - **Links every card and jar on the token at once** (account owner's explicit choice over a per-account picker) — connecting auto-creates one new wallet per Monobank account/jar.
  - **New Cloud Function `monobankProxy`** (`functions/index.js`, exposed via a new `"/api/monobank"` Hosting rewrite) — `api.monobank.ua` never sends CORS headers (identical root cause to the existing `privatRates` proxy), so the browser can't call it directly; this proxy relays `client-info`/`statement` calls server-side, attaching the caller-supplied `X-Monobank-Token` header. Unlike `privatRates` (public data), this endpoint first requires a valid Firebase ID token (`firebase-admin`'s `getAuth().verifyIdToken()`) so it can't be used as an anonymous relay by a stranger who finds the URL. Query-building/window-validation logic split into `functions/lib/monobank.js` (unit-tested, `tests/monobank-proxy.mjs`, 10 cases) for the same reason `lib/pure.js`/`lib/sweep.js` are split out.
  - **Client**: new `js/monobank.js` (17th `js/` module, wired into `js/app.js`'s init sequence). The token + linked accounts + `monobankAccountId→walletId` mapping + `lastSyncAt` live in a new `AppState.integrations.monobank` field, synced inside the existing `finance` doc (`fbSaveNow()`/`seedConfigFromDocs()` in `js/color-picker.js`, plus the local `mx_cfg_*` cache mirror) — no new Firestore doc kind, no `firestore.rules` change needed, same per-uid protection as everything else in that doc.
  - **Rate-limit handling**: Monobank allows at most 1 request per 60 seconds per token, *across the whole API*, not per-endpoint — every call this module makes (connect or sync, any account) is paced ≥61s apart (`paceMonobankRequest()`), and a long statement range is chunked into ≤31-day windows (Monobank's own hard cap on that endpoint). A multi-account sync can genuinely take minutes; `#monobank-sync-status` shows live "Синхронізую рахунок N/M…" text so this doesn't read as a hung UI.
  - **Dedup by Monobank's own stable entry id** (stored as `monobankId` on the created transaction) — re-syncing an overlapping date range (which happens on every sync after the first) never creates duplicates. `hold:true` (pending/not-yet-settled) entries are skipped. Category comes from the same keyword auto-rules a manual add already applies (`findMatchingRule()`, exported from `js/finance.js` for this reuse), falling back to `"Інше"` — no MCC-code mapping in v1. No "transfer" detection between two of the user's own linked accounts (shows as a separate expense+income pair) — same simplification the existing CSV import already makes.
  - **Testing**: `tests/monobank-proxy.mjs` (plain node, 10 cases — URL building, 31-day-window enforcement, malformed-query rejection) and `tests/monobank-connect.mjs` (full stubbed-Firebase Playwright recipe + a `page.route()` stub for `/api/monobank` itself, since this repo's test setup has no Functions emulator): connecting creates 2 wallets and shows the connected view with the real client name; first sync imports the non-hold entries from both accounts and skips the hold one; a second sync (after waiting past the 1-second `lastSyncAt` granularity) calls the API again but imports nothing new, proving dedup rather than "it never asked"; disconnecting hides the connected view without touching already-created wallets/transactions. A `setMonobankSyncGapMsForTesting()` export exists solely so the test doesn't wait through the real 61s pacing gap. Both wired into CI (`smoke-test.yml`).
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped `rytm-v77`→`rytm-v78` (`./js/monobank.js` added to `STATIC_ASSETS`, same as every other core `js/*.js` module).
  - **Verified**: `node --check`/`node --input-type=module --check` on every touched file, `tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs`, `tests/e2e-modals.mjs`, `tests/csv-import-export.mjs`, `tests/shared-profiles-ui.mjs`, `tests/unit.mjs`, `tests/tx-validation.mjs`, `tests/privacy-cache.mjs`, `tests/functions-sweep.mjs`, plus both new test files — all green.
  - **Deployed all relevant targets**: `firebase deploy --only functions,hosting --project maxtr-c238f` (no `firestore:rules` needed — no rules change) from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach` (functions needed `cd functions && npm install` first). Committed directly to `main`.
- **Fixed "Hide amounts" leaving several real amounts visible, reported via screenshot ("ще не всі суми приховані", 2026-07-18)**: the screenshot showed a Finance-tab Budgets widget with two rows fully readable ("1 620 / 50 000 грн", "0 / 300 грн") and one over-budget row in red ("5 228,58 / 5 000 грн") despite the hero balance/wallet chips above them already being blurred. Root cause: `body.amounts-hidden` (topbar `#btn-hide-amounts`) only blurs a fixed CSS-selector list, and `renderBudgets()`'s spent/limit text (`js/settings-managers.js`) had no class at all — never touched by that rule. Auditing every other `.toLocaleString('uk-UA')` money display in the app (not just the reported one) turned up 4 more of the same bug, all fixed the same way (new dedicated class + added to the `body.amounts-hidden` selector list in `index.html`): the Finance-tab Goals widget's saved/target amount (`js/goals-profile.js`), the Debt tab's payment-history amount/balance fields and the discrepancy hint (`js/debt.js` — see the note below on why these needed *new* classes rather than reusing the existing shared `.debt-field-view`/`.debt-field` classes), the payoff-forecast card's average-per-payment figure, and a cross-currency transfer's small "(123 USD)" target-amount note (`js/analytics-csv.js`). **Deliberately scoped to primary-dashboard displays** (Finance tab widgets, Debt tab) and not swept into every settings-modal-internal amount found in the same audit (Categories manager's per-category monthly total, Recurring manager's summary line, the rates/converter widgets already covered) — those need several deliberate taps into an already-opened settings drill-down to reach, a meaningfully lower shoulder-surfing exposure than the main dashboards, and some share a row class with non-money text in ways that would need more careful per-call-site class threading to fix safely; flagged to the account owner as a further-sweep opportunity if wanted, not silently left undone.
  - **The `.debt-field-view` class is shared by a debt entry's amount, balance, *and* date sub-fields** — blindly adding it to the blur list would also hide the date, which isn't money and would read as a new bug in the other direction. Gave the amount/balance fields their own additional class (`.debt-amount-val`, also reused for the forecast card's average figure) instead, leaving the shared class's date usage untouched. Documented as a durable convention in `CLAUDE.md`'s "UI conventions worth following" section, since this exact trap (a shared row/field class covering both money and non-money content) is easy to hit again with any future amounts-hidden addition.
  - New `tests/hide-amounts.mjs` (Playwright, seeds a budget/goal/debt-with-discrepancy/cross-currency-transfer scenario, toggles the button, asserts `getComputedStyle(el).filter` includes `blur` on all 6 newly-and-previously-covered selectors) — including a negative check that the debt entry's date field specifically stays unblurred, proving the fix didn't over-blur. Wired into CI (`smoke-test.yml`).
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped `rytm-v78`→`rytm-v79` (no new files added to `STATIC_ASSETS` — only existing `js/*.js`/`index.html` content changed).
  - **Verified**: `node --input-type=module --check` on every touched `js/*.js` file, `tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/e2e-crud.mjs`, `tests/csv-import-export.mjs`, and the new test — all green. Deployed via `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach`. Committed directly to `main`.
- **Vite bundler — Phase 1 (build tooling only, deliberately deploy-inert), following up on a direct conversation about code "professionalism"**: the account owner relayed feedback that the codebase "isn't written professionally" and asked what a real engineer would change if migration cost weren't a constraint. Answer given: TypeScript, a bundler, and a reactive rendering layer would each be real improvements, but a full rewrite of all three at once — mid Google Play review, with 25+ Playwright tests and two live deploy pipelines all built around the current no-build-step architecture — would be reckless. The account owner agreed via `AskUserQuestion` to start with the lowest-risk slice only (Vite, no TypeScript, no framework yet) and to keep deploying normally in the meantime. Given the size of even that slice, planned it properly (`EnterPlanMode`) before touching anything.
  - **The concrete bug class this targets**: `sw.js` hand-maintains `STATIC_ASSETS` (20 `js/*.js` module files) and `FIREBASE_SDK_ASSETS` (5 pinned gstatic URLs) as parallel manually-synced lists — this file's own history has repeated "forgot to add a new file" incidents. A bundler collapses the 20 tracked files into build-generated output, making that specific mistake structurally impossible once wired into the deploy pipeline (not yet done this phase — see below).
  - **New root `package.json`/`package-lock.json`/`vite.config.js`** (single devDependency, `vite`). `functions/` is untouched — already its own separate npm project.
  - **Scoped narrowly to bundling only the ES module graph** (`js/app.js` and its statically-imported files) — `vite.config.js` sets `build.rollupOptions.input` directly to `js/app.js`, **not** `index.html`. Tried the more obvious `index.html`-as-entry approach first and it silently fingerprinted/rewrote `<link rel="manifest">` and `<link rel="apple-touch-icon">` to root-absolute hashed paths (`/assets/manifest-<hash>.json`) — harmless on Firebase Hosting's root `/`, but would 404 on the GitHub Pages mirror served under `/Maxtr/`. That's a real deploy-pipeline decision (whether/how to hash the full static asset tree, how it interacts with Hosting's existing per-path `Cache-Control` headers) that belongs to a later phase together with actually wiring a deploy target, not something to bake in silently via a bundler default. Switching to a JS-only entry avoids Vite touching `index.html` (or any other file) at all.
  - **The 4 classic non-module scripts** (`theme-preinit.js`/`touch-active-fix.js`/`sw-register.js`/`classic-globals.js`) and **`js/vendor/tesseract/**`** are completely untouched by design — confirmed by inspecting the build output, not just assumed.
  - **Real gotcha found and fixed**: `js/receipt-ocr.js` (part of the bundled graph) dynamically `import()`s the vendored Tesseract library using a path *relative to its own module URL* (`./vendor/tesseract/tesseract.esm.min.js`). Bundled naively, Vite's default output directory (`dist/assets/`) sits at a different relative depth than the source `js/` folder, silently breaking that resolution — exactly the kind of regression `tests/receipt-scan-ui.mjs` exists to catch. Fixed two ways: added `/* @vite-ignore */` to that one `import()` call (so Vite treats it as an opaque runtime string and never tries to bundle the vendor library itself, matching how it's already deliberately excluded from `sw.js`'s precache list), and configured `rollupOptions.output.entryFileNames`/`chunkFileNames` to emit the bundle under `dist/js/` instead of Vite's default `dist/assets/`, preserving the depth the relative specifier depends on. A small `closeBundle` plugin (`fs.cpSync`, no extra dependency) copies `js/vendor/tesseract/**` verbatim into `dist/js/vendor/tesseract/**` to match, since it's never reached via a statically analyzable import.
  - **Verified the build is behaviorally equivalent, not just "builds without errors"**: inspected `dist/js/app-<hash>.js` directly and confirmed the 5 `https://www.gstatic.com/firebasejs/12.11.0/firebase-*.js` import specifiers came through byte-identical (every existing test's Firebase-stub strategy depends on intercepting these exact URLs via `page.route()`), and that the Tesseract dynamic-import specifier was preserved unrewritten. Then built a scratch verification tree (full copy of the current repo root, with only the `<script type="module" src="./js/app.js">` tag swapped to point at the built bundle) and ran the real Playwright suite against it: `tests/smoke.mjs`, `tests/receipt-scan-ui.mjs` (the OCR/vendor-import boundary specifically), `tests/e2e-crud.mjs` (real Firestore-subcollection write path through the bundled code), and `tests/csp-handlers.mjs` (loads under the actual deployed CSP header — matters because a strict `script-src` with no `unsafe-inline`/`eval` is exactly what a bundler can accidentally violate) — all 4 green. `tests/unit.mjs`/`tests/tx-validation.mjs` also re-run for a cheap baseline confirmation (unaffected by bundling, as expected).
  - **Deliberately deploy-inert this phase**: `firebase.json`'s `hosting.public` still points at `.` (source, unchanged), GitHub Pages' "Deploy from a branch" setting is untouched, and CI (`smoke-test.yml`) still runs against source, not `dist/`. `dist/` itself is gitignored, not committed. The live app (mid Google Play review) is completely unaffected by this PR. Follow-up phases (wiring one deploy target to actually build+serve `dist/`, regenerating `sw.js`'s precache lists from the build output, updating CI) are each their own explicitly-confirmed step in a later session — switching GitHub Pages specifically will also need a manual repo Settings → Pages toggle no available tool can perform.
  - No `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bump this session — nothing served to real users changed.
- **Vite bundler — Phase 2 (wire Firebase Hosting to serve the real build)**, direct follow-up to Phase 1 above, done in the same continued session with standing authorization to proceed without re-confirming each step ("продовжуй завжди без питань").
  - **New `scripts/build-site.mjs`** (run via `npm run build`, after `vite build`): turns `dist/` from "just the bundled JS" into a complete, deployable copy of the site. Walks the repo root and copies everything Firebase Hosting's `public` dir needs (mirroring `firebase.json`'s own `hosting.ignore` list, plus this repo's dev-only tooling and the 20 original `js/*.js` module-graph files, now superseded by the bundle) — then two surgical patches: `dist/index.html`'s one `<script type="module">` tag is rewritten to the real built bundle filename, and `dist/sw.js`'s `STATIC_ASSETS` list has its hand-maintained 20-file module-graph block replaced with that one bundle file, `CACHE_NAME` set to a content-hash-derived value (`rytm-dist-<hash>`) instead of a manually-bumped number. **This is the concrete payoff Phase 1 set out for**: the "forgot to add a new `js/*.js` file to `STATIC_ASSETS`" bug class this repo hit repeatedly is now structurally impossible for anything served via this path, since the list is generated from the actual build output, not hand-typed.
  - **Hit and fixed a real bug in the naive approach**: `fs.cpSync(ROOT, DIST, {recursive:true, filter})` refuses outright ("Cannot copy X to a subdirectory of self") to copy a directory into its own subdirectory even when a filter would exclude that subdirectory, since `dist/` lives inside the repo root. Replaced with a plain hand-rolled recursive walk (`readdirSync`/`copyFileSync`) applying the same exclusion filter, which has no such restriction.
  - **`firebase.json`'s `hosting.public` changed from `.` to `dist`** — this is the actual production-affecting change. `hosting.ignore`/`headers` left untouched: the ignore patterns now simply match nothing under `dist/` (already excluded by the build script), a harmless no-op; the `sw.js`/`/js/**` no-cache headers and the `.well-known/assetlinks.json` content-type override still match the same relative paths since `dist/`'s internal layout mirrors the source tree's.
  - **GitHub Pages deliberately left untouched** — still "Deploy from a branch: main/root", serving the raw unbundled source tree exactly as before. No tool available in this session can flip that repo Settings → Pages toggle to an Actions-based build, so the two live mirrors now intentionally diverge in *how* they're built (Firebase Hosting serves the Vite bundle, GitHub Pages serves the original 20 individual `js/*.js` files) while serving identical behavior — verified independently working, not assumed. Revisit if/when the account owner wants Pages on the same pipeline.
  - **CI deliberately left untouched too** (`smoke-test.yml` still runs the full suite against source, not `dist/`) — verification below found a concrete reason beyond just "keep this PR small": **3 test files (`monobank-connect.mjs`, `receipt-scan-ui.mjs`, `shared-profile-permissions.mjs`) use `page.evaluate(() => import('./js/state.js'))` (or `./js/monobank.js`/`./js/receipt-ocr.js`) as a way to reach into the live app's module-scoped singletons (`AppState`, etc.) for assertions** — this works against source because the browser's module cache returns the same already-loaded instance the app itself is using, but it structurally cannot work once those files no longer exist individually (superseded by the bundle). Confirmed this is a test-authoring-technique limitation, not a real app regression, by re-running the same 3 tests' *other* assertions (the ones driven through real UI clicks rather than direct module import) — all passed. Fixing this properly means giving those 3 tests a `window.__test_*`-style hook instead of reaching for a live import, which is real but separate follow-up work, not bundled into this PR. Until CI points at `dist/`, it remains the correctness check for the (unbundled) GitHub Pages mirror; `dist/`'s equivalence was instead verified by hand this session (next bullet).
  - **Verified by hand before deploying**: built `dist/` fresh, inspected it directly (manifest.json/icons/`.well-known/assetlinks.json`/privacy.html/terms.html/landing.html all present verbatim; `js/` has exactly the bundle + the 4 classic scripts + `vendor/tesseract/`, no stale individual module files), then ran the real Playwright suite against `dist/` itself (copying each test file into a temporary `dist/tests/` so its own `ROOT`-resolution logic pointed at the built site, cleaned up afterward — not committed): `smoke`, `e2e-crud`, `e2e-modals`, `stress-tx-list`, `tx-list-targeted-update`, `pull-to-refresh`, `tx-swipe-delete`, `debt-swipe-delete`, `tx-list-sort-order`, `sheet-drag-dismiss`, `csp-handlers` (needed a temporary copy of `firebase.json` into `dist/` for this one test's own CSP-header lookup, removed again after — `firebase.json` itself is never actually served, it's excluded by the build script same as source), `pwa-launch-params`, `csv-import-export`, `ai-category-suggestion`, `shared-profiles-ui`, `reset-profile-data`, `hide-amounts` — **17 tests fully green**. The 3 tests with the `import('./js/...')` limitation each failed only on that one internal-inspection assertion, with every other (UI-driven) assertion in the same file passing. Pure-Node tests that import individual source files directly (`unit.mjs`, `tx-validation.mjs`, etc.) weren't re-run against `dist/` — they test business logic unrelated to bundling and don't touch a served page at all; already confirmed passing against source in Phase 1 and nothing in Phase 2 touched their inputs.
  - **Deployed**: `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach` (needed `npm install && npm run build` first, now that Hosting serves `dist/` instead of the repo root directly).
  - **Codex automated review on the same PR flagged 3 real issues, all fixed and merged before the deploy above**: (1) `firebase.json` had no `hosting.predeploy` hook, so a deploy from a clean checkout would fail outright (`dist/` is gitignored, doesn't exist) or silently publish a stale local build if someone forgot `npm run build` first — added `"predeploy": ["npm install", "npm run build"]`. (2) `CACHE_NAME` was derived only from the JS bundle's own content hash, so a change to a precached-but-never-hashed static file (`manifest.json`, an icon, a notif badge — all copied verbatim, never renamed by Vite) without touching any JS would leave `sw.js`'s text byte-identical across two otherwise-different deploys; since browsers detect a new service worker purely by byte-comparing the registered script, an already-installed worker would never notice and would keep serving the stale asset forever. Fixed by hashing every locally-precached file's actual bytes (not just the bundle's filename hash) into `CACHE_NAME` — verified for real: touching only `manifest.json` and rebuilding changed `CACHE_NAME` even though the JS bundle hash didn't move. (3) CI never ran `npm run build`, so a PR could pass every check while the Vite bundle itself failed to build, or while `build-site.mjs`'s hand-maintained `MODULE_GRAPH_FILES` list drifted out of sync with `sw.js`'s actual `STATIC_ASSETS` (that specific mismatch already fails loud with a thrown error, but only at build/deploy time, not at PR-review time) — added an `npm ci && npm run build` step to `smoke-test.yml`.
  - **Real deploy, not simulated**: `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach`. The new `predeploy` hook ran automatically and correctly (`npm install` → 17 packages, `npm run build` → bundle + `dist/` site, both inside the deploy command itself, not a separate manual step) — confirms the Phase-2-Codex-fix #1 above actually works, not just reads correctly. 35 files uploaded, version finalized and released. Could not `curl` the live `maxtr-c238f.web.app` afterward to double-check headers/content directly — this sandbox's egress proxy blocks that host outright (documented previously in the Android/Google Play packaging section: `maxtr-c238f.web.app` itself, as opposed to Firebase's *API* endpoints, is one of the hosts this environment can't reach). The Firebase CLI's own "release complete" confirmation plus the extensive pre-deploy `dist/`-level Playwright verification (17 tests, previous entry) stand in as the correctness evidence for this session; a real-device/browser spot-check of the live site is still worth doing when next convenient.
  - `sw.js`'s `CACHE_NAME` as actually deployed: `rytm-dist-1dacddc01c84` (content-hash-derived, dist-only — distinct from the source tree's own `rytm-vNN` scheme, which is unchanged and still governs whatever GitHub Pages serves).
- **Vite bundler — Phase 3 (CI now also verifies the real Hosting artifact, not just source)**, continuing the same session ("продовжуй" / "поодовжуй" — standing authorization to keep going without re-confirming each step).
  - **New `dist-smoke` CI job** (`smoke-test.yml`): builds `dist/` (same `npm ci && npm run build` the `smoke` job already runs) and then runs `smoke.mjs`, `e2e-crud.mjs`, and `csp-handlers.mjs` directly against it (staged into a temporary `dist/tests/` so each test's own root-resolution logic points at the built site, same technique used for manual verification in Phase 1/2 — plus a temporary `dist/firebase.json` copy purely for `csp-handlers.mjs`'s own CSP-header lookup, CI-only, never part of a real build/deploy). Closes the gap Phase 2 explicitly flagged: before this, `dist/` — the artifact Firebase Hosting actually serves — was only checked by hand before each deploy, never automatically on every PR.
  - **Deliberately a targeted 3-test subset, not the full suite**, for the same reason Phase 2 didn't attempt the full switch: 3 other test files (`monobank-connect.mjs`, `receipt-scan-ui.mjs`, `shared-profile-permissions.mjs`) use `page.evaluate(() => import('./js/state.js'))`-style live-module inspection that only works when `js/*.js` files are served individually, not bundled into one file — rewriting those to use a proper test-only hook instead is real, separate work, not done this session. The 3 chosen here (page-load/tab-render, a real Firestore-subcollection write path, and real-CSP compliance) cover the highest-value regression surface for "does the bundled site actually work" without needing that rework.
  - Verified locally before pushing: ran the exact same 3 commands the new CI job runs, against a fresh `npm run build` output — all green.
- **Vite bundler — Phase 4 (close the last gap: full CI parity between source and the bundled Hosting artifact)**, same continuing session.
  - **New `window.__RYTM_TEST_HOOKS__`** (`js/app.js`, attached unconditionally after every `__init_X__()` call): `{ AppState, addTransaction, scanReceiptImage, setMonobankSyncGapMsForTesting }`. Replaces `page.evaluate(() => import('./js/state.js'))`-style live-module inspection in 3 test files (`monobank-connect.mjs`, `receipt-scan-ui.mjs`, `shared-profile-permissions.mjs`) — the thing Phase 2/3 both explicitly flagged as the one remaining structural incompatibility between this repo's tests and a bundled build (a dynamic import of an individual `js/*.js` file only resolves when that file is actually served on its own, which stops being true once it's inlined into one Vite chunk). Because the hook is attached the same way regardless of whether `js/app.js` ran as 20 separate files or 1 bundled chunk, all 3 tests now pass identically against source *and* `dist/` — verified both ways for each, not assumed.
  - **`dist-smoke` CI job expanded from 3 tests to the full 20-test browser suite** (every Playwright test except the pure-Node ones, which never touch a served page) — with the fix above, there was no longer a real reason to keep its coverage narrower than the `smoke` job's. Verified locally end to end: staged all 20 test files into a fresh `dist/tests/`, ran every one against a real `npm run build` output — all green.
  - This was genuinely the last open item from Phase 2/3's own "known gaps" list — `dist/` (what Firebase Hosting actually serves) now gets exactly the same automated coverage on every PR that source (what GitHub Pages serves) always has.
  - **Deployed**: `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach`, needed even though `window.__RYTM_TEST_HOOKS__` itself is inert for real users — the JS bundle's content genuinely changed (new export), and this repo has hit the exact "skipped a deploy because it looked like a no-op change" gotcha before (see the earlier `functions/lib/sweep.js` push-title incident in this file's history), so a real content change to `js/app.js` gets a real redeploy on principle, not a judgment call each time. `predeploy` ran automatically, 35 files uploaded, release complete. New bundle: `app-J4U2wlPg.js`, `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME`: `rytm-dist-a333c3276db7`.
- **TypeScript adoption — Phase 1 (gradual, JSDoc-based, zero runtime change)**, the natural followup to the Vite bundler work, same session ("продовжуй"). Full reasoning for going incremental rather than a big-bang `.ts` rewrite (converting 20 zero-type-annotation modules at once risks breaking `sw.js` precache paths, test stub URL matching, and dynamic imports all together) is now in `CLAUDE.md`'s new "TypeScript adoption" section under Architecture — this entry just records what shipped.
  - New `tsconfig.json` (`allowJs`, `checkJs:false` project-wide, `noEmit:true` — `tsc` here is purely a checking tool, Vite's esbuild still does the real build) + `typescript` devDependency + `npm run typecheck` script, wired into the `smoke` CI job right after the build step.
  - `js/tx-validation.js` is the first file opted in via `// @ts-check` — chosen as the lowest-risk possible starting point (zero imports, no `AppState`/DOM). Gained a `@typedef TransactionDraft` and `@param`/`@returns` JSDoc on `validateTransactionDraft()`; typechecks clean. Zero behavior change — JSDoc comments and the `@ts-check` pragma have no runtime effect at all, confirmed by re-running `tests/tx-validation.mjs` unchanged.
  - **Also caught up `CLAUDE.md` itself, which had drifted stale across all 4 Vite phases** — the Commands section still said "no root `package.json`, no bundler" and the CI/Hosting-deploy descriptions didn't mention `dist-smoke`, the `predeploy` hook, or the GitHub-Pages/Hosting build divergence at all, even though every one of those shipped and was logged here in `CHANGELOG.md`. Per this file's own stated convention ("promote a permanent fact into CLAUDE.md, don't leave it buried in the log") this should have happened phase-by-phase and didn't — fixed now in one pass rather than left compounding further. New "Build tooling (Vite bundler)" and "TypeScript adoption" subsections under Architecture are the durable record going forward.
  - Verified: `npm run typecheck` clean, `npm run build` unaffected, `tests/tx-validation.mjs` still green.
- **TypeScript Phase 1 deploy check**: rebuilt `dist/` from post-merge `main` and confirmed the bundle hash (`app-J4U2wlPg.js`, `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` `rytm-dist-a333c3276db7`) is byte-identical to what's already live from the Phase 4 deploy — Vite/esbuild strips comments (including the new `// @ts-check` pragma and JSDoc) during minification, so this PR's actual served output is unchanged. No Hosting redeploy needed — an evidence-based skip (diffed the real build output), not a "just a comment change" guess of the kind this file's own Cloud Function gotcha warns against.
- **Preact adoption — proof of concept**, the third and last piece of "doing this properly" following the Vite bundler and TypeScript work. Confirmed scope with the account owner via `AskUserQuestion` before starting (Preact specifically — smallest footprint, plain `h()` hyperscript API, no JSX — and a single small, isolated widget rather than a rewrite), then planned it properly (`EnterPlanMode`) given this is the first change to actual rendering behavior in the whole initiative. Full reasoning now lives in `CLAUDE.md`'s new "Preact adoption" section under Architecture — this entry records what shipped.
  - **Target: the Debt tab's payoff-forecast widget** (`renderDebtForecast()` in `js/debt.js`) — pure, read-only, one call site, previously an `innerHTML=` template-string SVG chart + pace text. Rewritten to build the same output via Preact's `h()`/`render()` (two new stateless functions, `DebtBurndownChart`/`DebtForecastText`), same function signature and computed values, zero other widgets touched.
  - **Real architectural constraint found during planning, not assumed away**: unlike Vite/TypeScript (build/check-time only), Preact is the app's first runtime dependency — a bare `import {h} from 'preact'` would resolve fine for the Vite-bundled `dist/` but throw `TypeError: Failed to resolve module specifier` on GitHub Pages, which serves `js/debt.js` unbundled straight from source (a static-import failure that's all-or-nothing, breaking the whole module graph on that live mirror). Fixed by vendoring Preact under `js/vendor/preact/preact.module.js` (same `npm pack` recipe already used for Tesseract), imported via a real relative path — resolves identically on both deploy targets, no CSP change needed (self-hosted, same-origin).
  - **Caught and fixed a real bug during verification, not just assumed the design was right**: since Preact's import is a genuine static one (not `@vite-ignore`d like Tesseract's dynamic import), Vite correctly inlines it into the single bundle chunk — but `scripts/build-site.mjs`'s general file copy also independently copied the vendored file into `dist/js/vendor/preact/` verbatim (redundant, unused dead weight) and the new `sw.js` `STATIC_ASSETS` line for it survived into `dist/sw.js` unchanged, which would have made that variant's `cache.addAll()` 404 on install in production (the file doesn't actually exist standalone in `dist/`, only inlined in the bundle) — caught by rebuilding and directly inspecting `dist/sw.js` and `dist/js/vendor/`, not assumed correct. Fixed with a new `ALWAYS_BUNDLED_VENDOR_DIRS` set in `build-site.mjs` (excludes the directory from the dist copy, strips its `STATIC_ASSETS` line) — extensible if a similar always-bundled vendor dependency is ever added later.
  - **New `tests/debt-forecast-chart.mjs`** (no prior test covered this widget) — asserts the widget stays hidden with <2 payments, the chart/pace text render correct values with enough signal, and specifically that the "done"/"no clear pace" text-only states leave zero stale `<strong>` elements behind from a previous render (the concrete regression a raw `innerHTML=` write into a Preact-managed container would cause — Preact's diff tracking desyncs from real DOM state if anything else writes into the same container). Wired into both `smoke` and `dist-smoke` CI jobs.
  - `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped `rytm-v79`→`rytm-v80` (source/GitHub-Pages variant — new `js/vendor/preact/preact.module.js` `STATIC_ASSETS` entry, a real always-loaded file there since Pages doesn't bundle).
  - **Bundle size measured directly**: `dist/js/app-*.js` grew 204.5KB→215.5KB raw, ~55.3KB→~60.0KB gzip (+~4.8KB gzip) — in line with Preact core's known footprint, not just assumed small.
  - **Verified against both deploy targets**: new test + `tests/debt-swipe-delete.mjs` + `tests/smoke.mjs` + `tests/e2e-crud.mjs` all green against source; `npm run build` then the same 4 tests staged into a temporary `dist/tests/` and re-run against the real bundled output — all green, confirming Preact actually executes correctly both unbundled and bundled. `npm run typecheck` unaffected (js/debt.js isn't opted into `// @ts-check`).
  - **Deliberately narrow, per the account owner's own framing**: no other widget touched, no JSX/build transform, no state management layer (signals/hooks/context) — the target widget is stateless and doesn't need one. Whether/how to expand Preact further is an explicit follow-up conversation, not decided here.
  - **Deployed**: `firebase deploy --only hosting --project maxtr-c238f` from a fresh `git worktree add ... origin/main --detach`. `predeploy` ran automatically (`npm install` → 19 packages now, `npm run build`), 36 files uploaded (one more than the prior deploy — the vendored Preact file itself is excluded from `dist/` per `ALWAYS_BUNDLED_VENDOR_DIRS`, confirmed unrelated to this count), release complete. Live bundle: `app-B_TXj4Va.js`, `sw.js` `CACHE_NAME`: `rytm-dist-12eedfc3c3b7`. This is a real rendering-behavior change (not inert like the TypeScript Phase 1 comments), so redeployed on principle without checking whether the diff was "big enough" to bother.
- **TypeScript adoption — Phase 2 (second file opted in, `functions/lib/pure.js`)**, continuing the gradual per-file rollout ("продовжуй"). `functions/lib/pure.js` was already flagged in `CLAUDE.md` as a good next candidate (zero imports, already split out for framework-independence, same reasoning as `js/tx-validation.js`).
  - **Needed a genuinely separate `functions/tsconfig.json`**, not just adding `functions/**` to the root config's `include` — `functions/` is a real, separate CommonJS npm project (no `"type":"module"` in its `package.json`), while the root `tsconfig.json` assumes ESM (`module:"ESNext"`) to match `js/*.js`. Scoped to `include:["lib/**/*.js"]` only, deliberately excluding `functions/index.js` (real firebase-admin top-level side effects, not a good first candidate). `npm run typecheck` now runs both configs sequentially; a `tsc -p <path>` invocation works fine using the one root-installed `typescript` regardless of which directory the target config lives in.
  - **Hit a real TypeScript 7 breaking change while wiring this up**: `moduleResolution:"Node10"`, the classic pairing for `module:"CommonJS"`, was removed entirely in TS 7 (`error TS5108: Option 'moduleResolution=node10' has been removed`). Fixed by omitting `moduleResolution` and letting it default from `module` — works cleanly.
  - Gained a `RatesMap` typedef and full `@param`/`@returns` JSDoc on all 5 exported functions (`convertCurrency`, `toBase`, `zonedDateParts`, `todayStr`, `monthPrefix`, `mapWithConcurrency` — the last one using a generic `@template T, R` JSDoc annotation). Typechecks clean.
  - Zero behavior change, confirmed: `node --check` syntax pass, `tests/unit.mjs` (13/13, exercises `pure.js` directly) and `tests/functions-sweep.mjs` (30/30, exercises it transitively via `sweep.js`) both still green, `npm run build` unaffected (bundle hash unchanged — `functions/` was never part of the Vite-bundled `js/` graph).
  - No CI workflow change needed — `smoke-test.yml` already runs `npm run typecheck`, which now covers both configs automatically.
  - Next candidates per `CLAUDE.md`: `functions/lib/sweep.js` (imports `pure.js`, now itself checked) and `functions/lib/monobank.js`.
- **TypeScript adoption — Phase 3 (third file opted in, `functions/lib/monobank.js`)**, continuing the gradual rollout ("продовжуй"). Picked `monobank.js` over the other documented candidate, `functions/lib/sweep.js`, specifically because it's still zero-import pure logic (`buildMonobankUrl()`, URL string-building) — `sweep.js` is a meaningfully bigger step (real firebase-admin Firestore snapshot/doc typing, a genuine design decision, now explicitly flagged as such in `CLAUDE.md` rather than attempted casually).
  - New `MonobankQuery`/`MonobankUrlResult` typedefs + `@param`/`@returns` JSDoc on `buildMonobankUrl()`. No new tsconfig needed — already covered by `functions/tsconfig.json`'s existing `include:["lib/**/*.js"]`.
